The Imamate of the Inferior: Three Views
Three positions on imamate of the inferior.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three major positions on whether an inferior person can be imam when a superior exists, and the rational and practical arguments behind each view.

Core Idea
The imamate of the inferior is not always forbidden; context and suitability matter.

This passage from Sharh al-Mawaqif presents a classic debate in Islamic political theology: can a less qualified person lead the community when a more qualified person is available? The author outlines three positions: the Imamiyya's absolute prohibition based on rational ugliness, the majority's pragmatic allowance, and a nuanced distinction that considers potential discord. As you read, notice how each view appeals to reason, analogy, and social stability.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before interpreting.
Note the structure: three positions are presented sequentially.
2
Identify the Imamiyya argument
Find why the Imamiyya forbid it. Notice their analogy with al-Shafi'i and the claim that it is 'rationally ugly' (qabih aqlan).
This is a rationalist argument based on the concept of ugliness in kalam.
3
Understand the majority view
The majority (aktharun) permit it. They distinguish between roles: placing an inferior in a task where he is inferior is ugly, but imamate is different. The inferior may be more suitable for leadership.
Focus on the phrase 'perhaps he is more suitable for imamate than the superior'.
4
Examine the third view
A group differentiates based on fitna (discord). If appointing the superior causes discord, it is not obligatory; otherwise, it is obligatory.
This view introduces a practical condition: social stability.
5
Reflect on the common misunderstanding
The source mentions a common misunderstanding that the imamate of the inferior is always impermissible. See how the passage corrects this by showing majority permission.
The passage thus provides a nuanced picture.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقصد السادس : في إمامة المفضول ] ( في إمامة المفضول مع وجود الفاضل منعه (قوم كالإمامية ( لأنه قبيح عقلاً فإن ) من ألزم الشافعي حضور درس بعض آحاد الفقهاء والعمل بفتواه عد سفيها قاضياً بغير قضية العقل وجوزه الأكثرون وقالوا : جعل المفضول رئيساً ومقتدى فيما هو مفضول فيه كما في المثال المذكور مستقبح، وأما في غيره كما فيما نحن بصدده فلا. إذ لعله أصلح للإمامة من الفاضل إذ المعتبر في ولاية كل أمر والقيام به معرفة مصالحه ومفاسده وقوة القيام بلوازمه ورب مفضول في علمه وعمله هو بالزعامة ) والرياسة ( أعرف وبشرائطها أقوم ) وعلى تحمل أعبائها أقدر ) وفصل قوم ) في هذه المسألة فقالوا : نصب الأفضل إن أثار فتنة لم يجب) كما إذا فرض أن العسكر والرعايا لا ينقادون للفاضل بل للمفضول ) وإلا وجب).
The Sixth Objective: On the Imamate of the Inferior. (On the imamate of the inferior when a superior exists. Some people, like the Imamiyya, forbid it because it is rationally ugly. For making al-Shafi'i attend the lesson of some of the jurists and act according to his fatwa would be considered foolish... judging without the judgment of reason. And the majority permitted it and said: Making the inferior a leader and an example in that in which he is inferior, as in the mentioned example, is deemed ugly, but in other than that, as in what we are discussing, it is not. For perhaps he is more suitable for imamate than the superior, since what is considered in every authority and undertaking is knowledge of its benefits and harms and strength in fulfilling its requirements. Perhaps an inferior in his knowledge and actions is more knowledgeable about leadership and its conditions, more capable of bearing its burdens.) And some people made a distinction in this issue and said: Appointing the superior, if it causes discord, is not obligatory, as when one assumes that the army and subjects do not obey the superior but rather the inferior; otherwise, it is obligatory.
Source pages p. 405

Commentary
This passage is a classification of the different positions on the permissibility of the imamate of an inferior person (mafdul) when a superior (fadil) is present. The author presents three views. First, the Imamiyya (Shia) forbid it absolutely, arguing it is rationally ugly (qabih aqlan). They analogize that if one obliged al-Shafi'i to attend the lesson of a minor jurist and follow his opinion, that would be deemed foolish. Second, the majority (aktharun) permit it, distinguishing between cases where the inferior is placed in a role where he is inferior (e.g., a less knowledgeable jurist giving a fatwa) which is indeed ugly, but in the case of political imamate, the inferior may be more suitable for leadership due to political acumen or acceptance by the people. Third, a group differentiates: if appointing the superior would cause discord (fitna), then it is not obligatory; otherwise, it is obligatory to appoint the superior. This reflects a pragmatic approach that considers the greater good and social stability.

Key Terms
إمامة المفضول
الفاضل
قبيح عقلاً
فتنة
الأكثرون

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The imamate of the inferior is always impermissible.
Correction: The majority allow it, especially when the inferior is more suitable for leadership or when the superior would cause discord.

Checkpoint
According to the majority view presented in the passage, why can an inferior (mafdul) be imam even when a superior (fadil) exists?
A) Because the inferior is always more knowledgeable in religious matters.
B) Because the inferior may be more suitable for leadership in terms of political acumen and acceptance by the people.
C) Because the superior is not obligated to lead.
D) Because the Imamiyya forbid it, so the majority oppose them.

Key Takeaway
The imamate of the inferior is permitted by the majority when the inferior is more suitable for leadership or when appointing the superior would cause discord.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When choosing a leader in your community, do you prioritize their knowledge and piety (the 'superior' in religious terms) or their ability to practically lead and maintain unity? How does this lesson challenge your default preference?
?
The third position says that appointing the superior is not obligatory if it causes discord. Recall a situation where insisting on the most qualified person created conflict. Were you willing to compromise for harmony? What does this teach you about the relationship between truth and unity?
?
The majority argue that an 'inferior' may be more knowledgeable about leadership conditions. Have you ever dismissed someone because they lacked knowledge in one area but were skilled in another? How can you apply this lesson to evaluate people more fairly today?

Veneration of All Companions
States the obligation to venerate all Companions and cites Quranic evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that veneration of all Companions is a religious obligation based on explicit Quranic praise.

Core Idea
All Companions are divinely praised; to honor them is to honor God's word.

This lesson introduces a key tenet of Sunni orthodoxy: the obligatory veneration of all the Prophet's Companions. The author grounds this duty not in mere tradition but in direct Quranic commendation. As you read the passage, observe how the single ruling is supported by multiple verses, each highlighting different aspects of the Companions' virtue.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central ruling
Find the sentence that states what is obligatory regarding the Companions. Notice the verb 'يجب' (it is obligatory).
2
Locate the Quranic evidence
The author cites four Quranic verses as proof. Read each verse translation and see how each verse praises the Companions or the believers among them.
The verses are from Surah al-Tawbah (9:100), al-Tahrim (66:8), al-Fath (48:29), and al-Fath (48:18).
3
Understand the reasoning
Why does the author say it is obligatory to venerate them? Because God Himself has magnified and praised them in the Quran. Reflect on the logical link: divine praise implies honor is due.
4
Consider the scope
The phrase 'all of them' is explicit. Note that the obligation includes all Companions, not just a subset. The verses cited refer to groups like Muhajirun, Ansar, and those under the tree, but the author's conclusion is comprehensive.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقصد السابع : تعظيم الصحابة كلهم ] ( أنه يجب تعظيم الصحابة كلهم والكف عن القدح فيهم لأن الله سبحانه وتعالى عظمهم وأثنى عليهم في غير موضع من كتابه كقوله : والسابقون الأولون من المهاجرين والأنصار ﴾ [التوبة : ١٠٠ ] ، وقوله : يوم لا يخزي الله النبي والذين آمنو معه نورهم يسعى بنى أيديهم ﴾ [التحريم: ۸] وقوله : والذين أشداء على الكفار رحماء بينهم تراهم ركعاً سجداً يبتغون فضلاً من الله ورضواناً ) [الفتح: ۲۹]، وقوله : لقد رضي الله عن المؤمنين إذ يبايعونك تحت الشجرة )
The Seventh Objective: Veneration of All Companions. (It is obligatory to venerate all the Companions and to refrain from disparaging them, because God, glorified and exalted, has magnified them and praised them in several places in His Book, such as His statement: 'And the foremost, the first of the Muhajirun and the Ansar' [Quran 9:100], and His statement: 'On the Day when God will not disgrace the Prophet and those who believe with him, their light will run before them' [Quran 66:8], and His statement: 'Those who are severe against the disbelievers, merciful among themselves, you see them bowing and prostrating, seeking bounty from God and pleasure' [Quran 48:29], and His statement: 'God was well pleased with the believers when they gave you the pledge under the tree' [Quran 48:18].)
Source pages p. 405

Commentary
This passage is a normative statement establishing the obligation to venerate all the Companions (sahaba) and to refrain from disparaging them (al-qadih fihim). The author grounds this duty in divine commendation: God has magnified and praised them in multiple Quranic verses. Four verses are cited: (1) 'And the foremost, the first of the Muhajirun and the Ansar' (9:100) which praises the early emigrants and helpers. (2) 'On the Day when God will not disgrace the Prophet and those who believe with him, their light will run before them' (66:8) indicating God's honor to the believers. (3) 'Those who are severe against the disbelievers, merciful among themselves...' (48:29) describing the Companions' attributes. (4) 'God was well pleased with the believers when they gave you the pledge under the tree' (48:18) referring to the pledge of Ridwan. The passage thus provides a clear doctrinal directive based on scripture.

Key Terms
تعظيم الصحابة
القدح
المهاجرين
الأنصار
بيعة الرضوان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Only some Companions are to be venerated while others may be criticized.
Correction: The author asserts that all Companions must be venerated, based on Quranic praise that applies broadly to the early Muhajirun, Ansar, and those under the tree, implying all are included.

Checkpoint
On what basis does the author assert that it is obligatory to venerate all the Companions?
A) Consensus of the scholars.
B) Quranic verses in which God magnifies and praises the Companions.
C) Hadiths from the Prophet.
D) Rational proofs.

Key Takeaway
All Companions must be venerated because God Himself has praised them in the Quran.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear someone disparage a Companion, do you feel a personal obligation to correct them based on God's explicit praise in the Quran? What will you do the next time you encounter such a situation?
?
Are there any Companions you feel less inclined to venerate due to stories you've heard? How can you align your heart with the Quranic verses that praise them all, even if your intellect struggles?
?
If you truly believe that God has praised all the Companions, how does that affect your attitude towards sectarian divisions that vilify some of them? What concrete step will you take this week to honor the Companions collectively?

Imamate of the Inferior and the Salaf's Consensus
The author states the Salaf's consensus on the order of caliphs and the obligation to follow it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the position of the Salaf regarding the order of the first four caliphs and the doctrinal stance on the imamate of the inferior.

Core Idea
The Salaf's consensus on the order of caliphs obliges us to follow it, even if reasoning is uncertain.

This lesson introduces the sixth and seventh topics of the fourth observatory. The author begins by acknowledging that the rationality of the imamate of the inferior is not definitively proven, but the Salaf agreed upon a specific order. This agreement, due to their righteousness, implies knowledge, so we must follow them in that and entrust the true reality to God.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the imamate of the inferior
Read the Arabic text and its translation. Notice the initial statement about conjecture and the parenthesis from the Salaf.
2
Identify the Salaf's claim
The Salaf said the best are Abu Bakr, then Umar, then Uthman, then Ali. Understand that this order is a point of consensus.
This order is accepted by Ahl al-Sunna.
3
Understand the implication
The author argues that their consensus implies they knew it, so we must follow them and leave the true reality to God.
This reflects a Sunni approach to tafdil.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المرصد الرابع - المقصدين السادس والسابع : في إمامة المفضول
ظننا
غايته الظن كيف ولا قطع بأن إمامة المفضول لا تصح مع وجود الفاضل، (لكنا وجدنا السلف قالوا بأن الأفضل أبو بكر ثم عمر ثم عثمان ثم علي، وحسن بهم يقضي بأنهم لو لم يعرفوا ذلك لما أطبقوا عليه فوجب علينا اتباعهم في ذلك ) القول ( وتفويض ما هو الحق فيه إلى الله. قال الآمدي : وقد يراد بالتفضيل اختصاص أحد الشخصين عن الآخر إما بأصل فضيلة لا وجود لها في الآخر كالعالم والجاهل، وإما بزيادة فيها ككونه أعلم .مثلا وذلك أيضا غير مقطوع به فيما بين الصحابة إذ ما من فضيلة تبين اختصاصها بواحد منهم إلا ويمكن بيان مشاركة غيره له فيها وبتقدير عدم المشاركة فقد يمكن بيان اختصاص الآخر بفضيلة أخرى، ولا سبيل إلى الترجيح بكثرة الفضائل لاحتماله أن تكون الفضيلة الواحد أرجح من فضائل كثيرة إما لزيادة شرفها في نفسها أو لزيادة كميتها فلا جزم بالأفضلية بهذا المعنى أيضاً.
The Fourth Observatory - The Sixth and Seventh Topics: On the Imamate of the Inferior. Our assumption [؟] its end is conjecture, how? And there is no certainty that the imamate of the inferior is not valid in the presence of the superior, (but we found that the Salaf said that the best is Abu Bakr, then Umar, then Uthman, then Ali, and it is well with them that they would not have agreed upon that if they had not known it, so we must follow them in that) the statement (and entrust what is true therein to God. Al-Amidi said: And by preference (tafdil) may be meant the specialization of one of the two persons over the other either by a fundamental virtue not present in the other, like the scholar and the ignorant, or by an excess in it, like being more knowledgeable for example. And that also is not certain among the Companions, for there is no virtue specified for one of them except that it is possible to show the participation of another in it, and assuming no participation, it is possible to show the other's specialization in another virtue. And there is no way to preponderance by multiplicity of virtues because it is possible that one virtue is more preponderant than many virtues, either due to greater honor in itself or greater quantity. So there is no certainty of superiority in this sense either.
Source pages p. 405

Commentary
This passage introduces the sixth and seventh topics of the fourth observatory: the Imamate of the inferior and the veneration of the Companions. The author begins by stating that the aim of this discussion is conjecture because there is no definitive proof that the imamate of the inferior is invalid when a superior exists. However, he notes that the Salaf agreed that the best of the Companions are Abu Bakr, then Umar, then Uthman, then Ali, and that such agreement from them indicates they knew this truth, so we must follow them in that and entrust the true reality to God. Then he quotes al-Amidi's explanation of the concept of preference (tafdil): it can mean either a fundamental virtue completely absent in the other, like knowledge versus ignorance, or a greater degree of the same virtue, like being more knowledgeable. But even this kind of preference is not certain among the Companions, because any virtue claimed for one can potentially be shown to be shared by another, and even if not shared, the other may have another virtue. Moreover, weighing by number of virtues is inconclusive because a single virtue could outweigh many due to its nobility or magnitude. Therefore, certainty of superiority in this sense is also unattainable.

Key Terms
إمامة المفضول
السلف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why must we follow the Salaf's order of the caliphs?
A) Because it is proven by rational arguments.
B) Because the Salaf agreed upon it and their agreement indicates knowledge.
C) Because Allah commanded it directly.
D) Because the imamate of the inferior is invalid.

Key Takeaway
The Salaf's consensus on the order of the caliphs obliges us to follow, even without rational certainty.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think about the order of the caliphs, do you accept it merely because it is a fact of history, or because you trust the Salaf's judgment? Examine your heart: is there any part of you that resents this order because your own reasoning would place someone else first? Will you entrust that feeling to God and submit to the consensus, even if your intellect is not fully satisfied?
?
The passage says we must follow the Salaf's consensus 'and entrust what is true therein to God.' Is there a point in your life where you have clung to your own reasoning over a clear consensus of the righteous predecessors? Are you willing today to surrender that area to God, even if you never receive a logical explanation?

The Meaning of Tafdil and Its Uncertainty Among Companions
Al-Amidi defines tafdil and explains why it is not certain among the Companions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Amidi's definition of tafdil and the reasons why certainty about superiority among the Companions is unattainable.

Core Idea
Tafdil can mean a unique virtue or greater degree, but among Companions, such preference cannot be certain.

This lesson continues from the previous by examining the concept of tafdil (preference) as defined by al-Amidi. It explains two types of preference and then argues that even this kind of preference cannot be definitively established among the Companions due to possible shared virtues and the difficulty of weighing virtues.

Guided Path
1
Read al-Amidi's definition of tafdil
Read the Arabic from 'قال الآمدي' to the end. Note the two types of preference: by a fundamental virtue absent in the other, or by an excess in a virtue.
2
Understand the uncertainty
The passage argues that no virtue can be exclusively assigned to one Companion; others may share it. Even if exclusive, another may have a different virtue. Counting virtues is inconclusive.
This shows the difficulty of claiming absolute superiority.
3
Reflect on the conclusion
Thus, certainty about superiority in this sense is impossible among the Companions.
This aligns with Sunni caution on tafdil.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Checkpoint
According to al-Amidi, what are the two meanings of tafdil?
A) Having more money and more children.
B) Having a fundamental virtue absent in the other, or having an excess in a virtue.

D) Being chosen by the community and having leadership.

?
When you think about the people you admire for their faith or character, do you catch yourself ranking them like the Companions? How does al-Amidi's argument challenge that habit and push you to see each person's unique virtue without comparison?
?
You may have friends you consider 'better Muslims'—but based on this lesson, can you truly be certain of that ranking? What would it mean for your relationships if you stopped assuming you know who is closer to Allah?
?
Al-Amidi notes that a single virtue may outweigh many others. In your own life, are you scattered across many small good deeds while neglecting one great, sincere virtue—like ihsan or deep tawakkul? Which one virtue could you focus on today to tip the scale?

The Obligation to Venerate the Companions
The author enumerates scriptural and rational proofs for the obligatory veneration of all Companions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scriptural and rational basis for the obligation to venerate all the Companions and refrain from disparaging them.

Core Idea
The Quran and Sunnah command love and respect for all Companions.

The author begins by establishing that veneration of the Companions is obligatory. He cites multiple Quranic verses and hadiths that praise them, and then appeals to their evident sacrifice and piety. This lesson examines those proofs.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic source passage and its literal translation. Notice how the author piles up evidence from Quran and hadith.
2
Identify the Quranic verses
Identify the four Quranic verses cited by the author. What do they say about the Companions?
The verses are from Surah al-Tawba, al-Tahrim, al-Fath, and al-Fath.
3
Identify the hadiths
Find the three hadiths quoted. What do they teach about the Companions' status?
They include 'Khayr al-qurun', 'La tasubbu ashabi', and 'Allah Allah fi ashabi'.
4
Understand the rational argument
The author adds a rational argument from their observable deeds. How does this reinforce the obligation?

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقصد السابع : تعظيم الصحابة كلهم
( أنه يجب تعظيم الصحابة كلهم والكف عن القدح فيهم لأن الله سبحانه وتعالى عظمهم وأثنى عليهم في غير موضع من كتابه كقوله : والسابقون الأولون من المهاجرين والأنصار ﴾ [التوبة : ١٠٠ ] ، وقوله : يوم لا يخزي الله النبي
والذين آمنو معه نورهم يسعى بنى أيديهم ﴾ [التحريم: ۸] وقوله : والذين أشداء على الكفار رحماء بينهم تراهم ركعاً سجداً يبتغون فضلاً من الله ورضواناً ) [الفتح: ۲۹]، وقوله : لقد رضي الله عن المؤمنين إذ يبايعونك تحت الشجرة ) [الفتح : ۱۸] ، إلى غير ذلك من الآيات الدالة على عظم قدرهم وكرامتهم عند الله ) والرسول قد أحبهم وأثنى عليهم في أحاديث كثيرة ( منها قوله عليه السلام: «خير القرون قرني ثم الذين يلونهم ثم الذين يلونهم ، ومنها قوله : « لا تسبوا أصحابي فلو أن أحد أنفق مثل أحد ذهبا ما بلغ مد أحدهم ولا نصيفه» ومنها قوله : «الله الله في أصحابي لا تتخذوهم غرضاً بعدي فمن أحبهم فيحبي أحبهم، ومن أبغضهم فببغضي أبغضهم ومن آذاهم فقد آذاني ومن آذاني فقد آذى الله آذى الله فيوشك أن ومن يأخذه إلى غير ذلك من الأحاديث المشهورة في الكتب الصحاح ( ثم إن من تأمل سيرتهم ووقف على مآثرهم وجدهم في الدين وبذلهم أموالهم وأنفسهم في نصرة الله ورسوله لم يتخالجه شك في عظم شأنهم وبراءتهم عما ينسب إليهم المبطلون من المطاعن ومنعه ذلك أي تيقنه بحالهم ( عن الطعن فيهم فرأى ذلك مجانباً للإيمان، ونحن لا نلوث كتابنا بأمثال ذلك وهي مذكورة في المطولات مع التقصي عنها فارجع إليها إن أردت الوقوف عليها ( وأما الفتن والحروب الواقعة بين الصحابة، فالهشامية ) من المعتزلة ( أنكروا ،وقوعها، ولا شك أنه مكابرة للتواتر في قتل عثمان ووقعة الجمل ،وصفين والمعترفون بوقوعها منهم من سکت عن الكلام) فيها بتخطئة أو تصويب وهم طائفة من أهل السنة ) فإن أرادوا أنه اشتغال بما لا فلا يعني بأس به. إذ قال الشافعي ) وغيره من السلف : ( تلك دماء طهر الله عنها أيدينا فلنطهر عنها ألسنتنا، وإن أرادوا أنا لا نعلم أوقعت أم لا، فباطل لوقوعها قطعاً) وأنت خبير بأن الشق الثاني من الترديد ينافي الاعتراف بوقوعها ( واتفق العمرية أصحاب عمرو بن ،عبيد والواصلية أصحاب واصل بن عطاء، على رد شهادة الفريقين قالوا : لو شهد الجميع بباقة بقلة لم نقبلها، أما العمرية : فلأنهم يرون فسق الجميع من الفريقين ( وأما الواصلية : فلانهم يفسقون أحد الفريقين لا بعينه فلا يعلم عدالة شيء منهما . والذي عليه الجمهور من الأمة هو ( أن المخطئ قتلة عثمان ومحاربو علي لأنهما إما
قوله : (مد أحدهم ولا نصيفه المد ربع الصاع والنصيف مكيل دون المد ويجيء بمعنى النصف كالعشير بمعنى العشر أي لا ينال أحدكم بإنفاق مثل جبل أحد ذهباً من الفضيلة، والأجر ما ينال أحدهم بإنفاق مد طعام أو نصف منه لما يقارن من مزيد الإخلاص وصدق النية وكمال النفس مع ما بهم من البؤس والضر.
قوله : ( لا تتخذوهم (عرضاً أي هدفاً يرمونهم بالمنكرات والفواحش . قوله: (ينافي الاعتراف بوقوعها فلا يصح جعل هذا الشق من شقي الترديد في
المعترفين.
The Seventh Topic: Veneration of All the Companions (It is obligatory to venerate all the Companions and refrain from disparaging them, because Allah the Exalted has magnified them and praised them in many places of His Book, such as His saying: 'And the foremost, the first of the Muhajirun and the Ansar' [9:100], and His saying: 'On the Day when Allah will not disgrace the Prophet and those who believed with him, their light proceeding before them' [66:8], and His saying: 'Those who are severe against the disbelievers, merciful among themselves; you see them bowing and prostrating, seeking bounty from Allah and [His] pleasure' [48:29], and His saying: 'Certainly Allah was pleased with the believers when they pledged allegiance to you under the tree' [48:18], and other verses indicating the greatness of their status and their honor with Allah. And the Messenger loved them and praised them in many hadiths, including his saying, peace be upon him: 'The best of generations is my generation, then those who follow them, then those who follow them,' and his saying: 'Do not insult my Companions, for if anyone were to spend the equivalent of Mount Uhud in gold, he would not reach the measure of a mudd of one of them, nor half of it,' and his saying: 'Allah, Allah regarding my Companions! Do not take them as targets after me. Whoever loves them loves me, and whoever hates them hates me, and whoever harms them harms me, and whoever harms me harms Allah, and whoever harms Allah, Allah will soon seize him.' And other famous hadiths in the authentic books. Then whoever contemplates their conduct and comes to know their exploits finds them in religion, their spending of their wealth and themselves in support of Allah and His Messenger, such that no doubt enters him about the greatness of their status and their innocence from the accusations that the false ones attribute to them. And that—i.e., his certainty of their state—prevents him from disparaging them, and he sees that as contrary to faith. And we do not sully our book with things like that; they are mentioned in the lengthy works with investigation, so refer to them if you want to know them. As for the seditions and wars that occurred among the Companions, the Hishamiyya among the Mu'tazila denied their occurrence. There is no doubt that is an obstinate denial of the widespread transmission of the killing of Uthman, the Battle of the Camel, and Siffin. And those who acknowledge their occurrence, among them are those who remain silent about them without declaring error or correctness, and they are a group from the Ahl al-Sunna. If they mean that it is an occupation with what does not concern them, then there is no harm. For al-Shafi'i and others of the Salaf said: 'Those are bloodstains from which Allah has purified our hands, so let us purify our tongues from them.' And if they mean that we do not know whether they occurred or not, then it is false because their occurrence is certain. And you are aware that the second part of the disjunction contradicts the acknowledgment of their occurrence. And the Umariyya, the followers of Amr ibn Ubayd, and the Wasiliyya, the followers of Wasil ibn Ata, agreed to reject the testimony of either party. They said: If all of them testified on a bunch of herbs [؟], we would not accept it. As for the Umariyya, it is because they consider all of both parties to be corrupt. As for the Wasiliyya, it is because they consider one of the parties to be corrupt, not specifically, so the integrity of either is not known. And the view held by the majority of the community is that the wrongdoers are the killers of Uthman and the fighters against Ali, because they are either... (then footnotes: His saying: (A mudd of one of them nor half of it): the mudd is a quarter of a sa', and the naseef is a measure less than a mudd, and it comes in the meaning of half, like 'asheer' meaning a tenth. That is, none of you will attain, by spending the equivalent of Mount Uhud in gold, the virtue and reward that one of them attains by spending a mudd of food or half of it, due to the greater sincerity, truthful intention, perfection of soul, and the hardship and poverty they experienced. His saying: (Do not take them as targets): i.e., a target at which they shoot with objectionable things and obscenities. His saying: (contradicts the acknowledgment of their occurrence): so it is not correct to make this part of the two parts of the disjunction among those who acknowledge.)
Source pages p. 405

Commentary
This passage covers the seventh topic on the obligatory veneration of all the Companions and addresses the issue of the conflicts among them. The author provides several proofs: Quranic verses praising the Companions, hadiths of the Prophet commanding love and respect for them, and the argument from their observable deeds and sacrifices. He urges restraint from speaking about the accusations against them, directing the reader to longer works. Then he discusses the fitan (seditions) among the Companions. He mentions the Hishamiyyah branch of the Mu'tazila who deny the occurrence of those wars, which he calls stubbornness against mutawatir reports. Among those who acknowledge the wars, some (a group of Ahl al-Sunnah) remain silent, not declaring any party wrong. He explains that if they mean not to engage in a useless matter, that is acceptable quoting al-Shafi'i; but if they claim ignorance of the occurrence, that is false because the events are certain. He then notes that the second part contradicts the acknowledgment. He also mentions the Umariyyah and Wasiliyyah who reject the testimony of both parties, explaining their reasons. Finally, he states the majority position: the wrongdoers are the killers of Uthman and those who fought Ali. The footnotes clarify the linguistic meaning of 'mudd' and 'naseef' in the hadith about spending gold, explain 'la tattakhidhuhum gharadan', and explain that the second part of the disjunction contradicts the acknowledgment.

Key Terms
تعظيم الصحابة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following Quranic verses is NOT cited by the author to support veneration of the Companions?
A) [9:100]
B) [66:8]
C) [48:29]
D) [2:255]

Key Takeaway
The Quran and Sunnah provide overwhelming evidence for the obligation to venerate all Companions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you find in your heart any trace of disdain or disrespect for any Companion, even a tiny one? If so, what does that reveal about your love for the Prophet, who said 'Whoever loves them loves me'? Will you today make a firm resolve to purge that feeling?
?
The Prophet warned that even spending the equivalent of Mount Uhud in gold could not match the status of a Companion. Is there any 'mountain of gold' in your mind—like a particular act or mistake—that you use to justify criticizing a Companion? How can you submit your reasoning to the Prophet's explicit command?
?
Have you ever sincerely reflected on the sacrifices of the Companions—leaving homes, enduring persecution, spending their wealth—until your heart is filled with love for them? If not, what concrete step will you take this week to learn about the life of one Companion to develop that love?

The Fitnah Among the Companions: Denial and Silence
The author discusses the denial of fitnah by Hishamiyya and the silent position of some Ahl al-Sunna.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Hishamiyya's denial of the fitnah and the position of some Ahl al-Sunna who remain silent, along with the author's critique.

Core Idea
Denying the fitnah is obstinate, but silence is acceptable if not implying ignorance.

After establishing the virtue of the Companions, the author tackles the contentious issue of the wars among them. He first addresses the Hishamiyya, a Mu'tazili sect that denied the occurrence of these conflicts, which he considers stubbornness against mutawatir reports. Then he discusses those who acknowledge but choose silence, a stance he examines critically.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the fitnah
Read the Arabic and translation focusing on the Hishamiyya and the silent group.
2
Understand the Hishamiyya position
What did the Hishamiyya claim about the wars? Why does the author reject their view?
They denied the occurrence, contradicting tawatur.
3
Analyze the silent stance
Some Ahl al-Sunna remained silent. What are the two possible interpretations the author gives?
One is acceptable (avoiding useless talk), the other is false (ignorance of occurrence).
4
Grasp the author's critique
Why does the author say the second part of the disjunction contradicts acknowledgment?

The Seventh Topic: Veneration of All the Companions (It is obligatory to venerate all the Companions and refrain from disparaging them, because Allah the Exalted has magnified them and praised them in many places of His Book, such as His saying: 'And the foremost, the first of the Muhajirun and the Ansar' [9:100], and His saying: 'On the Day when Allah will not disgrace the Prophet and those who believed with him, their light proceeding before them' [66:8], and His saying: 'Those who are severe against the disbelievers, merciful among themselves; you see them bowing and prostrating, seeking bounty from Allah and [His] pleasure' [48:29], and His saying: 'Certainly Allah was pleased with the believers when they pledged allegiance to you under the tree' [48:18], and other verses indicating the greatness of their status and their honor with Allah. And the Messenger loved them and praised them in many hadiths, including his saying, peace be upon him: 'The best of generations is my generation, then those who follow them, then those who follow them,' and his saying: 'Do not insult my Companions, for if anyone were to spend the equivalent of Mount Uhud in gold, he would not reach the measure of a mudd of one of them, nor half of it,' and his saying: 'Allah, Allah regarding my Companions! Do not take them as targets after me. Whoever loves them loves me, and whoever hates them hates me, and whoever harms them harms me, and whoever harms me harms Allah, and whoever harms Allah, Allah will soon seize him.' And other famous hadiths in the authentic books. Then whoever contemplates their conduct and comes to know their exploits finds them in religion, their spending of their wealth and themselves in support of Allah and His Messenger, such that no doubt enters him about the greatness of their status and their innocence from the accusations that the false ones attribute to them. And that—i.e., his certainty of their state—prevents him from disparaging them, and he sees that as contrary to faith. And we do not sully our book with things like that; they are mentioned in the lengthy works with investigation, so refer to them if you want to know them. As for the seditions and wars that occurred among the Companions, the Hishamiyya among the Mu'tazila denied their occurrence. There is no doubt that is an obstinate denial of the widespread transmission of the killing of Uthman, the Battle of the Camel, and Siffin. And those who acknowledge their occurrence, among them are those who remain silent about them without declaring error or correctness, and they are a group from the Ahl al-Sunna. If they mean that it is an occupation with what does not concern them, then there is no harm. For al-Shafi'i and others of the Salaf said: 'Those are bloodstains from which Allah has purified our hands, so let us purify our tongues from them.' And if they mean that we do not know whether they occurred or not, then it is false because their occurrence is certain. And you are aware that the second part of the disjunction contradicts the acknowledgment of their occurrence. And the Umariyya, the followers of Amr ibn Ubayd, and the Wasiliyya, the followers of Wasil ibn Ata, agreed to reject the testimony of either party. They said: If all of them testified on a bunch of herbs [؟], we would not accept it. As for the Umariyya, it is because they consider all of both parties to be corrupt. As for the Wasiliyya, it is because they consider one of the parties to be corrupt, not specifically, so the integrity of either is not known. And the view held by the majority of the community is that the wrongdoers are the killers of Uthman and the fighters against Ali, because they are either... (then footnotes: His saying: (A mudd of one of them nor half of it): the mudd is a quarter of a sa', and the naseef is a measure less than a mudd, and it comes in the meaning of half, like 'asheer' meaning a tenth. That is, none of you will attain, by spending the equivalent of Mount Uhud in gold, the virtue and reward that one of them attains by spending a mudd of food or half of it, due to the greater sincerity, truthful intention, perfection of soul, and the hardship and poverty they experienced. His saying: (Do not take them as targets): i.e., a target at which they shoot with objectionable things and obscenities. His saying: (contradicts the acknowledgment of their occurrence): so it is not correct to make this part of the two parts of the disjunction among those who acknowledge.)

Commentary
This passage covers the seventh topic on the obligatory veneration of all the Companions and addresses the issue of the conflicts among them. The author provides several proofs: Quranic verses praising the Companions, hadiths of the Prophet commanding love and respect for them, and the argument from their observable deeds and sacrifices. He urges restraint from speaking about the accusations against them, directing the reader to longer works. Then he discusses the fitan (seditions) among the Companions. He mentions the Hishamiyyah branch of the Mu'tazila who deny the occurrence of those wars, which he calls stubbornness against mutawatir reports. Among those who acknowledge the wars, some (a group of Ahl al-Sunnah) remain silent, not declaring any party wrong. He explains that if they mean not to engage in a useless matter, that is acceptable quoting al-Shafi'i; but if they claim ignorance of the occurrence, that is false because the events are certain. He then notes that the second part contradicts the acknowledgment. He also mentions the Umariyyah and Wasiliyyah who reject the testimony of both parties, explaining their reasons. Finally, he states the majority position: the wrongdoers are the killers of Uthman and those who fought Ali. The footnotes clarify the linguistic meaning of 'mudd' and 'naseef' in the hadith about spending gold, explain 'la tattakhidhuhum gharadan', and explain that the second part of the disjunction contradicts the acknowledgment.

Checkpoint
What is the author's main criticism of the Hishamiyya position?
A) They are too lenient.
B) They deny events that are mutawatir.
C) They side with Ali.
D) They accept testimony from both sides.

Key Takeaway
Denying the fitnah is wrong, but remaining silent is acceptable if it aims to avoid harmful discourse.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear about conflicts among Muslims, past or present, do you find it easier to deny the problem, take a side, or remain silent? Which intention drives your response—fear of involvement or desire for truth? Commit to one concrete change in how you engage with such fitnah.
?
The Hishamiyya denied clear historical evidence to protect their own view. Is there a belief or assumption you hold that you have never questioned because accepting the evidence would be too uncomfortable? What would it cost you to submit to the truth?
?
Al-Shafi'i said that Allah purified our hands from the blood of the fitnah, so we should purify our tongues. What are the 'bloodstains' in your own life—gossip, arguments, or grudges—that you need to purify your tongue from starting today? Name one relationship you will intentionally guard your tongue about this week.

Sectarian Positions on the Fitnah: The Majority View
The author discusses the Umariyya and Wasiliyya positions on testimony, then states the majority view on the wrongdoers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the positions of the Umariyya, Wasiliyya, and the majority of the community regarding the wrongdoers in the conflicts among the Companions.

Core Idea
The majority identifies the killers of Uthman and fighters against Ali as the wrongdoers.

In this final section on the fitnah, the author presents the views of two Mu'tazili sects—the Umariyya and Wasiliyya—who reject the testimony of both parties in the conflict. He then states the majority position, which holds the killers of Uthman and the fighters against Ali as the wrongdoers. The passage also includes footnote clarifications on related terms.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on sectarian positions
Read the Arabic and translation starting from 'Wat-tafaqat al-Umariyya' to the end.
2
Understand the Umariyya and Wasiliyya positions
What did these two sects agree on? Why did they reject testimony from the parties?
They rejected testimony because they considered both parties or one party as corrupt.
3
Grasp the majority view
What is the consensus of the majority? Who are identified as the wrongdoers?
The wrongdoers are the killers of Uthman and those who fought against Ali.
4
Review the footnotes
The footnotes explain terms like 'mudd', 'naseef', and 'gharad'. How do these clarify the hadiths?
They explain that even a small amount of spending from the Companions is more virtuous than spending a mountain of gold from later generations.

المقصد السابع : تعظيم الصحابة كلهم
( أنه يجب تعظيم الصحابة كلهم والكف عن القدح فيهم لأن الله سبحانه وتعالى عظمهم وأثنى عليهم في غير موضع من كتابه كقوله : والسابقون الأولون من المهاجرين والأنصار ﴾ [التوبة : ١٠٠ ] ، وقوله : يوم لا يخزي الله النبي
والذين آمنو معه نورهم يسعى بنى أيديهم ﴾ [التحريم: ۸] وقوله : والذين أشداء على الكفار رحماء بينهم تراهم ركعاً سجداً يبتغون فضلاً من الله ورضواناً ) [الفتح: ۲۹]، وقوله : لقد رضي الله عن المؤمنين إذ يبايعونك تحت الشجرة ) [الفتح : ۱۸] ، إلى غير ذلك من الآيات الدالة على عظم قدرهم وكرامتهم عند الله ) والرسول قد أحبهم وأثنى عليهم في أحاديث كثيرة ( منها قوله عليه السلام: «خير القرون قرني ثم الذين يلونهم ثم الذين يلونهم ، ومنها قوله : « لا تسبوا أصحابي فلو أن أحد أنفق مثل أحد ذهبا ما بلغ مد أحدهم ولا نصيفه» ومنها قوله : «الله الله في أصحابي لا تتخذوهم غرضاً بعدي فمن أحبهم فيحبي أحبهم، ومن أبغضهم فببغضي أبغضهم ومن آذاهم فقد آذاني ومن آذاني فقد آذى الله آذى الله فيوشك أن ومن يأخذه إلى غير ذلك من الأحاديث المشهورة في الكتب الصحاح ( ثم إن من تأمل سيرتهم ووقف على مآثرهم وجدهم في الدين وبذلهم أموالهم وأنفسهم في نصرة الله ورسوله لم يتخالجه شك في عظم شأنهم وبراءتهم عما ينسب إليهم المبطلون من المطاعن ومنعه ذلك أي تيقنه بحالهم ( عن الطعن فيهم فرأى ذلك مجانباً للإيمان، ونحن لا نلوث كتابنا بأمثال ذلك وهي مذكورة في المطولات مع التقصي عنها فارجع إليها إن أردت الوقوف عليها ( وأما الفتن والحروب الواقعة بين الصحابة، فالهشامية ) من المعتزلة ( أنكروا ،وقوعها، ولا شك أنه مكابرة للتواتر في قتل عثمان ووقعة الجمل ،وصفين والمعترفون بوقوعها منهم من سکت عن الكلام) فيها بتخطئة أو تصويب وهم طائفة من أهل السنة ) فإن أرادوا أنه اشتغال بما لا فلا يعني بأس به. إذ قال الشافعي ) وغيره من السلف : ( تلك دماء طهر الله عنها أيدينا فلنطهر عنها ألسنتنا، وإن أرادوا أنا لا نعلم أوقعت أم لا، فباطل لوقوعها قطعاً) وأنت خبير بأن الشق الثاني من الترديد ينافي الاعتراف بوقوعها ( واتفق العمرية أصحاب عمرو بن ،عبيد والواصلية أصحاب واصل بن عطاء، على رد شهادة الفريقين قالوا : لو شهد الجميع بباقة بقلة لم نقبلها، أما العمرية : فلأنهم يرون فسق الجميع من الفريقين ( وأما الواصلية : فلانهم يفسقون أحد الفريقين لا بعينه فلا يعلم عدالة شيء منهما . والذي عليه الجمهور من الأمة هو ( أن المخطئ قتلة عثمان ومحاربو علي لأنهما إما
قوله : (مد أحدهم ولا نصيفه المد ربع الصاع والنصيف مكيل دون المد ويجيء بمعنى النصف كالعشير بمعنى العشر أي لا ينال أحدكم بإنفاق مثل جبل أحد ذهباً من الفضيلة، والأجر ما ينال أحدهم بإنفاق مد طعام أو نصف منه لما يقارن من مزيد الإخلاص وصدق النية وكمال النفس مع ما بهم من البؤس والضر.
قوله : ( لا تتخذوهم (عرضاً أي هدفاً يرمونهم بالمنكرات والفواحش . قوله: (ينافي الاعتراف بوقوعها فلا يصح جعل هذا الشق من شقي الترديد في
المعترفين.
The Seventh Topic: Veneration of All the Companions (It is obligatory to venerate all the Companions and refrain from disparaging them, because Allah the Exalted has magnified them and praised them in many places of His Book, such as His saying: 'And the foremost, the first of the Muhajirun and the Ansar' [9:100], and His saying: 'On the Day when Allah will not disgrace the Prophet and those who believed with him, their light proceeding before them' [66:8], and His saying: 'Those who are severe against the disbelievers, merciful among themselves; you see them bowing and prostrating, seeking bounty from Allah and [His] pleasure' [48:29], and His saying: 'Certainly Allah was pleased with the believers when they pledged allegiance to you under the tree' [48:18], and other verses indicating the greatness of their status and their honor with Allah. And the Messenger loved them and praised them in many hadiths, including his saying, peace be upon him: 'The best of generations is my generation, then those who follow them, then those who follow them,' and his saying: 'Do not insult my Companions, for if anyone were to spend the equivalent of Mount Uhud in gold, he would not reach the measure of a mudd of one of them, nor half of it,' and his saying: 'Allah, Allah regarding my Companions! Do not take them as targets after me. Whoever loves them loves me, and whoever hates them hates me, and whoever harms them harms me, and whoever harms me harms Allah, and whoever harms Allah, Allah will soon seize him.' And other famous hadiths in the authentic books. Then whoever contemplates their conduct and comes to know their exploits finds them in religion, their spending of their wealth and themselves in support of Allah and His Messenger, such that no doubt enters him about the greatness of their status and their innocence from the accusations that the false ones attribute to them. And that—i.e., his certainty of their state—prevents him from disparaging them, and he sees that as contrary to faith. And we do not sully our book with things like that; they are mentioned in the lengthy works with investigation, so refer to them if you want to know them. As for the seditions and wars that occurred among the Companions, the Hishamiyya among the Mu'tazila denied their occurrence. There is no doubt that is an obstinate denial of the widespread transmission of the killing of Uthman, the Battle of the Camel, and Siffin. And those who acknowledge their occurrence, among them are those who remain silent about them without declaring error or correctness, and they are a group from the Ahl al-Sunna. If they mean that it is an occupation with what does not concern them, then there is no harm. For al-Shafi'i and others of the Salaf said: 'Those are bloodstains from which Allah has purified our hands, so let us purify our tongues from them.' And if they mean that we do not know whether they occurred or not, then it is false because their occurrence is certain. And you are aware that the second part of the disjunction contradicts the acknowledgment of their occurrence. And the Umariyya, the followers of Amr ibn Ubayd, and the Wasiliyya, the followers of Wasil ibn Ata, agreed to reject the testimony of either party. They said: If all of them testified on a bunch of herbs [؟], we would not accept it. As for the Umariyya, it is because they consider all of both parties to be corrupt. As for the Wasiliyya, it is because they consider one of the parties to be corrupt, not specifically, so the integrity of either is not known. And the view held by the majority of the community is that the wrongdoers are the killers of Uthman and the fighters against Ali, because they are either... (then footnotes: His saying: (A mudd of one of them nor half of it): the mudd is a quarter of a sa', and the naseef is a measure less than a mudd, and it comes in the meaning of half, like 'asheer' meaning a tenth. That is, none of you will attain, by spending the equivalent of Mount Uhud in gold, the virtue and reward that one of them attains by spending a mudd of food or half of it, due to the greater sincerity, truthful intention, perfection of soul, and the hardship and poverty they experienced. His saying: (Do not take them as targets): i.e., a target at which they shoot with objectionable things and obscenities. His saying: (contradicts the acknowledgment of their occurrence): so it is not correct to make this part of the two parts of the disjunction among those who acknowledge.)
Source pages p. 405

Commentary
This passage covers the seventh topic on the obligatory veneration of all the Companions and addresses the issue of the conflicts among them. The author provides several proofs: Quranic verses praising the Companions, hadiths of the Prophet commanding love and respect for them, and the argument from their observable deeds and sacrifices. He urges restraint from speaking about the accusations against them, directing the reader to longer works. Then he discusses the fitan (seditions) among the Companions. He mentions the Hishamiyyah branch of the Mu'tazila who deny the occurrence of those wars, which he calls stubbornness against mutawatir reports. Among those who acknowledge the wars, some (a group of Ahl al-Sunnah) remain silent, not declaring any party wrong. He explains that if they mean not to engage in a useless matter, that is acceptable quoting al-Shafi'i; but if they claim ignorance of the occurrence, that is false because the events are certain. He then notes that the second part contradicts the acknowledgment. He also mentions the Umariyyah and Wasiliyyah who reject the testimony of both parties, explaining their reasons. Finally, he states the majority position: the wrongdoers are the killers of Uthman and those who fought Ali. The footnotes clarify the linguistic meaning of 'mudd' and 'naseef' in the hadith about spending gold, explain 'la tattakhidhuhum gharadan', and explain that the second part of the disjunction contradicts the acknowledgment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of the community, who are the wrongdoers in the fitnah?
A) Both parties
B) The killers of Uthman and those who fought Ali
C) Ali and his supporters
D) Muawiya and his supporters

Key Takeaway
The majority of scholars hold that the killers of Uthman and the fighters against Ali are the wrongdoers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear about the conflict between the Companions, do you find yourself taking sides? How does knowing that the majority identified the killers of Uthman and those who fought Ali as wrongdoers challenge you to view the fitnah with humility rather than partisanship? Will you commit to avoiding sectarian loyalty that blinds you to truth?
?
The Umariyya and Wasiliyya judged the witnesses as corrupt. How often do you dismiss someone's testimony or character based on their association with a group? Are you willing to judge individuals fairly rather than condemn whole groups? What step can you take this week to practice that fairness?
?
This lesson shows that scholars disagreed on who was wrong. Does your certainty about historical events ever keep you from recognizing your own potential for error? How can you remain confident in truth while staying open to correction?

Veneration of the Companions: Qur'anic and Prophetic Evidence
Author cites Qur'an and hadith for veneration of Companions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scriptural basis for venerating all Companions through explicit Qur'anic verses and authentic hadiths.

Core Idea
The Qur'an and Prophet command love and respect for all Companions.

This lesson begins with the foundational proofs for the high status of the Companions. The author cites a Qur'anic verse and several well-known hadiths that establish their special rank and warn against reviling them. Understanding these texts is essential before discussing later historical events.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on veneration
Read the Arabic passage that includes the verse [al-Fath: 18] and the three hadiths. Notice the direct commands to honor the Companions.
The hadith about 'best generation' and 'do not revile' are especially important.
2
Identify the key evidence
Identify which Qur'anic verse is cited and what each hadith adds. The first hadith establishes temporal priority, the second warns against verbal abuse, and the third links love of Companions to love of the Prophet.
3
Reflect on the implications
Consider why the author places this evidence first. It sets a tone of respect that frames all subsequent discussion of the fitan.
This evidence is meant to be definitive and uncontroversial.

[ الفتح : ۱۸] ، إلى غير ذلك من الآيات الدالة على عظم قدرهم وكرامتهم عند الله ) والرسول قد أحبهم وأثنى عليهم في أحاديث كثيرة ( منها قوله عليه السلام: «خير القرون قرني ثم الذين يلونهم ثم الذين يلونهم ، ومنها قوله : « لا تسبوا أصحابي فلو أن أحد أنفق مثل أحد ذهبا ما بلغ مد أحدهم ولا نصيفه» ومنها قوله : «الله الله في أصحابي لا تتخذوهم غرضاً بعدي فمن أحبهم فيحبي أحبهم، ومن أبغضهم فببغضي أبغضهم ومن آذاهم فقد آذاني ومن آذاني فقد آذى الله آذى الله فيوشك أن ومن يأخذه إلى غير ذلك من الأحاديث المشهورة في الكتب الصحاح ( ثم إن من تأمل سيرتهم ووقف على مآثرهم وجدهم في الدين وبذلهم أموالهم وأنفسهم في نصرة الله ورسوله لم يتخالجه شك في عظم شأنهم وبراءتهم عما ينسب إليهم المبطلون من المطاعن ومنعه ذلك أي تيقنه بحالهم ( عن الطعن فيهم فرأى ذلك مجانباً للإيمان، ونحن لا نلوث كتابنا بأمثال ذلك وهي مذكورة في المطولات مع التقصي عنها فارجع إليها إن أردت الوقوف عليها ( وأما الفتن والحروب الواقعة بين الصحابة، فالهشامية ) من المعتزلة ( أنكروا ،وقوعها، ولا شك أنه مكابرة للتواتر في قتل عثمان ووقعة الجمل ،وصفين والمعترفون بوقوعها منهم من سکت عن الكلام) فيها بتخطئة أو تصويب وهم طائفة من أهل السنة ) فإن أرادوا أنه اشتغال بما لا فلا يعني بأس به. إذ قال الشافعي ) وغيره من السلف : ( تلك دماء طهر الله عنها أيدينا فلنطهر عنها ألسنتنا، وإن أرادوا أنا لا نعلم أوقعت أم لا، فباطل لوقوعها قطعاً) وأنت خبير بأن الشق الثاني من الترديد ينافي الاعتراف بوقوعها ( واتفق العمرية أصحاب عمرو بن ،عبيد والواصلية أصحاب واصل بن عطاء، على رد شهادة الفريقين قالوا : لو شهد الجميع بباقة بقلة لم نقبلها، أما العمرية : فلأنهم يرون فسق الجميع من الفريقين ( وأما الواصلية : فلانهم يفسقون أحد الفريقين لا بعينه فلا يعلم عدالة شيء منهما . والذي عليه الجمهور من الأمة هو ( أن المخطئ قتلة عثمان ومحاربو علي لأنهما إما
قوله : (مد أحدهم ولا نصيفه المد ربع الصاع والنصيف مكيل دون المد ويجيء بمعنى النصف كالعشير بمعنى العشر أي لا ينال أحدكم بإنفاق مثل جبل أحد ذهباً من الفضيلة، والأجر ما ينال أحدهم بإنفاق مد طعام أو نصف منه لما يقارن من مزيد الإخلاص وصدق النية وكمال النفس مع ما بهم من البؤس والضر.

إمامان فيحرم القطع والمخالفة (قطعاً إلا أن بعضهم كالقاضي أبي بكر ذهب إلى أن هذه التخطئة لا تبلغ إلى حد التفسيق ومنهم من ذهب إلى التفسيق كالشيعة وكثير من أصحابنا .
The Fourth Observatory - Seventh Objective: Veneration of all the Companions. [al-Fath: 18], and other verses indicating the greatness of their rank and honor with Allah. And the Messenger loved them and praised them in many hadiths, including his saying, peace be upon him: 'The best of generations is my generation, then those who follow them, then those who follow them.' And including his saying: 'Do not revile my Companions, for if anyone were to spend the equivalent of Mount Uhud in gold, he would not reach the measure of a mudd of one of them, nor half of it.' And including his saying: 'Allah, Allah regarding my Companions; do not make them targets after me. Whoever loves them loves me; whoever hates them hates me. Whoever harms them has harmed me; whoever harms me has harmed Allah; whoever harms Allah, Allah will soon seize him.' And other well-known hadiths in the authentic books. Then indeed, whoever contemplates their biography and stops at their noble deeds finds them in religion, and their spending of wealth and themselves in supporting Allah and His Messenger, no doubt enters him about the greatness of their status and their innocence from the accusations that the false ones attribute to them, and that prevents him, i.e., his certainty of their condition, from attacking them, and he sees that as incompatible with faith. And we do not soil our book with such things; they are mentioned in lengthy works with investigation about them, so refer to them if you wish to learn about them. As for the seditions and wars that occurred among the Companions, the Hishamiyya of the Mu'tazila denied their occurrence, and there is no doubt that it is an obstinate denial of the mutawatir reports of the killing of Uthman and the battles of Jamal and Siffin. And among those who acknowledge their occurrence, some remained silent about speaking about them, with declaration of error or correctness, and they are a group of Ahl al-Sunna. If they meant that it is an occupation with something that is not [important], then it is not problematic. For al-Shafi'i and other predecessors said: 'Those are bloods from which Allah has purified our hands, so let us purify our tongues from them.' And if they meant that we do not know whether they occurred or not, then it is false because they definitely occurred. And you are aware that the second part of the disjunction contradicts acknowledging their occurrence. And al-Umariyya, the followers of Amr ibn Ubayd, and al-Wasiliyya, the followers of Wasil ibn Ata, agreed on rejecting the testimony of both parties. They said: If all of them gave testimony about a single herb, we would not accept it. As for al-Umariyya, because they consider all of both parties to be sinful. As for al-Wasiliyya, because they consider one of the two parties sinful but not specifically, so the justice of any of them is not known. And what the majority of the umma holds is that the mistaken ones are the killers of Uthman and the fighters against Ali, because they are either two imams, so killing and opposing them are absolutely forbidden. However, some, like al-Qadi Abu Bakr, held that this declaration of error does not reach the level of declaring them sinful (tafsiq), and some went to declaring them sinful, like the Shia and many of our companions.
Source pages p. 406

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive discussion on the veneration of the Companions and the approach to the conflicts (fitan) that occurred among them. The author begins by stating the Qur'anic verse [al-Fath: 18] as evidence for their great rank. Then he presents several hadiths: 'The best of generations is my generation...', 'Do not revile my Companions...', and 'Allah, Allah regarding my Companions...'. These establish the love and honor due to them. The author then argues that anyone who studies their lives will have no doubt about their virtue and innocence from accusations. He then turns to the fitan, noting that the Hishamiyya among the Mu'tazila denied their occurrence, which is against the mutawatir reports of the killing of Uthman and the battles of Jamal and Siffin. Among those who acknowledge the fitan, some (a group from Ahl al-Sunna) remain silent without declaring who was right or wrong, following the principle of al-Shafi'i that we should not delve into these matters. Others claim ignorance of whether they occurred, which is false. The author then mentions that al-Umariyya and al-Wasiliyya reject the testimony of both parties, with different justifications. Finally, he states the position of the majority: the wrongdoer (al-mukhti') is the killers of Uthman and those who fought against Ali, because both were imams, thus their killing and opposition are absolutely forbidden. However, there is disagreement on whether this error amounts to tafsīq (declaring them sinful): al-Qadi Abu Bakr and others do not go that far, while the Shia and many of our companions do. The footnotes explain the meaning of 'mudd' and 'nasif' and the phrase 'do not make them targets.'

Key Terms
الصحابة
الفتح
خير القرون

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That some Companions are unworthy of veneration due to later conflicts.
Correction: The Qur'an and hadith demand veneration of all Companions collectively, regardless of later events.

Checkpoint
Which Qur'anic verse is cited as evidence for the high rank of the Companions?
A) al-Fath: 18
B) al-Baqarah: 285
C) al-Imran: 110
D) al-Hashr: 8

Key Takeaway
The Qur'an and authentic hadiths establish an unconditional obligation to venerate all Companions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet said, 'Whoever hates my Companions hates me.' Look into your heart: is there any trace of resentment or criticism towards any Companion, perhaps for something you've heard about him? Will you actively replace that feeling with love and seek to defend them from now on?
?
If you could spend Mount Uhud in gold for the sake of Islam, you would not reach the measure of a mudd of a Companion. How does this truth reshape your view of your own contributions and sacrifices? Will you stop measuring your worth by your deeds and instead humble yourself before their unmatched legacy?
?
The Prophet commanded, 'Do not make them targets after me.' In what ways might you—through jokes, casual talk, or accepting common narratives—be indirectly targeting the Companions? Will you make a firm resolve to guard your tongue and heart against any disrespect today?

The Virtue of the Companions and Their Innocence from Accusations
Author argues from biography that Companions are innocent and attacking them is against faith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that reflection on the Companions' lives confirms their excellence and innocence from false accusations, and that attacking them is incompatible with faith.

Core Idea
Studying the Companions' lives removes doubt about their virtue.

After presenting the scriptural evidence, the author now invites the reader to reflect on the actual biographies of the Companions. Their sacrifices and devotion are so clear that anyone who studies them will have no doubt about their greatness and will reject any accusations against them. The author also mentions that detailed responses to such accusations can be found elsewhere.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on contemplation
Read the Arabic passage starting from 'ثم إن من تأمل سيرتهم' to the end of the paragraph. Note the author's argument.
2
Understand the argument from biography
The author argues that studying the Companions' lives leads to certainty about their high status and innocence. This is a historical/empirical argument.
This complements the scriptural evidence.
3
Note the disclaimer
The author says he will not soil his book with the accusations, directing interested readers to longer works. This shows a conscious choice not to engage with false claims.

[ الفتح : ۱۸] ، إلى غير ذلك من الآيات الدالة على عظم قدرهم وكرامتهم عند الله ) والرسول قد أحبهم وأثنى عليهم في أحاديث كثيرة ( منها قوله عليه السلام: «خير القرون قرني ثم الذين يلونهم ثم الذين يلونهم ، ومنها قوله : « لا تسبوا أصحابي فلو أن أحد أنفق مثل أحد ذهبا ما بلغ مد أحدهم ولا نصيفه» ومنها قوله : «الله الله في أصحابي لا تتخذوهم غرضاً بعدي فمن أحبهم فيحبي أحبهم، ومن أبغضهم فببغضي أبغضهم ومن آذاهم فقد آذاني ومن آذاني فقد آذى الله آذى الله فيوشك أن ومن يأخذه إلى غير ذلك من الأحاديث المشهورة في الكتب الصحاح ( ثم إن من تأمل سيرتهم ووقف على مآثرهم وجدهم في الدين وبذلهم أموالهم وأنفسهم في نصرة الله ورسوله لم يتخالجه شك في عظم شأنهم وبراءتهم عما ينسب إليهم المبطلون من المطاعن ومنعه ذلك أي تيقنه بحالهم ( عن الطعن فيهم فرأى ذلك مجانباً للإيمان، ونحن لا نلوث كتابنا بأمثال ذلك وهي مذكورة في المطولات مع التقصي عنها فارجع إليها إن أردت الوقوف عليها ( وأما الفتن والحروب الواقعة بين الصحابة، فالهشامية ) من المعتزلة ( أنكروا ،وقوعها، ولا شك أنه مكابرة للتواتر في قتل عثمان ووقعة الجمل ،وصفين والمعترفون بوقوعها منهم من سکت عن الكلام) فيها بتخطئة أو تصويب وهم طائفة من أهل السنة ) فإن أرادوا أنه اشتغال بما لا فلا يعني بأس به. إذ قال الشافعي ) وغيره من السلف : ( تلك دماء طهر الله عنها أيدينا فلنطهر عنها ألسنتنا، وإن أرادوا أنا لا نعلم أوقعت أم لا، فباطل لوقوعها قطعاً) وأنت خبير بأن الشق الثاني من الترديد ينافي الاعتراف بوقوعها ( واتفق العمرية أصحاب عمرو بن ،عبيد والواصلية أصحاب واصل بن عطاء، على رد شهادة الفريقين قالوا : لو شهد الجميع بباقة بقلة لم نقبلها، أما العمرية : فلأنهم يرون فسق الجميع من الفريقين ( وأما الواصلية : فلانهم يفسقون أحد الفريقين لا بعينه فلا يعلم عدالة شيء منهما . والذي عليه الجمهور من الأمة هو ( أن المخطئ قتلة عثمان ومحاربو علي لأنهما إما
قوله : (مد أحدهم ولا نصيفه المد ربع الصاع والنصيف مكيل دون المد ويجيء بمعنى النصف كالعشير بمعنى العشر أي لا ينال أحدكم بإنفاق مثل جبل أحد ذهباً من الفضيلة، والأجر ما ينال أحدهم بإنفاق مد طعام أو نصف منه لما يقارن من مزيد الإخلاص وصدق النية وكمال النفس مع ما بهم من البؤس والضر.
قوله : ( لا تتخذوهم (عرضاً أي هدفاً يرمونهم بالمنكرات والفواحش . قوله: (ينافي الاعتراف بوقوعها فلا يصح جعل هذا الشق من شقي الترديد في المعترفين.
إمامان فيحرم القطع والمخالفة (قطعاً إلا أن بعضهم كالقاضي أبي بكر ذهب إلى أن هذه التخطئة لا تبلغ إلى حد التفسيق ومنهم من ذهب إلى التفسيق كالشيعة وكثير من أصحابنا .
The Fourth Observatory - Seventh Objective: Veneration of all the Companions. [al-Fath: 18], and other verses indicating the greatness of their rank and honor with Allah. And the Messenger loved them and praised them in many hadiths, including his saying, peace be upon him: 'The best of generations is my generation, then those who follow them, then those who follow them.' And including his saying: 'Do not revile my Companions, for if anyone were to spend the equivalent of Mount Uhud in gold, he would not reach the measure of a mudd of one of them, nor half of it.' And including his saying: 'Allah, Allah regarding my Companions; do not make them targets after me. Whoever loves them loves me; whoever hates them hates me. Whoever harms them has harmed me; whoever harms me has harmed Allah; whoever harms Allah, Allah will soon seize him.' And other well-known hadiths in the authentic books. Then indeed, whoever contemplates their biography and stops at their noble deeds finds them in religion, and their spending of wealth and themselves in supporting Allah and His Messenger, no doubt enters him about the greatness of their status and their innocence from the accusations that the false ones attribute to them, and that prevents him, i.e., his certainty of their condition, from attacking them, and he sees that as incompatible with faith. And we do not soil our book with such things; they are mentioned in lengthy works with investigation about them, so refer to them if you wish to learn about them. As for the seditions and wars that occurred among the Companions, the Hishamiyya of the Mu'tazila denied their occurrence, and there is no doubt that it is an obstinate denial of the mutawatir reports of the killing of Uthman and the battles of Jamal and Siffin. And among those who acknowledge their occurrence, some remained silent about speaking about them, with declaration of error or correctness, and they are a group of Ahl al-Sunna. If they meant that it is an occupation with something that is not [important], then it is not problematic. For al-Shafi'i and other predecessors said: 'Those are bloods from which Allah has purified our hands, so let us purify our tongues from them.' And if they meant that we do not know whether they occurred or not, then it is false because they definitely occurred. And you are aware that the second part of the disjunction contradicts acknowledging their occurrence. And al-Umariyya, the followers of Amr ibn Ubayd, and al-Wasiliyya, the followers of Wasil ibn Ata, agreed on rejecting the testimony of both parties. They said: If all of them gave testimony about a single herb, we would not accept it. As for al-Umariyya, because they consider all of both parties to be sinful. As for al-Wasiliyya, because they consider one of the two parties sinful but not specifically, so the justice of any of them is not known. And what the majority of the umma holds is that the mistaken ones are the killers of Uthman and the fighters against Ali, because they are either two imams, so killing and opposing them are absolutely forbidden. However, some, like al-Qadi Abu Bakr, held that this declaration of error does not reach the level of declaring them sinful (tafsiq), and some went to declaring them sinful, like the Shia and many of our companions.
Source pages p. 406

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive discussion on the veneration of the Companions and the approach to the conflicts (fitan) that occurred among them. The author begins by stating the Qur'anic verse [al-Fath: 18] as evidence for their great rank. Then he presents several hadiths: 'The best of generations is my generation...', 'Do not revile my Companions...', and 'Allah, Allah regarding my Companions...'. These establish the love and honor due to them. The author then argues that anyone who studies their lives will have no doubt about their virtue and innocence from accusations. He then turns to the fitan, noting that the Hishamiyya among the Mu'tazila denied their occurrence, which is against the mutawatir reports of the killing of Uthman and the battles of Jamal and Siffin. Among those who acknowledge the fitan, some (a group from Ahl al-Sunna) remain silent without declaring who was right or wrong, following the principle of al-Shafi'i that we should not delve into these matters. Others claim ignorance of whether they occurred, which is false. The author then mentions that al-Umariyya and al-Wasiliyya reject the testimony of both parties, with different justifications. Finally, he states the position of the majority: the wrongdoer (al-mukhti') is the killers of Uthman and those who fought against Ali, because both were imams, thus their killing and opposition are absolutely forbidden. However, there is disagreement on whether this error amounts to tafsīq (declaring them sinful): al-Qadi Abu Bakr and others do not go that far, while the Shia and many of our companions do. The footnotes explain the meaning of 'mudd' and 'nasif' and the phrase 'do not make them targets.'

Key Terms
سيرتهم
مآثرهم
المبطلون
المطاعن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what prevents a person from attacking the Companions after studying their lives?
A) Lack of evidence
B) Certainty of their innocence
C) Fear of public opinion
D) Lack of time

Key Takeaway
A frank study of the Companions' lives leaves no room for doubt about their excellence and innocence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear a negative remark about a Companion, does your heart immediately defend them, or do you entertain doubt? Have you truly contemplated their sacrifices as this lesson demands? What will you do the next time such an accusation comes your way?
?
The author says certainty of the Companions' innocence prevents attacking them and sees that as incompatible with faith. Is there any Companion you have secretly doubted or criticised in your heart? Will you repent from that and commit to studying their lives to remove that doubt?
?
You have just read that studying the Companions' biographies removes doubt. When will you actually take time to read their stories? What is stopping you from doing that today?

Sects and Disagreements
intermediate
4 min
The Historical Reality of the Fitan and the Denial of the Hishamiyya
Author refutes Hishamiyya denial of fitan by invoking tawatur.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the fitan (civil wars) among the Companions are historically established via tawatur, and that denying them, as the Hishamiyya did, is obstinate.

Core Idea
The fitan among Companions are proven by mass transmission (tawatur).

The author now turns to the seditions that occurred among the Companions. He begins by addressing a group that denied these events entirely—the Hishamiyya subsect of the Mu'tazila. The author declares this denial an obstinate rejection of mutawatir reports, citing the killing of Uthman and the battles of Jamal and Siffin as well-known examples.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on fitan and Hishamiyya
Read the Arabic passage from 'وأما الفتن والحروب' to 'لوقوعها قطعاً'.
2
Understand the concept of tawatur
The author uses the term 'المتواتر' to mean reports transmitted by so many that their truth is certain. The three events are given as examples.
Tawatur is a key concept in kalam for establishing historical facts.
3
Analyze the refutation of denial
The author calls the denial 'مكابرة' (obstinate rejection) and provides two arguments: the first, that it contradicts tawatur; the second, that even those who remain silent acknowledge occurrence, and those who claim ignorance are refuted because it definitely happened.
This sets up the discussion of the proper response.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the fitan among Companions never happened.
Correction: The fitan are historically proven by mutawatir reports; denying them is obstinate.

Checkpoint
Which group denied the occurrence of the fitan according to the text?
A) The Hishamiyya
B) The Umariyya
C) The Wasiliyya
D) The Shia

Key Takeaway
The fitan among the Companions are historically certain, and denying them contradicts clear evidence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear about the conflicts among the Companions, do you find yourself instinctively taking sides or judging who was right? How does al-Shafiʿī's statement—'Those are bloods from which Allah has purified our hands, so let us purify our tongues from them'—expose a need in your own heart to avoid such judgments?
?
You know the fitan definitely occurred, yet do you ever subtly excuse yourself from learning about them because they are uncomfortable or confusing? The Hishamiyya denial is called 'obstinate'—but is your avoidance also a form of denial, and how will you respond to the truth of tawatur with courage instead of silence?
?
'And you are aware that the second part of the disjunction contradicts acknowledging their occurrence.' Is there any truth you claim to accept in your mind but live as if you are ignorant of it? What would change in your daily life if you truly acted on the certainty of this historical fact?

The Umariyya and Wasiliyya on Testimony and the Majority Ruling
Author presents positions on testimony rejection and the majority's ruling on error and tafsir.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the positions of Umariyya and Wasiliyya on rejecting testimony of both factions in the fitan, and the majority view that the killers of Uthman and fighters against Ali are mistaken, with a debate on whether this constitutes tafsir.

Core Idea
The majority condemn the killers of Uthman and fighters against Ali as mistaken, but differ on tafsir.

This lesson covers the final part of the passage, which addresses the legal and theological consequences of the fitan. Two Mu'tazili subsects, al-Umariyya and al-Wasiliyya, agreed that the testimony of both warring parties should be rejected, but for different reasons. The author then presents the majority Sunni position: the killers of Uthman and those who fought against Ali are mistaken, since both were imams. However, there is a difference of opinion on whether this error amounts to declaring them sinful (tafsir).

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on Umariyya and Wasiliyya
Read from 'واتفق العمرية' to the end of the Arabic. Focus on the two groups and their reasoning.
2
Understand the two rationales
Al-Umariyya considered both parties sinful, so their testimony is rejected. Al-Wasiliyya considered one party sinful but not specifically identified, so the justice of any individual is unknown.
Both lead to same practical conclusion: rejection of all testimony from the fitan participants.
3
Analyze the majority view
The majority of the umma holds that the mistaken party is the killers of Uthman and those who fought Ali. Some (like al-Qadi Abu Bakr) say this error does not reach tafsir; others (like the Shia and many Ash'aris) consider it tafsir.
This shows a spectrum of opinion within Ahl al-Sunna.

قوله : (مد أحدهم ولا نصيفه المد ربع الصاع والنصيف مكيل دون المد ويجيء بمعنى النصف كالعشير بمعنى العشر أي لا ينال أحدكم بإنفاق مثل جبل أحد ذهباً من الفضيلة، والأجر ما ينال أحدهم بإنفاق مد طعام أو نصف منه لما يقارن من مزيد الإخلاص وصدق النية وكمال النفس مع ما بهم من البؤس والضر.
