إمامان فيحرم القطع والمخالفة (قطعاً إلا أن بعضهم كالقاضي أبي بكر ذهب إلى أن هذه التخطئة لا تبلغ إلى حد التفسيق ومنهم من ذهب إلى التفسيق كالشيعة وكثير من أصحابنا .
The Fourth Observatory - Seventh Objective: Veneration of all the Companions. [al-Fath: 18], and other verses indicating the greatness of their rank and honor with Allah. And the Messenger loved them and praised them in many hadiths, including his saying, peace be upon him: 'The best of generations is my generation, then those who follow them, then those who follow them.' And including his saying: 'Do not revile my Companions, for if anyone were to spend the equivalent of Mount Uhud in gold, he would not reach the measure of a mudd of one of them, nor half of it.' And including his saying: 'Allah, Allah regarding my Companions; do not make them targets after me. Whoever loves them loves me; whoever hates them hates me. Whoever harms them has harmed me; whoever harms me has harmed Allah; whoever harms Allah, Allah will soon seize him.' And other well-known hadiths in the authentic books. Then indeed, whoever contemplates their biography and stops at their noble deeds finds them in religion, and their spending of wealth and themselves in supporting Allah and His Messenger, no doubt enters him about the greatness of their status and their innocence from the accusations that the false ones attribute to them, and that prevents him, i.e., his certainty of their condition, from attacking them, and he sees that as incompatible with faith. And we do not soil our book with such things; they are mentioned in lengthy works with investigation about them, so refer to them if you wish to learn about them. As for the seditions and wars that occurred among the Companions, the Hishamiyya of the Mu'tazila denied their occurrence, and there is no doubt that it is an obstinate denial of the mutawatir reports of the killing of Uthman and the battles of Jamal and Siffin. And among those who acknowledge their occurrence, some remained silent about speaking about them, with declaration of error or correctness, and they are a group of Ahl al-Sunna. If they meant that it is an occupation with something that is not [important], then it is not problematic. For al-Shafi'i and other predecessors said: 'Those are bloods from which Allah has purified our hands, so let us purify our tongues from them.' And if they meant that we do not know whether they occurred or not, then it is false because they definitely occurred. And you are aware that the second part of the disjunction contradicts acknowledging their occurrence. And al-Umariyya, the followers of Amr ibn Ubayd, and al-Wasiliyya, the followers of Wasil ibn Ata, agreed on rejecting the testimony of both parties. They said: If all of them gave testimony about a single herb, we would not accept it. As for al-Umariyya, because they consider all of both parties to be sinful. As for al-Wasiliyya, because they consider one of the two parties sinful but not specifically, so the justice of any of them is not known. And what the majority of the umma holds is that the mistaken ones are the killers of Uthman and the fighters against Ali, because they are either two imams, so killing and opposing them are absolutely forbidden. However, some, like al-Qadi Abu Bakr, held that this declaration of error does not reach the level of declaring them sinful (tafsiq), and some went to declaring them sinful, like the Shia and many of our companions.
Source pages p. 406

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive discussion on the veneration of the Companions and the approach to the conflicts (fitan) that occurred among them. The author begins by stating the Qur'anic verse [al-Fath: 18] as evidence for their great rank. Then he presents several hadiths: 'The best of generations is my generation...', 'Do not revile my Companions...', and 'Allah, Allah regarding my Companions...'. These establish the love and honor due to them. The author then argues that anyone who studies their lives will have no doubt about their virtue and innocence from accusations. He then turns to the fitan, noting that the Hishamiyya among the Mu'tazila denied their occurrence, which is against the mutawatir reports of the killing of Uthman and the battles of Jamal and Siffin. Among those who acknowledge the fitan, some (a group from Ahl al-Sunna) remain silent without declaring who was right or wrong, following the principle of al-Shafi'i that we should not delve into these matters. Others claim ignorance of whether they occurred, which is false. The author then mentions that al-Umariyya and al-Wasiliyya reject the testimony of both parties, with different justifications. Finally, he states the position of the majority: the wrongdoer (al-mukhti') is the killers of Uthman and those who fought against Ali, because both were imams, thus their killing and opposition are absolutely forbidden. However, there is disagreement on whether this error amounts to tafsīq (declaring them sinful): al-Qadi Abu Bakr and others do not go that far, while the Shia and many of our companions do. The footnotes explain the meaning of 'mudd' and 'nasif' and the phrase 'do not make them targets.'

الواصلية
الشهادة
التفسيق
المخطئ
قتلة عثمان
محاربو علي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That all participants in the fitan are considered sinful (fasiq) by Sunni majority.
Correction: The majority only declares the killers of Uthman and fighters against Ali as mistaken, and whether this is tafsir is debated.

Checkpoint
According to the majority of the umma, who are considered the mistaken party (al-mukhti') in the fitan?
A) Both sides equally
B) The killers of Uthman and the fighters against Ali
C) Ali and his supporters
D) Uthman and his supporters

Key Takeaway
The majority holds that those who killed Uthman and fought Ali are mistaken, but there is no consensus on whether this error amounts to sinfulness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear about the early conflicts among the Sahaba, do you find yourself quickly taking sides or condemning one party? How does this lesson’s distinction between error and sinfulness challenge you to withhold judgment and trust in Allah’s mercy for those who made ijtihad? What step will you take today to avoid repeating their mistakes in your own conflicts?
?
The Umariyya and Wasiliyya rejected the testimony of everyone involved because they saw sin in all. Is there a person or group you have dismissed entirely because of a perceived fault? How can you, like the majority, recognize the possibility of sincere intention even in error, and what change in attitude does this demand of you?
?
Al-Qadi Abu Bakr refrained from declaring the mistaken party sinful, while others did. Reflect on a time you were quick to label someone’s mistake as a sin. How does the reminder that error does not automatically equal sin affect your view of those who differ from you? Commit to one concrete way you will practice hilm (forbearance) this week.

Dispute over Requiring Imam's Permission
Dispute over Imam's permission and classification of obligation types.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the different positions regarding whether commanding good and forbidding evil requires the Imam's permission, and how these positions are classified.

Core Idea
The obligation to command good is disputed, not on its existence but on its condition.

This lesson explores the range of opinions on whether commanding good and forbidding evil depends on the Imam's authorization. From the Rawafid's strict condition to the various views of Ahl al-Sunna and Mu'tazila, we see a spectrum of reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage describing the Rawafid view and the subsequent divisions.
2
Identify the three main positions
Identify the Rawafid, Ahl al-Sunna, and Mu'tazila positions, noting the internal split between al-Jubba'i and Abu Hashim.
3
Reflect on the significance
Notice how each school grounds its obligation differently—some by reason, some by revelation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الآمدي : ذهب بعض الروافض إلى أنه لا يجب بل لا يجوز الأمر بالمعروف والنهي عن المنكر إلا بنصب الإمام واستنابته كما في إقامة الحدود وذهب من عداهم إلى وجوبه مطلقاً، ثم اختلفوا فذهب أهل السنة إلى وجوبه شرعاً، والجبائي وابنه إلى وجوبه عقلاً ثم اختلفا فقال الجبائي : يجب مطلقاً فيما يدرك حسنه وقبحه عقلاً، وقال أبو هاشم : إن تضمن الأمر بالمعروف والنهي عن المنكر دفع ضرر عن الآمر والناهي ولا يندفع عنه إلا بذلك ،وجب، وإلا فلا والذي يدل على وجوبه عندنا الإجماع فإن القائل :قائلان قائل بوجوبه مطلقاً وقائل بوجوبه باستنابة الإمام فقد اتفق الكل على وجوبه في الجملة والكتاب كقوله تعالى : ﴿ ولتكن منكم أمة يدعون إلى الخير ويأمرون بالمعروف وينهون عن المنكر ﴾ [آل عمران : ١٠٤]، والسنة كقوله عليه السلام لتأمرون بالمعروف ولتنهن عن المنكر أو ليسلطن الله شراركم على خياركم فيدعو خياركم فلا يستجاب لهم. وأما عدم توقف جوازه على استنابة الإمام فيدل عليه أن كل واحد من آحاد الصحابة كان يشتغل بالأمر بالمعروف والنهي عن المنكر بلا استنابة وإذن من الإمام، وكان ذلك شائعاً ذائعاً فيما بينهم ولم يوجد نكير فكان إجماعاً على جوازه ( ولوجوبه )
Al-Amidi said: Some of the Rawafid held that commanding good and forbidding evil is not obligatory, rather not even permissible, except with the appointment and deputization of the Imam, like the execution of legal punishments. And those other than them held its obligation absolutely. Then they differed: the Ahl al-Sunna held its obligation by divine law (shar'an), while al-Jubba'i and his son held its obligation by reason ('aqlan). Then they differed: al-Jubba'i said it is obligatory absolutely regarding what is perceived as good and bad by reason, while Abu Hashim said: if commanding good and forbidding evil entails repelling harm from the commander and forbiddener, and that harm is not repelled except by that, then it is obligatory; otherwise not. And what indicates its obligation according to us is consensus (ijma'), for there are two groups: one holds it obligatory absolutely, and the other holds it obligatory with the deputization of the Imam, and all agreed on its obligation in general. And the Book (Quran) like His saying: 'Let there be from you a nation inviting to good, commanding good, and forbidding evil' [Al 'Imran 104], and the Sunna like his saying, peace be upon him: 'You must command good and forbid evil, or else Allah will set your worst over your best, and your best will supplicate and not be answered.' And as for the non-dependence of its permissibility on the deputization of the Imam, it is indicated by the fact that every single one of the Companions was engaged in commanding good and forbidding evil without deputization or permission from the Imam, and that was widespread among them, and there was no objection, so it was a consensus (ijma') on its permissibility (and its obligation).
Source pages p. 407

Commentary
This passage is an argument supporting the obligation of commanding good and forbidding evil without needing the Imam's permission. It begins by presenting the view of some Rawafid (a Shi'a group) who make it conditional on the Imam's appointment, like hudud punishments. Then it presents the views of others: Ahl al-Sunna say it is obligatory by divine law, while the Mu'tazilite al-Jubba'i and his son Abu Hashim say by reason. Al-Jubba'i says it is obligatory absolutely when the act is rationally good or bad, while Abu Hashim qualifies it with the condition of repelling harm. The author then provides the proof from consensus: all parties agree on its obligation in general, even if they disagree on the condition of the Imam. The Quran and hadith are cited as textual evidences. Finally, the proof that permissibility does not depend on the Imam is the practice of the Companions who did it without authorization, and the lack of objection from others constitutes consensus.

Key Terms
الروافض
الإمام
شرعاً
عقلاً

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Commanding good is only valid if the ruler gives permission.
Correction: The Rawafid hold this view, but the majority of scholars, including the Companions, held it obligatory regardless of permission.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which group holds that commanding good is not permissible without Imam's permission?
A) Ahl al-Sunna
B) Al-Jubba'i
C) Rawafid
D) Abu Hashim

Key Takeaway
The central dispute is not whether commanding good is obligatory, but under what conditions and on what basis—revealed law or reason.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Jubba'i said commanding good is obligatory by reason for every rationally good act, while Abu Hashim said it's only obligatory if it repels harm that cannot be repelled otherwise. Honestly, which scholar's view aligns more with how you actually live? Are you selective about when you command good based on expected outcomes, or do you feel a universal duty? What does that reveal about your faith?
?
The Rawafid require the Imam's permission to command good. In your life, do you wait for a leader or authority figure to give you permission before you speak out against wrongdoing? Where does that hesitation come from, and is it justified according to this lesson?
?
Ahl al-Sunna base the obligation on divine law, not reason alone. Do you ever rely on your own moral reasoning without checking revelation? How confident are you that your sense of right and wrong is aligned with Allah's commands? What would it take for you to submit your conscience to the Shariah even when it contradicts your rational preference?

Proofs for Obligation and Permission
Evidence for the obligation and permission of commanding good.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the proofs provided for the obligation of commanding good and for its permissibility without Imam's permission.

Core Idea
Evidence from consensus, Quran, hadith, and Companions' practice establishes the obligation.

After presenting the differing views, Al-Amidi now turns to the evidence. He argues that despite the disagreement, all parties agree that commanding good is obligatory in some form. Additionally, the Quran, hadith, and the unanimous practice of the Companions who acted without the Imam's permission confirm both the obligation and its independence from the Imam.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the second part of the source text which includes the proofs.
2
Identify the three proofs
Identify the consensus (all groups agree), the Quranic verse, and the hadith.
3
Identify the fourth proof
Identify the proof from the Companions' practice as consensus for permissibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الآمدي : ذهب بعض الروافض إلى أنه لا يجب بل لا يجوز الأمر بالمعروف والنهي عن المنكر إلا بنصب الإمام واستنابته كما في إقامة الحدود وذهب من عداهم إلى وجوبه مطلقاً، ثم اختلفوا فذهب أهل السنة إلى وجوبه شرعاً، والجبائي وابنه إلى وجوبه عقلاً ثم اختلفا فقال الجبائي : يجب مطلقاً فيما يدرك حسنه وقبحه عقلاً، وقال أبو هاشم : إن تضمن الأمر بالمعروف والنهي عن المنكر دفع ضرر عن الآمر والناهي ولا يندفع عنه إلا بذلك ،وجب، وإلا فلا والذي يدل على وجوبه عندنا الإجماع فإن القائل :قائلان قائل بوجوبه مطلقاً وقائل بوجوبه باستنابة الإمام فقد اتفق الكل على وجوبه في الجملة والكتاب كقوله تعالى : ﴿ ولتكن منكم أمة يدعون إلى الخير ويأمرون بالمعروف وينهون عن المنكر ﴾ [آل عمران : ١٠٤]، والسنة كقوله عليه السلام لتأمرون بالمعروف ولتنهن عن المنكر أو ليسلطن الله شراركم على خياركم فيدعو خياركم فلا يستجاب لهم. وأما عدم توقف جوازه على استنابة الإمام فيدل عليه أن كل واحد من آحاد الصحابة كان يشتغل بالأمر بالمعروف والنهي عن المنكر بلا استنابة وإذن من الإمام، وكان ذلك شائعاً ذائعاً فيما بينهم ولم يوجد نكير فكان إجماعاً على جوازه ( ولوجوبه )
Al-Amidi said: Some of the Rawafid held that commanding good and forbidding evil is not obligatory, rather not even permissible, except with the appointment and deputization of the Imam, like the execution of legal punishments. And those other than them held its obligation absolutely. Then they differed: the Ahl al-Sunna held its obligation by divine law (shar'an), while al-Jubba'i and his son held its obligation by reason ('aqlan). Then they differed: al-Jubba'i said it is obligatory absolutely regarding what is perceived as good and bad by reason, while Abu Hashim said: if commanding good and forbidding evil entails repelling harm from the commander and forbiddener, and that harm is not repelled except by that, then it is obligatory; otherwise not. And what indicates its obligation according to us is consensus (ijma'), for there are two groups: one holds it obligatory absolutely, and the other holds it obligatory with the deputization of the Imam, and all agreed on its obligation in general. And the Book (Quran) like His saying: 'Let there be from you a nation inviting to good, commanding good, and forbidding evil' [Al 'Imran 104], and the Sunna like his saying, peace be upon him: 'You must command good and forbid evil, or else Allah will set your worst over your best, and your best will supplicate and not be answered.' And as for the non-dependence of its permissibility on the deputization of the Imam, it is indicated by the fact that every single one of the Companions was engaged in commanding good and forbidding evil without deputization or permission from the Imam, and that was widespread among them, and there was no objection, so it was a consensus (ijma') on its permissibility (and its obligation).

Commentary
This passage is an argument supporting the obligation of commanding good and forbidding evil without needing the Imam's permission. It begins by presenting the view of some Rawafid (a Shi'a group) who make it conditional on the Imam's appointment, like hudud punishments. Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The obligation of commanding good depends on the Imam's permission because the Rawafid say so.
Correction: The consensus and practice of the Companions show it is obligatory without permission.

What is the main proof given for the permissibility of commanding good without Imam's permission?
A) Quranic verse

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you witness wrongdoing in your family or community, do you speak up, or do you remain silent out of fear or comfort? Reflect on your excuses in light of the hadith warning that neglect will cause Allah to send the worst over the best—and your supplication may go unanswered.
?
The Companions acted without waiting for anyone's permission. What is stopping you from commanding good right now in your sphere of influence? Identify one specific situation today where you will actively correct a wrong or encourage a good, and commit to doing it.
?
If you believe that commanding good is only for scholars or leaders, how has that belief allowed you to avoid responsibility? How would your life change if you accepted that every believer is obligated to enjoin good and forbid evil, as proven by the consensus and the Companions' example?

The Hadith on the Seventy-Three Sects and Its Miraculous Nature
Hadith of the 73 sects and the initial unity of the Companions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Prophet's prediction of the 73 sects was a miracle fulfilled precisely as foretold, and that the early Muslim community was initially united in creed.

Core Idea
The Prophet's foretelling of the sects is a miracle confirmed by history.

This lesson begins with a famous hadith in which the Prophet, peace be upon him, informed his ummah that it would split into 73 sects, with only one saved. This prediction itself is considered one of his miracles because it came to pass exactly as he said. Al-Amidi then notes that at the time of the Prophet's death, the Muslims were united in belief and practice, except for hypocrites.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and its context
Read the Arabic passage that cites the hadith and the statement that it is a miracle. Notice the wording of the hadith and the claim of miraculous fulfillment.
The hadith is a key text in sectarian discussions.
2
Understand the miracle claim
Reflect on why the later division of the ummah is considered a miracle—it confirms the Prophet's truthfulness.
3
Note the initial unity
Al-Amidi mentions that at the Prophet's death, Muslims were upon one creed except for hypocrites. This sets the stage for later disputes.
The unity was on fundamental beliefs, not on every detail.

تذييل للكتاب في ذكر الفرق التي أشار إليها الرسول الله بقوله : «ستفترق أمتي ثلاثاً وسبعين فرقة كلها في النار إلا واحدة وهي ما أنا عليه وأصحابي» وكان ذلك معجزاته حيث وقع ما أخبر به قال الآمدي كان المسلمون عند وفاة النبي عليه السلام على عقيدة واحدة وطريقة واحدة إلا من كان يبطن النفاق ويظهر الوفاق، ثم نشأ الخلاف فيما بينهم أولاً في أمور اجتهادية لا توجب إيماناً ولا كفراً، وكان غرضهم منها إقامة مراسم الدين وإدامة مناهج الشرع القويم وذلك كاختلافهم عند قول النبي في مرض موته : ائتوني بقرطاس أكتب لكم كتابا لا تضلوا بعدي» حتى قال عمر: إن النبي قد غيبه الوجع حسبنا كتاب الله وكثر اللغط في ذلك حتى النبي : قوموا عني لا ينبغي عندي التنازع وكاختلافهم بعد ذلك في جيش أسامة فقال قوم: بوجوب الاتباع لقوله عليه السلام : جهزوا جيش أسامة، لعن من تخلف عنه وقال : قوم بالتخلف انتظاراً لما يكون من رسول الله في مرضه، وكاختلافهم بعد ذلك في موته حتى قال عمر: من قال : إن محمداً قد مات علوته بسيفي وإنما رفع إلى السماء كما رفع عيسى بن مريم. وقال أبو بكر: من كان يعبد محمداً فإن محمداً قد مات ومن كان يعبد إله محمد فإنه حي لا يموت، وتلا قوله تعالى: ﴿وما محمد إلا رسول قد خلت من قبله الرسل ﴾ [آل عمران : ١٤٤] الآية فرجع عن قوله
Appendix to the book mentioning the sects that the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, pointed to with his saying: 'My ummah will split into seventy-three sects, all in the Fire except one, which is what I and my Companions are upon.' And that was one of his miracles, since what he informed came to pass. Al-Amidi said: The Muslims at the time of the Prophet's death, peace be upon him, were upon one creed and one path, except for those who concealed hypocrisy and displayed agreement. Then disagreement arose among them initially in ijtihadi matters that do not entail faith or disbelief. Their purpose in them was to establish the rites of religion and perpetuate the paths of the straight law. Such as their disagreement when the Prophet said during his fatal illness: 'Bring me a sheet of paper, I will write for you a book after which you will not go astray,' until 'Umar said: 'The pain has overcome the Prophet; the Book of Allah is sufficient for us.' And there was much clamor until the Prophet said: 'Get up from me; conflict is not appropriate before me.' And their disagreement after that concerning the army of Usama: some said it is obligatory to obey his saying, peace be upon him: 'Prepare the army of Usama; curse be upon the one who stays behind,' and some said they should stay behind awaiting what would happen to the Messenger of Allah during his illness. And their disagreement after that concerning his death, until 'Umar said: 'Whoever says that Muhammad has died, I will strike him with my sword; he has only been raised to the heavens just as 'Isa ibn Maryam was raised.' And Abu Bakr said: 'Whoever used to worship Muhammad, then Muhammad has died; and whoever used to worship the God of Muhammad, then He is Living and does not die.' And he recited the verse: 'And Muhammad is no more than a messenger; messengers have passed away before him' [Al 'Imran 144] until he returned from his statement.
Source pages p. 408

Commentary
This passage is an appendix discussing the hadith of the 73 sects. It notes that this hadith is a miracle because the division actually occurred. Then it quotes al-Amidi stating that at the Prophet's death, Muslims were united except for hypocrites. The first disagreements were over ijtihadi matters (matters of legal reasoning) that do not affect faith or disbelief. Their intention was to uphold the religion. The passage then gives three examples: (1) the incident of the pen and paper where the Prophet wanted to write a document, but some disagreed due to his illness; (2) the dispute over sending Usama's army while the Prophet was ill; (3) the dispute over the Prophet's death, where 'Umar initially believed he had not died, and Abu Bakr corrected him with the Quranic verse about messengers dying. These examples show that even the Companions had differences, but they were over secondary matters, not fundamentals.

Key Terms
افتراق الأمة
معجزة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) My ummah will split into 72 sects, all saved except one
B) My ummah will split into 73 sects, all in the Fire except one
C) My ummah will split into 73 sects, all saved
D) My ummah will not split

Key Takeaway
The hadith of the 73 sects is a miraculous prediction that was fulfilled.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the Prophet's prophecy about division was a miracle that came true, does that not demand that you take his warnings about the saved sect seriously? Are you actively seeking to ensure you follow exactly what he and his Companions were upon? What specific step will you take this week to verify your path?
?
Al-Amidi notes that at the Prophet's death the Muslims were united in creed and path. How does your own involvement with the Muslim community reflect that unity—or contribute to division? What can you personally do to reduce sectarian tensions among Muslims you know?
?
The hypocrites at the time concealed their disbelief while appearing united. Ask yourself: Are you hiding any beliefs or practices that contradict the way of the Prophet and his Companions? Are you willing to bring them into the light and align yourself fully with the saved sect?

The Nature of Early Disputes Among the Companions
General principle of ijtihadi disputes and the pen-and-paper incident.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the early disagreements among the Companions were over ijtihadi matters that did not affect faith or disbelief, and their purpose was to uphold the religion.

Core Idea
Companion disagreements were over legal reasoning, not core beliefs.

This lesson examines the nature of the first differences that arose among the Companions after the Prophet's death. Al-Amidi clarifies that these were not theological disputes but ijtihadi matters, meaning they were based on independent reasoning and did not involve faith or disbelief. The Companions' intention was always to preserve the practices of Islam. The first example given is the incident of the pen and paper.

Guided Path
1
Read the general principle
Read the statement that disagreements were in ijtihadi matters not entailing faith or disbelief. Understand the terms 'ijtihadi' and their purpose.
Ijtihad means independent legal reasoning.
2
Examine the first example
Read the incident of the pen and paper. Notice the different opinions and how the Prophet resolved it.
This shows disagreement even among the most knowledgeable.
3
Reflect on the implications
Consider that such disagreements are natural and do not indicate a split in faith.

?

?

?
The Prophet stopped the clamor and said 'Get up from me; conflict is not appropriate before me.' How often do you persist in arguments even when they lead to division? What would it take for you to walk away from a dispute for the sake of unity, trusting that Allah's book is sufficient?

Further Examples: Usama's Army and the Death of the Prophet
Disputes over Usama's army and the Prophet's death.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand two more examples of ijtihadi disagreements among the Companions: the dispute over sending Usama's army and the initial confusion over the Prophet's death, and how Abu Bakr resolved it with the Quran.

Core Idea
Even in confusion, the Companions upheld the religion through reasoning and revelation.

This lesson continues with two more examples from the early disagreements. The first was about whether to dispatch Usama's army while the Prophet was ill. Some said it was obligatory, citing the Prophet's command; others said to wait. The second and more dramatic was the confusion over the Prophet's death, where Umar denied it at first, but Abu Bakr recited a Quranic verse, bringing unity.

Guided Path
1
Read the dispute over Usama's army
Read the passage about the disagreement on sending the army. Note both sides argued based on the Prophet's words.
This shows how ijtihad could lead to different conclusions even with clear prophetic commands.
2
Read the dispute over the Prophet's death
Read Umar's initial reaction and Abu Bakr's response. Understand how Abu Bakr used the Quran to correct the situation.
Umar's denial was due to shock, not disbelief.
3
Connect to the lesson's theme
Reflect that these examples further illustrate ijtihadi disagreements that did not break the unity of faith.

Sects and Disagreements

Objection to the hadith on 73 sects and al-Razi's response
Records an objection to the hadith's number of sects and al-Razi's response.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Razi defended the hadith of the 73 sects against the objection that the number is inaccurate by interpreting it as referring to a specific time.

Core Idea
The hadith's number 73 refers to a specific moment, not a fixed count for all time.

When critics argued that the number 73 in the hadith about sect division does not match reality—either too many or too few—Imam al-Razi offered a refined interpretation. He pointed out that the hadith speaks of a particular situation (في حال ما), meaning the number can vary. This lesson examines the objection and al-Razi's insightful response.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and response
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Note the structure: an objection followed by an answer.
Pay attention to the two possibilities the objector presents.
2
Analyze the objection
The objector says if '73 sects' means roots of religions, the count is too high; if it means branches, the count is too low. Understand this dual critique.
3
Understand al-Razi's answer
Al-Razi argues the hadith refers to a specific time (في حال ما), so the number 73 is not a fixed total for all times. This resolves the objection.
Think about how this interpretation defends the hadith's authenticity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (بقوله : ستفترق إلخ ) طعن بعضهم في صحة هذا الخبر فقال : إن أراد باثنين وسبعين فرقة أصول الأديان فلن يبلغ هذا العدد وإن أراد الفروع فإنها تتجاوز هذا العدد إلى أضعاف ذلك. أجاب الإمام الرازي بأن المراد ستفترق أمتي في حال ما وليس فيه دلالة على أن افتراقها في سائر الأحوال لا يجوز أن يزيد وينقص.
His saying: ('By his saying: "they will split, etc.") Some criticized the authenticity of this report and said: If he meant by seventy-three sects the roots of religions, then this number would not be reached; and if he meant the branches, then it exceeds this number to many times that. Imam al-Razi answered: The meaning is 'my ummah will split in a particular situation' and there is no indication in it that its splitting in other situations cannot increase or decrease.
Source pages p. 408

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer regarding the hadith of the 73 sects. The objector argues that the number 73 does not correspond to reality: if it refers to fundamental religious sects, there are fewer; if it refers to branches (furu'), there are many more. So the hadith seems inaccurate. Al-Razi responds by interpreting the hadith as referring to a specific point in time (a particular situation), not a fixed number for all time. The number can vary over time. Thus, the hadith is not claiming that exactly 73 sects exist forever; it is a prediction of a particular historical moment.

Key Terms
أصول الأديان
فروع
تفترق في حال ما

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The hadith predicts exactly 73 sects will exist for all time.
Correction: Imam al-Razi explained that the hadith refers to a particular situation, so the number can vary over time.

Checkpoint
How did Imam al-Razi respond to the objection that the number 73 does not match the actual number of sects?
A) He said it is metaphorical
B) He said the hadith refers to a specific time, not all time
C) He reinterpreted the wording
D) He rejected the hadith

Key Takeaway
Al-Razi clarifies that the hadith's number 73 applies to a specific time, not as a permanent fixed count.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a hadith that seems to conflict with reality, do you quickly dismiss it or, like al-Razi, seek an interpretation that preserves its truth? Think of a specific example from your own life where you might have rejected a religious teaching because it didn't fit your limited view.
?
The critic assumed the number 73 had to match his own observation. Where in your life do you impose your limited perspective on Allah's words, demanding they conform to your expectations? What would it take for you to trust that His wisdom is greater than your understanding?
?
Al-Razi's answer shows that a truth can be specific to a context without being universal. Is there a verse or hadith you have been applying too rigidly or too loosely? Commit to studying its context before making it a rule for yourself or others.

Early Disagreements and the Eight Major Sects
Describes early Muslim disagreements and lists the eight major sects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the historical process that led to the emergence of the 73 sects and the identity of the eight major Islamic sects.

Core Idea
Disagreements grew over time, crystallizing into 73 sects, of which eight are major.

This passage takes us through the early historical disagreements among the Companions after the Prophet's death—from burial place to legal rulings—showing how differences gradually escalated until sects formed. It then identifies the eight major sects that the author will discuss in subsequent chapters.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once through, then the English translation. Notice how the author describes a sequence of disagreements that escalate over time.
Pay attention to the names and events mentioned.
2
Identify the two main parts
The passage has a clear break: first, a historical narrative of disagreements; second, a list of the eight major sects. Mark where the transition occurs.
Look for 'وإذا عرفت هذا فنقول'.
3
Trace the escalation of disagreement
List the key disagreements mentioned in order: burial place, imamate, zakat, caliphate appointments, battles, legal rulings, and finally the emergence of figures like Ma'bad al-Juhani on qadar.
This shows how small differences grew into major sectarian divisions.
4
Memorize the eight major sects
The passage lists eight sects. Write them down in Arabic and English. They are: المعتزلة (Mu'tazila), الشيعة (Shia), الخوارج (Khawarij), المرجئة (Murji'a), الجبرية (Jabriyya), النجارية (Najjariyya), المشبهة (Mushabbiha), and الناجية (al-Najiya, the saved sect).
Note that الناجية is not a separate group but refers to Ahl al-Sunnah.

Conclusion of the Fourth Observation. They prevented me? The group up to his saying: And Umar said: 'As if I had not heard this verse until now.' And their disagreement after that about the place of his burial, whether in Mecca, Medina, or Jerusalem, until they heard what was narrated from him: 'That prophets are buried where they die.' And their disagreement about the Imamate and the affirmation of inheritance from the Prophet, and about fighting those who withheld Zakat, until Umar said: 'How can we fight them? The Prophet, peace be upon him, said: I have been commanded to fight people until they say 'There is no god but Allah'; when they say it, they protect from me their blood and their wealth.' Abu Bakr said to him: 'Did he not say: except by its right? And among its rights are the establishment of prayer and the payment of Zakat. By God, if they withhold a rope's end they used to give to the Prophet, I would fight them for it.' Then their disagreement after that about appointing Abu Bakr over Umar for the Caliphate, then about the matter of the Shura until the matter was settled on Uthman, then their disagreement about his killing and about the Caliphate of Ali and Muawiya and what happened in the Battle of the Camel and Siffin. Then their disagreement also about some subsidiary rulings, like their disagreement about al-Kalala, the inheritance of the grandfather from the brothers, the blood money for fingers, and the blood money for teeth, and other such rulings. And disagreement kept increasing and escalating little by little until the last days of the Companions, until Ma'bad al-Juhani, Ghaylan al-Dimashqi, and Yunus al-Iswari appeared, and they disagreed about al-Qadar and attributing all things to Allah's decree. And disagreement kept branching out and opinions diverging until the people of Islam and the holders of views split into seventy-three sects. And if you know this, we say: Know that the major Islamic sects are eight: the Mu'tazila, the Shia, the Khawarij, the Murji'a, the Jabriyya, the Najjariyya, the Mushabbiha, and al-Najiya (the saved sect).
Source pages p. 409

Commentary
This passage is a historical survey. It begins by recalling a narration about Umar's statement upon hearing a verse, then recounts various disagreements among the Companions after the Prophet's death: about his burial place, about the imamate and inheritance, about fighting those who withheld zakat, about the appointment of Abu Bakr, the shura, the killing of Uthman, the battles of Jamal and Siffin, and later about subsidiary legal rulings. The disagreement gradually increased, eventually leading to the appearance of Ma'bad al-Juhani, Ghaylan al-Dimashqi, and Yunus al-Iswari, who raised issues about al-Qadar (divine decree). This branching of opinions resulted in the famous division of the Muslim community into 73 sects. The author then states that the major (kubār) of these sects are eight: the Mu'tazila, the Shia, the Khawarij, the Murji'a, the Jabriyya, the Najjariyya, the Mushabbiha, and al-Najiya (which refers to the saved sect, i.e., Ahl al-Sunnah). The passage sets the stage for the subsequent detailed discussion of these sects.

Key Terms
القدر (al-Qadar)
الفرق الإسلامية (Islamic sects)
المعتزلة (Mu'tazila)
الشيعة (Shia)
الخوارج (Khawarij)
المرجئة (Murji'a)
الجبرية (Jabriyya)
النجارية (Najjariyya)
المشبهة (Mushabbiha)
الناجية (al-Najiya)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The eight sects listed are all the 73 sects.
Correction: The author lists the eight major sects; the full 73 include many subgroups and offshoots of these eight.

Key Takeaway
The eight major Islamic sects are the Mu'tazila, Shia, Khawarij, Murji'a, Jabriyya, Najjariyya, Mushabbiha, and al-Najiya (the saved sect).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read about the Companions differing even on where to bury the Prophet, do you feel a pang of doubt about the infallibility of the early community? How does the lesson's reminder that the Prophet foretold 73 sects strengthen your commitment to seeking the saved sect rather than following your own preference?
?
Think of a contemporary intra-Muslim conflict you've witnessed. Which of the early disagreements listed (burial, zakat, leadership, or fiqh) does it resemble most? Knowing that these disputes occurred among the Sahaba, what steps will you take to lower your anger and listen to those you disagree with?
?
The passage ends by naming eight sects, including 'al-Najiya'. If you were to be completely honest, which of these eight do you find yourself instinctively sympathizing with—by upbringing, environment, or desire? Are you willing to study the saved sect's doctrine even if it challenges your current leanings?

The Origin of the Mu'tazila: Wāṣil's Separation
Narrates the story of Wāṣil's separation from al-Hasan al-Basri.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the historical circumstances that led to the formation of the Mu'tazila and the meaning of their name.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazila began when Wāṣil bin 'Aṭā' separated from al-Hasan al-Basri's circle.

This lesson introduces the founding moment of the Mu'tazila. A visitor's question about the status of a major sinner triggered a division. Wāṣil's response, given before his teacher could answer, led al-Hasan to declare that Wāṣil had 'separated' from them, giving the sect its name. Understanding this origin story clarifies the core issue that defined early Kalām: the fate of the grave sinner.

Guided Path
1
Read the origin story
Read the Arabic passage from 'الفرق الأولى المعتزلة' to 'قد اعتزل عنا واصل' carefully. Note the setting: a man asks al-Hasan al-Basri about the Khawarij and Murji'a positions.
The question reveals the two extremes that Wāṣil will reject.
2
Identify the key figures
Identify al-Hasan al-Basri, Wāṣil bin 'Aṭā', and the two groups mentioned: the Wa'īdiyya (Khawarij) and the Murji'a.
The Khawarij excommunicated sinners; the Murji'a postponed judgment.
3
Understand why al-Hasan said 'he separated'
Notice the timing: al-Hasan was reflecting, but Wāṣil spoke first. The phrase 'قد اعتزل عنا واصل' is the direct reason for the name 'Mu'tazila'.
The name is derived from the verb 'i'tazala' (to separate).
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider how this event set the Mu'tazila apart: they took a middle position between Khawarij and Murji'a. This is the first step toward understanding their theological identity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفرق الأولى المعتزلة أصحاب واصل بن عطاء العزال اعتزل عن مجلس الحسن البصري وذلك أنه دخل على الحسن رجل فقال : يا إمام الدين ظهر في زماننا جماعة يكفرون صاحب الكبيرة يعني وعيدية الخوارج وجماعة أخرى يرجئون الكبائر يقولون : لا تضر مع الإيمان معصية كما لا تنفع مع الكفر طاعة، فكيف تحكم لنا أن نعتقد في ذلك؟ فتفكر الحسن وقبل أن يجيب قال واصل: أنا لا أقول : إن صاحب الكبيرة مؤمن مطلق ولا كافر مطلق ثم قام إلى إسطوانة من أسطوانات المسجد ) وأخذ يقرر ) على جماعة من أصحاب الحسن ما أجاب به من ( أن مرتكب الكبيرة ليس بمؤمن ولا كافر ويثبت له المنزلة بين المنزلتين ) قائلاً المؤمن اسم مدح والفاسق لا يستحق المدح فلا يكون مؤمناً، وليس بكافر أيضاً لإقراره بالشهادتين ولو وجد سائر أعمال الخير فيه فإذا مات بلا توبة خلد في النار إذ ليس في الآخرة إلا فريقان فريق في الجنة وفريق في السعير، لكن يخفض عليه ويكون در کته فوق دركات الكفار ) فقال الحسن : قد اعتزل عنا واصل) فلذلك وأصحابه معتزلة ) ويلقبون بالقدرية لإسنادهم أفعال العباد إلى قدرتهم وإنكارهم القدر فيها ( وإنهم قالوا: إن من يقول بالقدر خيره وشره من الله أولى باسم القدرية) منا وذلك لأن مثبت القدر أحق بأن ينسب إليه من نافيه . فنقول : كما يصح نسبة مثبته إليه يصح نسبة النافي أيضا إذا بالغ في نفيه لأنه ملتبس به (و) لا يمكن حمل القدرية على المثبتين له لأنه ( يرده قوله عليه السلام القدرية مجوس هذه الأمة») فإنه يقتضي مشاركتهم للمجوس فيما اشتهروا به من إثبات خالقين لا في قولهم بأن الله خلق شيئاً، ثم أنكره والنافون له هم المشاركون لهم في تلك الصفة المشهورة حيث يجعلون العبد خالقاً لأفعاله وينسبون القبائح والشرور إليه دون الله سبحانه ( و ) يرده أيضاً ( قوله عليه السلام) في حق القدرية : ((هم خصماء الله في القدر )) ولا خصومة للقائل بتفويض الأمور كلها إليه تعالى إنما الخصومة لمن يعتقد أنه يقدر على ما لا يريد الله بل يكرهه . (و) المعتزلة لقبوا أنفسهم بأصحاب العدل والتوحيد وذلك ( لقولهم بوجوب الأصلح ونفي الصفات القديمة ) يعني : أنهم قالوا : قوله : ( وإنكارهم القدرة فيها دفع لما يرد على كلام المصنف من أن المناسب على ما ذكره هو القدرة بضم القاف، فأشار الشارح إلى أن إسناد أفعال العباد إلى قدرتهم يتضمن نفي القدرة فيها، فالتسمية باعتبار هذا المتضمن وليكن هذا آخر ما أردنا إيراده في حواشي المواقف فنسأل الله تعالى أن يجعله خالصاً لوجهه الكريم. إنه هو البر الرحيم وأن ينفع به المخلصين. ويجعله ذخراً ليوم الدين والحمد لله رب العالمين والصلاة والصلام على محمد وآله أجمعين . • تمت الحاشية تأليف العالم العلامة والبحر الفهامة الشيخ حسن جلبي تغمده برحمته آمين .
The first sect: the Mu'tazila, the followers of Wāṣil bin 'Atā' al-Ghazzāl. He separated from the circle of al-Hasan al-Basri. That was because a man entered upon al-Hasan and said: 'O Imam of the religion, in our time there has appeared a group that declares the committer of a major sin an unbeliever, meaning the Wa'īdiyya of the Khawarij, and another group that postpones (judgment on) major sins, saying: Disobedience does not harm with faith just as obedience does not benefit with disbelief. So what do you command us to believe regarding this?' So al-Hasan reflected, and before he could answer, Wāṣil said: 'I do not say that the committer of a major sin is absolutely a believer nor absolutely an unbeliever.' Then he stood by one of the pillars of the mosque and began to explain to a group of al-Hasan's companions his answer: that the committer of a major sin is neither a believer nor an unbeliever, and he affirms for him the intermediate position (al-manzila bayna al-manzilatayn), saying: 'Believer is a term of praise, and the sinner does not deserve praise, so he is not a believer. And he is not an unbeliever because of his affirmation of the two testimonies, even if he lacks other good deeds. If he dies without repentance, he will be in Hell forever, since in the Hereafter there are only two groups: a group in Paradise and a group in the Blaze. But his punishment will be lighter, and his level will be above the levels of the unbelievers.' So al-Hasan said: 'Wāṣil has separated from us.' Therefore, he and his followers are called Mu'tazila. And they are also called Qadariyya because they attribute the actions of servants to their own power (qudra) and deny divine decree (qadar) concerning them. They said: 'One who affirms qadar, its good and evil from Allah, is more deserving of the name Qadariyya than us, because the affirmer of qadar is more entitled to be named after it than its denier.' We say: Just as it is possible to attribute (the name) to its affirmer, it is also possible to attribute it to its denier if he goes to excess in denying it, because he is involved with it. And it is not possible to apply Qadariyya to the affirmers, because the saying of the Prophet, peace be upon him, 'The Qadariyya are the Magians of this Ummah' refutes it. For it necessitates their sharing with the Magians in what they are famous for, namely affirming two creators, not in their saying that Allah created something and then denied it. The deniers are the ones who share with them in that famous attribute, as they make the servant the creator of his actions and attribute ugly things and evils to him instead of Allah, exalted be He. It is also refuted by his saying, peace be upon him, regarding the Qadariyya: 'They are the adversaries of Allah concerning al-Qadar.' There is no adversary for the one who delegates all affairs to Him, exalted be He. Rather, the adversary is the one who believes that he has power over what Allah does not will, but rather detests. And the Mu'tazila called themselves the People of Justice and Unity (Ahl al-ʿAdl wa al-Tawḥīd) because of their saying concerning the necessity of that which is most beneficial (wujūb al-aṣlaḥ) and the negation of the eternal attributes ṣifāt al-qadīma). Meaning: they said... His saying: 'And their denial of the power (qudra) in it' is a rebuttal to what might be said against the author's words, that the appropriate term based on what he mentioned is qudra (with a ḍamma on the qāf). So the commentator indicates that attributing the actions of servants to their power (qudra) entails the denial of qadar in them, so the naming is by virtue of this entailment. And let this be the last of what we intended to include in the Hashiyat al-Mawaqif. We ask Allah Almighty to make it purely for His noble face. Indeed, He is the Beneficent, the Merciful, and to benefit the sincere with it, and to make it a treasure for the Day of Judgment. Praise be to Allah, Lord of the worlds, and blessings and peace be upon Muhammad and all his family. The hashya is completed, authored by the great scholar, the sea of understanding, Sheikh Hasan Jalbī, may Allah envelop him in His mercy. Amen.
Source pages p. 409

Commentary
This passage narrates the origin of the Mu'tazila and outlines their key doctrines. It begins by identifying Wāṣil bin 'Aṭā' al-Ghazzāl as the founder, who left al-Hasan al-Basri's circle. The immediate cause was a man's question about the ruling on the committer of a major sin: the Khawarij were excommunicating them (takfīr), while the Murji'a were saying no harm comes from sin with faith. Al-Hasan was about to answer, but Wāṣil interjected with his famous doctrine: 'the intermediate position' (al-manzila bayna al-manzilatayn). He argued that a major sinner is neither a believer (since believer is a term of praise and the sinner does not deserve it) nor an unbeliever (because he still professes the shahāda). He will be in Hell if he dies without repentance, but his punishment will be lighter than that of unbelievers. Thereupon al-Hasan said 'Wāṣil has separated from us,' hence the name Mu'tazila. They were also called Qadariyya because they attribute human actions to their own power (qudra) and deny divine predetermination (qadar) in such actions. The passage then discusses the appropriateness of this name: some argued that the affirmers of qadar are more deserving of the name, but the author responds with two prophetic hadiths. The first, 'The Qadariyya are the Magians of this Ummah,' indicates that deniers of qadar resemble Magians by positing two creators (the servant creates his own actions). The second, 'They are the adversaries of Allah concerning al-Qadar,' only applies to those who claim they can do what Allah does not will—thus, deniers of qadar are the real adversaries, not the affirmers. The Mu'tazila themselves preferred the title 'People of Justice and Unity' (Ahl al-ʿAdl wa al-Tawḥīd) because they asserted the necessity of al-aṣlaḥ (what is best for creation) and denied eternal attributes. The commentator adds a linguistic note: the name Qadariyya is derived from qudra (power) rather than qadar, since their error lies in claiming power independent of Allah's decree. The passage concludes with a standard colophon ending the book.

Key Terms
المعتزلة (Mu'tazila)
المنزلة بين المنزلتين (al-manzila bayna al-manzilatayn)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila originated from Wāṣil's separation over the issue of the grave sinner, adopting an intermediate position between the Khawarij and Murji'a.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you fall into sin, does your heart lean more toward the Khawarij's despair (I am a disbeliever) or the Murji'a's complacency (it doesn't matter)? Wāṣil's answer forces you to neither minimize sin nor lose hope. Which tendency do you need to fight today, and what concrete step will you take to correct it?
?
Al-Hasan al-Basri paused to think before answering. Wāṣil rushed in with his own answer. When you face a question about your own sins, do you pause to seek guidance or do you rush to a comfortable conclusion? Commit today to a specific practice of pausing before speaking about matters of sin and repentance.
?
Wāṣil did not sugarcoat the outcome: the unrepentant grave sinner will be in Hell forever, though with lighter punishment. Does this truth truly move you to fear for yourself and to warn those you love? Write down one person you know who is persisting in a major sin, and decide right now how you will lovingly speak the truth to them this week.

The Intermediate Position: Al-Manẓila bayn al-Manẓilatayn
Explains Wāṣil's doctrine of the intermediate position.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazili doctrine of the intermediate position and its rationale.

Core Idea
A major sinner is neither a believer nor an unbeliever, but in an intermediate state.

Wāṣil's answer to the visitor's question introduced a novel classification: the committer of a major sin is not a believer (because believer is praise) and not an unbeliever (because he professes faith), but occupies a middle category. This doctrine became a hallmark of the Mu'tazila. Let's examine its reasoning and implications as presented in the text.

Guided Path
1
Read the core statement
Focus on Wāṣil's words: 'أنا لا أقول : إن صاحب الكبيرة مؤمن مطلق ولا كافر مطلق' and the explanation that follows.
Note the absolute negation of the two labels.
2
Analyze the reasoning
Wāṣil gives two reasons: 1) 'Believer' is praise, and a sinner does not deserve it. 2) He is not an unbeliever because he affirms the shahada even if lacking other good deeds.
This logical deduction is based on the meanings of the terms.
3
Understand the eschatological consequence
If he dies without repentance, he will be in Hell forever, but with lighter punishment. The text states: 'يخفض عليه ويكون دركته فوق دركات الكفار'.
This is distinct from the Khawarij (eternal damnation same as disbelievers) and Murji'a (no harm from sin).

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفرق الأولى المعتزلة أصحاب واصل بن عطاء العزال اعتزل عن مجلس الحسن البصري وذلك أنه دخل على الحسن رجل فقال : يا إمام الدين ظهر في زماننا جماعة يكفرون صاحب الكبيرة يعني وعيدية الخوارج وجماعة أخرى يرجئون الكبائر يقولون : لا تضر مع الإيمان معصية كما لا تنفع مع الكفر طاعة، فكيف تحكم لنا أن نعتقد في ذلك؟ فتفكر الحسن وقبل أن يجيب قال واصل: أنا لا أقول : إن صاحب الكبيرة مؤمن مطلق ولا كافر مطلق ثم قام إلى إسطوانة من أسطوانات المسجد ) وأخذ يقرر ) على جماعة من أصحاب الحسن ما أجاب به من ( أن مرتكب الكبيرة ليس بمؤمن ولا كافر ويثبت له المنزلة بين المنزلتين ) قائلاً المؤمن اسم مدح والفاسق لا يستحق المدح فلا يكون مؤمناً، وليس بكافر أيضاً لإقراره بالشهادتين ولو وجد سائر أعمال الخير فيه فإذا مات بلا توبة خلد في النار إذ ليس في الآخرة إلا فريقان فريق في الجنة وفريق في السعير، لكن يخفض عليه ويكون در کته فوق دركات الكفار ) فقال الحسن : قد اعتزل عنا واصل) فلذلك وأصحابه معتزلة ) ويلقبون بالقدرية لإسنادهم أفعال العباد إلى قدرتهم وإنكارهم القدر فيها ( وإنهم قالوا: إن من يقول بالقدر خيره وشره من الله أولى باسم القدرية) منا وذلك لأن مثبت القدر أحق بأن ينسب إليه من نافيه . فنقول : كما يصح نسبة مثبته إليه يصح نسبة النافي أيضا إذا بالغ في نفيه لأنه ملتبس به (و) لا يمكن حمل القدرية على المثبتين له لأنه ( يرده قوله عليه السلام القدرية مجوس هذه الأمة») فإنه يقتضي مشاركتهم للمجوس فيما اشتهروا به من إثبات خالقين لا في قولهم بأن الله خلق شيئاً، ثم أنكره والنافون له هم المشاركون لهم في تلك الصفة المشهورة حيث يجعلون العبد خالقاً لأفعاله وينسبون القبائح والشرور إليه دون الله سبحانه ( و ) يرده أيضاً ( قوله عليه السلام) في حق القدرية : ((هم خصماء الله في القدر )) ولا خصومة للقائل بتفويض الأمور كلها إليه تعالى إنما الخصومة لمن يعتقد أنه يقدر على ما لا يريد الله بل يكرهه . (و) المعتزلة لقبوا أنفسهم بأصحاب العدل والتوحيد وذلك ( لقولهم بوجوب الأصلح ونفي الصفات القديمة ) يعني : أنهم قالوا : قوله : ( وإنكارهم القدرة فيها دفع لما يرد على كلام المصنف من أن المناسب على ما ذكره هو القدرة بضم القاف، فأشار الشارح إلى أن إسناد أفعال العباد إلى قدرتهم يتضمن نفي القدرة فيها، فالتسمية باعتبار هذا المتضمن وليكن هذا آخر ما أردنا إيراده في حواشي المواقف فنسأل الله تعالى أن يجعله خالصاً لوجهه الكريم. إنه هو البر الرحيم وأن ينفع به المخلصين. ويجعله ذخراً ليوم الدين والحمد لله رب العالمين والصلاة والصلام على محمد وآله أجمعين . • تمت الحاشية تأليف العالم العلامة والبحر الفهامة الشيخ حسن جلبي تغمده برحمته آمين .
The first sect: the Mu'tazila, the followers of Wāṣil bin 'Atā' al-Ghazzāl. He separated from the circle of al-Hasan al-Basri. That was because a man entered upon al-Hasan and said: 'O Imam of the religion, in our time there has appeared a group that declares the committer of a major sin an unbeliever, meaning the Wa'īdiyya of the Khawarij, and another group that postpones (judgment on) major sins, saying: Disobedience does not harm with faith just as obedience does not benefit with disbelief. So what do you command us to believe regarding this?' So al-Hasan reflected, and before he could answer, Wāṣil said: 'I do not say that the committer of a major sin is absolutely a believer nor absolutely an unbeliever.' Then he stood by one of the pillars of the mosque and began to explain to a group of al-Hasan's companions his answer: that the committer of a major sin is neither a believer nor an unbeliever, and he affirms for him the intermediate position (al-manzila bayna al-manzilatayn), saying: 'Believer is a term of praise, and the sinner does not deserve praise, so he is not a believer. And he is not an unbeliever because of his affirmation of the two testimonies, even if he lacks other good deeds. If he dies without repentance, he will be in Hell forever, since in the Hereafter there are only two groups: a group in Paradise and a group in the Blaze. But his punishment will be lighter, and his level will be above the levels of the unbelievers.' So al-Hasan said: 'Wāṣil has separated from us.' Therefore, he and his followers are called Mu'tazila. And they are also called Qadariyya because they attribute the actions of servants to their own power (qudra) and deny divine decree (qadar) concerning them. They said: 'One who affirms qadar, its good and evil from Allah, is more deserving of the name Qadariyya than us, because the affirmer of qadar is more entitled to be named after it than its denier.' We say: Just as it is possible to attribute (the name) to its affirmer, it is also possible to attribute it to its denier if he goes to excess in denying it, because he is involved with it. And it is not possible to apply Qadariyya to the affirmers, because the saying of the Prophet, peace be upon him, 'The Qadariyya are the Magians of this Ummah' refutes it. For it necessitates their sharing with the Magians in what they are famous for, namely affirming two creators, not in their saying that Allah created something and then denied it. The deniers are the ones who share with them in that famous attribute, as they make the servant the creator of his actions and attribute ugly things and evils to him instead of Allah, exalted be He. It is also refuted by his saying, peace be upon him, regarding the Qadariyya: 'They are the adversaries of Allah concerning al-Qadar.' There is no adversary for the one who delegates all affairs to Him, exalted be He. Rather, the adversary is the one who believes that he has power over what Allah does not will, but rather detests. And the Mu'tazila called themselves the People of Justice and Unity (Ahl al-ʿAdl wa al-Tawḥīd) because of their saying concerning the necessity of that which is most beneficial (wujūb al-aṣlaḥ) and the negation of the eternal attributes ṣifāt al-qadīma). Meaning: they said... His saying: 'And their denial of the power (qudra) in it' is a rebuttal to what might be said against the author's words, that the appropriate term based on what he mentioned is qudra (with a ḍamma on the qāf). So the commentator indicates that attributing the actions of servants to their power (qudra) entails the denial of qadar in them, so the naming is by virtue of this entailment. And let this be the last of what we intended to include in the Hashiyat al-Mawaqif. We ask Allah Almighty to make it purely for His noble face. Indeed, He is the Beneficent, the Merciful, and to benefit the sincere with it, and to make it a treasure for the Day of Judgment. Praise be to Allah, Lord of the worlds, and blessings and peace be upon Muhammad and all his family. The hashya is completed, authored by the great scholar, the sea of understanding, Sheikh Hasan Jalbī, may Allah envelop him in His mercy. Amen.
Source pages p. 409

Commentary
This passage narrates the origin of the Mu'tazila and outlines their key doctrines. It begins by identifying Wāṣil bin 'Aṭā' al-Ghazzāl as the founder, who left al-Hasan al-Basri's circle. The immediate cause was a man's question about the ruling on the committer of a major sin: the Khawarij were excommunicating them (takfīr), while the Murji'a were saying no harm comes from sin with faith. Al-Hasan was about to answer, but Wāṣil interjected with his famous doctrine: 'the intermediate position' (al-manzila bayna al-manzilatayn). He argued that a major sinner is neither a believer (since believer is a term of praise and the sinner does not deserve it) nor an unbeliever (because he still professes the shahāda). He will be in Hell if he dies without repentance, but his punishment will be lighter than that of unbelievers. Thereupon al-Hasan said 'Wāṣil has separated from us,' hence the name Mu'tazila. They were also called Qadariyya because they attribute human actions to their own power (qudra) and deny divine predetermination (qadar) in such actions. The passage then discusses the appropriateness of this name: some argued that the affirmers of qadar are more deserving of the name, but the author responds with two prophetic hadiths. The first, 'The Qadariyya are the Magians of this Ummah,' indicates that deniers of qadar resemble Magians by positing two creators (the servant creates his own actions). The second, 'They are the adversaries of Allah concerning al-Qadar,' only applies to those who claim they can do what Allah does not will—thus, deniers of qadar are the real adversaries, not the affirmers. The Mu'tazila themselves preferred the title 'People of Justice and Unity' (Ahl al-ʿAdl wa al-Tawḥīd) because they asserted the necessity of al-aṣlaḥ (what is best for creation) and denied eternal attributes. The commentator adds a linguistic note: the name Qadariyya is derived from qudra (power) rather than qadar, since their error lies in claiming power independent of Allah's decree. The passage concludes with a standard colophon ending the book.

Key Terms
المنزلة بين المنزلتين (al-manzila bayna al-manzilatayn)
صاحب الكبيرة (committer of major sin)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Wāṣil, why is a major sinner not a believer?
A) Because he lacks all good deeds
B) Because 'believer' is a term of praise and the sinner does not deserve it
C) Because he denies the prophethood
D) Because he does not pray

Key Takeaway
The intermediate position places the major sinner in a separate category: not a believer, not an unbeliever, but destined for a lighter Hell if unrepentant.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever excuse a major sin by thinking, 'I still believe in Allah and the Messenger, so I'm basically okay'? How does this lesson challenge that comfort and reveal its danger? What is one sin you need to repent from immediately because you cannot assume leniency?
?
If you were to die tonight with an unrepented major sin, where would this doctrine place you in the Hereafter? Does knowing that you would be in Hell forever, even if with lighter torment, change how you view your minor sins or delays in repentance? How will you remind yourself daily of this reality?
?
This lesson defines 'believer' as a term of praise. Look at your own life: if your actions were weighed right now, would you deserve to be called a believer? In what area of obedience are you failing to earn that title, and what specific step will you take today to close that gap?

Sects and Disagreements
intermediate
6 min
The Name 'Qadariyya' Applied to the Mu'tazila
Discusses the naming of the Mu'tazila as Qadariyya and defends it with hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Mu'tazila were called Qadariyya and how they defended their naming against opponents.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazila were called Qadariyya because they denied divine decree and attributed actions to human power.

The Mu'tazila were also known as Qadariyya due to their belief that humans create their own actions, thus denying divine predestination. The text discusses a debate: who deserves the name 'Qadariyya' more—those who affirm qadar or those who deny it? The author uses two Prophetic hadiths to argue that the deniers are the true Qadariyya, because they share with the Magians in positing two creators (the servant and Allah).

Guided Path
1
Read the naming passage
Read from 'ويلقبون بالقدرية' to 'ما يكرهه' carefully. Follow the argument: the Mu'tazila are called Qadariyya because they attribute actions to their own power and deny qadar.
Note the alternative viewpoint that affirmers of qadar are more deserving of the name.
2
Understand the two hadiths
The author provides two hadiths to refute the alternative view: 1) 'The Qadariyya are the Magians of this Ummah' and 2) 'They are the adversaries of Allah concerning al-Qadar.'
The first shows resemblance to Magians in affirming two creators; the second shows they oppose Allah by claiming power over what He does not will.
3
Grasp the linguistic point
The commentator adds that the name is derived from qudra (power) rather than from qadar, since the error lies in claiming independent power.
This explains why the name 'Qadariyya' fits the deniers better.

Commentary
This passage narrates the origin of the Mu'tazila and outlines their key doctrines. It begins by identifying Wāṣil bin 'Aṭā' al-Ghazzāl as the founder, who left al-Hasan al-Basri's circle. He will be in Hell if he dies without repentance, but his punishment will be lighter than that of unbelievers. Thereupon al-Hasan said 'Wāṣil has separated from us,' hence the name Mu'tazila. The commentator adds a linguistic note: the name Qadariyya is derived from qudra (power) rather than qadar, since their error lies in claiming power independent of Allah's decree. The passage concludes with a standard colophon ending the book.

Why does the author argue that the deniers of qadar are the true Qadariyya?
A) Because the Prophet called them Magians, and Magians affirm two creators
B) Because they recite the Qur'an more

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face difficulty or sin in your life, do you immediately attribute it to your own weakness or to others, forgetting that Allah is the Creator of all actions and that nothing occurs outside His decree? What does your reaction reveal about your belief in qadar?
?
The Mu'tazila called themselves 'People of Justice and Unity' but were known as Qadariyya by the scholars. Is there any area of your faith where you prefer a comfortable label over the truth that the revealed texts and scholars affirm? Are you willing to accept correction even when it challenges your self-image?
?
The hadith warns that deniers of qadar are 'adversaries of Allah.' Do you realize that your views on free will and decree can either draw you closer to Allah or place you in opposition to Him? Have you sincerely studied what Allah and His Messenger have said about qadar, or do you rely on your own reasoning?

Mu'tazila Self-Designation: People of Justice and Unity
States the Mu'tazila's self-title and its theological basis.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Mu'tazila called themselves 'People of Justice and Unity' and what those terms refer to.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazila named themselves after two core doctrines: God's justice (wujūb al-aṣlaḥ) and unity (negation of eternal attributes).

The Mu'tazila did not accept the label Qadariyya; instead, they proudly called themselves Ahl al-ʿAdl wa al-Tawḥīd (People of Justice and Unity). The text briefly explains that this name derives from their belief in the necessity of al-aṣlaḥ (what is best for creation) and their denial of eternal attributes. Understanding this self-designation reveals how the Mu'tazila viewed their own project: defending God's justice and oneness.

Guided Path
1
Read the self-designation
Locate the sentence: 'والمعتزلة لقبوا أنفسهم بأصحاب العدل والتوحيد' and the explanation that follows.
This is the Mu'tazila's own preferred title.
2
Analyze the two pillars
The text mentions two doctrines: 1) wujūb al-aṣlaḥ (obligation of what is best), 2) nafy al-ṣifāt al-qadīma (negation of eternal attributes). These reflect their understanding of 'adl (justice) and tawḥīd (unity).
These are explained in other lessons, but here they are simply named.
3
Connect to the earlier discussion
Notice that this self-designation contrasts with the pejorative label Qadariyya. It shows the Mu'tazila's positive theological program.

الفرق الأولى المعتزلة أصحاب واصل بن عطاء العزال اعتزل عن مجلس الحسن البصري وذلك أنه دخل على الحسن رجل فقال : يا إمام الدين ظهر في زماننا جماعة يكفرون صاحب الكبيرة يعني وعيدية الخوارج وجماعة أخرى يرجئون الكبائر يقولون : لا تضر مع الإيمان معصية كما لا تنفع مع الكفر طاعة، فكيف تحكم لنا أن نعتقد في ذلك؟ فتفكر الحسن وقبل أن يجيب قال واصل: أنا لا أقول : إن صاحب الكبيرة مؤمن مطلق ولا كافر مطلق ثم قام إلى إسطوانة من أسطوانات المسجد ) وأخذ يقرر ) على جماعة من أصحاب الحسن ما أجاب به من ( أن مرتكب الكبيرة ليس بمؤمن ولا كافر ويثبت له المنزلة بين المنزلتين ) قائلاً المؤمن اسم مدح والفاسق لا يستحق المدح فلا يكون مؤمناً، وليس بكافر أيضاً لإقراره بالشهادتين ولو وجد سائر أعمال الخير فيه فإذا مات بلا توبة خلد في النار إذ ليس في الآخرة إلا فريقان فريق في الجنة وفريق في السعير، لكن يخفض عليه ويكون در کته فوق دركات الكفار ) فقال الحسن : قد اعتزل عنا واصل) فلذلك وأصحابه معتزلة ) ويلقبون بالقدرية لإسنادهم أفعال العباد إلى قدرتهم وإنكارهم القدر فيها ( وإنهم قالوا: إن من يقول بالقدر خيره وشره من الله أولى باسم القدرية) منا وذلك لأن مثبت القدر أحق بأن ينسب إليه من نافيه . فنقول : كما يصح نسبة مثبته إليه يصح نسبة النافي أيضا إذا بالغ في نفيه لأنه ملتبس به (و) لا يمكن حمل القدرية على المثبتين له لأنه ( يرده قوله عليه السلام القدرية مجوس هذه الأمة») فإنه يقتضي مشاركتهم للمجوس فيما اشتهروا به من إثبات خالقين لا في قولهم بأن الله خلق شيئاً، ثم أنكره والنافون له هم المشاركون لهم في تلك الصفة المشهورة حيث يجعلون العبد خالقاً لأفعاله وينسبون القبائح والشرور إليه دون الله سبحانه ( و ) يرده أيضاً ( قوله عليه السلام) في حق القدرية : ((هم خصماء الله في القدر )) ولا خصومة للقائل بتفويض الأمور كلها إليه تعالى إنما الخصومة لمن يعتقد أنه يقدر على ما لا يريد الله بل يكرهه . (و) المعتزلة لقبوا أنفسهم بأصحاب العدل والتوحيد وذلك ( لقولهم بوجوب الأصلح ونفي الصفات القديمة ) يعني : أنهم قالوا : قوله : ( وإنكارهم القدرة فيها دفع لما يرد على كلام المصنف من أن المناسب على ما ذكره هو القدرة بضم القاف، فأشار الشارح إلى أن إسناد أفعال العباد إلى قدرتهم يتضمن نفي القدرة فيها، فالتسمية باعتبار هذا المتضمن وليكن هذا آخر ما أردنا إيراده في حواشي المواقف فنسأل الله تعالى أن يجعله خالصاً لوجهه الكريم. إنه هو البر الرحيم وأن ينفع به المخلصين. ويجعله ذخراً ليوم الدين والحمد لله رب العالمين والصلاة والصلام على محمد وآله أجمعين . • تمت الحاشية تأليف العالم العلامة والبحر الفهامة الشيخ حسن جلبي تغمده برحمته آمين .
The first sect: the Mu'tazila, the followers of Wāṣil bin 'Atā' al-Ghazzāl. He separated from the circle of al-Hasan al-Basri. That was because a man entered upon al-Hasan and said: 'O Imam of the religion, in our time there has appeared a group that declares the committer of a major sin an unbeliever, meaning the Wa'īdiyya of the Khawarij, and another group that postpones (judgment on) major sins, saying: Disobedience does not harm with faith just as obedience does not benefit with disbelief. So what do you command us to believe regarding this?' So al-Hasan reflected, and before he could answer, Wāṣil said: 'I do not say that the committer of a major sin is absolutely a believer nor absolutely an unbeliever.' Then he stood by one of the pillars of the mosque and began to explain to a group of al-Hasan's companions his answer: that the committer of a major sin is neither a believer nor an unbeliever, and he affirms for him the intermediate position (al-manzila bayna al-manzilatayn), saying: 'Believer is a term of praise, and the sinner does not deserve praise, so he is not a believer. And he is not an unbeliever because of his affirmation of the two testimonies, even if he lacks other good deeds. If he dies without repentance, he will be in Hell forever, since in the Hereafter there are only two groups: a group in Paradise and a group in the Blaze. But his punishment will be lighter, and his level will be above the levels of the unbelievers.' So al-Hasan said: 'Wāṣil has separated from us.' Therefore, he and his followers are called Mu'tazila. And they are also called Qadariyya because they attribute the actions of servants to their own power (qudra) and deny divine decree (qadar) concerning them. They said: 'One who affirms qadar, its good and evil from Allah, is more deserving of the name Qadariyya than us, because the affirmer of qadar is more entitled to be named after it than its denier.' We say: Just as it is possible to attribute (the name) to its affirmer, it is also possible to attribute it to its denier if he goes to excess in denying it, because he is involved with it. And it is not possible to apply Qadariyya to the affirmers, because the saying of the Prophet, peace be upon him, 'The Qadariyya are the Magians of this Ummah' refutes it. For it necessitates their sharing with the Magians in what they are famous for, namely affirming two creators, not in their saying that Allah created something and then denied it. The deniers are the ones who share with them in that famous attribute, as they make the servant the creator of his actions and attribute ugly things and evils to him instead of Allah, exalted be He. It is also refuted by his saying, peace be upon him, regarding the Qadariyya: 'They are the adversaries of Allah concerning al-Qadar.' There is no adversary for the one who delegates all affairs to Him, exalted be He. Rather, the adversary is the one who believes that he has power over what Allah does not will, but rather detests. And the Mu'tazila called themselves the People of Justice and Unity (Ahl al-ʿAdl wa al-Tawḥīd) because of their saying concerning the necessity of that which is most beneficial (wujūb al-aṣlaḥ) and the negation of the eternal attributes ṣifāt al-qadīma). Meaning: they said... His saying: 'And their denial of the power (qudra) in it' is a rebuttal to what might be said against the author's words, that the appropriate term based on what he mentioned is qudra (with a ḍamma on the qāf). So the commentator indicates that attributing the actions of servants to their power (qudra) entails the denial of qadar in them, so the naming is by virtue of this entailment. And let this be the last of what we intended to include in the Hashiyat al-Mawaqif. We ask Allah Almighty to make it purely for His noble face. Indeed, He is the Beneficent, the Merciful, and to benefit the sincere with it, and to make it a treasure for the Day of Judgment. Praise be to Allah, Lord of the worlds, and blessings and peace be upon Muhammad and all his family. The hashya is completed, authored by the great scholar, the sea of understanding, Sheikh Hasan Jalbī, may Allah envelop him in His mercy. Amen.
Source pages p. 409

Commentary
This passage narrates the origin of the Mu'tazila and outlines their key doctrines. It begins by identifying Wāṣil bin 'Aṭā' al-Ghazzāl as the founder, who left al-Hasan al-Basri's circle. The immediate cause was a man's question about the ruling on the committer of a major sin: the Khawarij were excommunicating them (takfīr), while the Murji'a were saying no harm comes from sin with faith. Al-Hasan was about to answer, but Wāṣil interjected with his famous doctrine: 'the intermediate position' (al-manzila bayna al-manzilatayn). He argued that a major sinner is neither a believer (since believer is a term of praise and the sinner does not deserve it) nor an unbeliever (because he still professes the shahāda). He will be in Hell if he dies without repentance, but his punishment will be lighter than that of unbelievers. Thereupon al-Hasan said 'Wāṣil has separated from us,' hence the name Mu'tazila. They were also called Qadariyya because they attribute human actions to their own power (qudra) and deny divine predetermination (qadar) in such actions. The passage then discusses the appropriateness of this name: some argued that the affirmers of qadar are more deserving of the name, but the author responds with two prophetic hadiths. The first, 'The Qadariyya are the Magians of this Ummah,' indicates that deniers of qadar resemble Magians by positing two creators (the servant creates his own actions). The second, 'They are the adversaries of Allah concerning al-Qadar,' only applies to those who claim they can do what Allah does not will—thus, deniers of qadar are the real adversaries, not the affirmers. The Mu'tazila themselves preferred the title 'People of Justice and Unity' (Ahl al-ʿAdl wa al-Tawḥīd) because they asserted the necessity of al-aṣlaḥ (what is best for creation) and denied eternal attributes. The commentator adds a linguistic note: the name Qadariyya is derived from qudra (power) rather than qadar, since their error lies in claiming power independent of Allah's decree. The passage concludes with a standard colophon ending the book.

Key Terms
أصحاب العدل والتوحيد (People of Justice and Unity)
وجوب الأصلح (wujūb al-aṣlaḥ)
نفي الصفات القديمة (negation of eternal attributes)

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Necessity of al-aṣlaḥ and negation of eternal attributes
C) Creation of the Qur'an and free will

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila identified themselves as champions of God's justice and unity, reflecting their core doctrines of wujūb al-aṣlaḥ and denial of eternal attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You now know that the Mu'tazila defined God's justice as His obligation to do what is best (wujūb al-aṣlaḥ). Do you accept that definition? If not, what is your understanding of God's justice, and where does it come from?
?
The Mu'tazila denied eternal attributes distinct from God's essence. Do you hold that God's attributes like knowledge and power are eternal and distinct? How would your life change if you believed they are not distinct? Would it affect how you relate to God?
?
The Mu'tazila proudly named themselves after their core doctrines. Are you willing to publicly identify with your deepest beliefs, even if they are controversial? What holds you back?
