The Nazzamiyya on Human Nature: Spirit and Body
Nazzamiyya doctrine on the composition of the human being.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Nazzamiyya's view that the human being is essentially the spirit, with the body as its instrument.

Core Idea
Man is spirit; body is just a tool.

This lesson focuses on the Nazzamiyya's conception of the human being. Influenced by naturalist philosophers, they defined the person as the spirit, a subtle body that permeates the physical body. The passage below gives their precise analogy.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition
Identify the claim: 'man is the spirit, the body is its instrument'.
2
Examine the analogy
Note how they describe the spirit's flow in the body like rose water in roses or oil in milk.
This shows their materialist influence.
3
Consider the source of this idea
The author notes al-Nazzam took this from the philosophers, especially naturalists.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النظامية : أصحاب إبراهيم بن سيار النظام وهو من شياطين القدرية طالع كتب الفلاسفة وخلط كلامهم بكلام المعتزلة، قالوا : لا يقدر الله أن يفعل بعباده في الدنيا ما لا صلاح لهم فيه، ولا ) يقدر أن يزيد ) في الآخرة ( أو ينقص من ثواب وعقاب ) لأهل الجنة والنار وتوهموا أن غاية تنزيهه تعالى الشرور والقبائح لا يكون إلا بسلب قدرته عليها، فهم في ذلك كمن هرب من المطر إلى الميزاب . ( و ) قالوا : (كونه) تعالى ( مريداً لفعله أنه خالقه ) على وفق علمه (و) كونه مريداً ( لفعل العبد أنه آمر به وقالوا الإنسان هو الروح والبدن (آلتها) وقد أخذه النظام من إلا أنه مال إلى الطبيعيين منهم فقال : الروح جسم لطيف سار في البدن سريان ماء الورد في الورد والدهن في اللبن والسمسم (و) قالوا : ( الأعراض ) كالألوان والطعوم والروائح وغيرها. (أجسام) كما هو مذهب هشام بن الحكم، فتارة يحكم بأن الأعراض أجسام وأخرى بأن الأجسام أعراض (و) قالوا: (الجوهر مؤلف من الأعراض المجتمعة ( والعلم مثل الجهل المركب ) والإيمان مثل الكفر) في تمام الماهية وأخذوا هذه المقالة من الفلاسفة حيث حكموا بأن حقيقتهما حصول الصورة في تمام القوة والامتياز بينهما بأمر خارجي هو مطابقة تلك الصورة لمتعلقها وعدم مطابقتها له . (و) قالوا: (الله خلق الخلق) أي : المخلوقات (دفعة) واحدة على ما هي عليه الآن معادناً ونباتاً وحيواناً وإنساناً وغير ذلك فلم يكن خلق آدم متقدماً على خلق أولاده إلا أنه تعالى كَمَنَ بعض المخلوقات في بعض. ( والتقدم والتأخر في الكون والظهور وهذه المقالة مأخوذة من كلام الفلاسفة القائلين بالخليط والكمون والبروز . (و) وقالوا : ( نظم القرآن ليس بمعجز) إنما المعجز إخباره بالغيب من الأمور السالفة والآتية وصرف الله العرب عن الاهتمام بمعارضته حتى لو خلاهم لأمكنهم الإتيان بمثله بل بأفصح منه، (و) قالوا : ( التواتر) الذي لا عدده ( يحتمل الكذب والإجماع والقياس ليس شيء منهما (بحجة و) قالوا : ( بالطفرة ومالوا إلى الرفض ووجوب النص على الإمام وثبوته ) أي : ثبوت النص من النبي على علي رضي الله عنه، لكن كتمه ( لكن كتمه عمر وقالوا : من خان ) بالسرقة ( ) فيما دون نصاب الزكاة كمائة وتسعة وتسعين درهماً وأربعة من الإبل مثلاً . (أو) ظلم به علی غیره بالغصب والتعدي ) لا يفسق
The Nazzamiyya: the followers of Ibrahim ibn Sayyar al-Nazzam, who was one of the devils of the Qadariyya. He read the books of the philosophers and mixed their words with the words of the Mu'tazila. They said: God cannot do for His servants in the world what is not beneficial for them, nor can He increase or decrease in the afterlife the reward and punishment of the people of Paradise and Hell. And they imagined that the ultimate purification of God from evils and abominations can only be by stripping Him of power over them. In that, they are like one who flees from rain into a drainpipe. And they said: His being willing for His act means that He is its creator according to His knowledge, and His being willing for the act of the servant means that He commands it. And they said: Man is the spirit, and the body is its instrument. Al-Nazzam took this from the [philosophers?], but he inclined to the naturalists among them, so he said: The spirit is a subtle body flowing in the body like the flow of rose water in roses and oil in milk and sesame. And they said: Accidents like colors, tastes, smells, etc. are bodies, as is the doctrine of Hisham ibn al-Hakam. Sometimes he judges that accidents are bodies, and sometimes that bodies are accidents. And they said: Substance is composed of accidents collected together. And knowledge is like compound ignorance, and faith is like disbelief in terms of complete essence. They took this statement from the philosophers, who judged that the reality of both is the acquisition of a form in the complete potential, and the distinction between them is by an external matter, namely the correspondence of that form to its object or its lack of correspondence. And they said: God created creation, i.e., creatures, all at once as they are now, minerals, plants, animals, humans, etc. So the creation of Adam was not prior to the creation of his children, except that God concealed some creatures within others. Priority and posteriority are in existence and manifestation. This statement is taken from the words of the philosophers who talk about mixture, concealment, and emergence. And they said: The composition of the Quran is not a miracle; the miracle is only its informing of the unseen from past and future matters, and God's turning away the Arabs from concerning themselves with challenging it, so that if He had left them, they could have produced something like it, indeed more eloquent than it. And they said: Mass transmission that has no number can contain lies, and consensus and analogy are not proofs. And they believed in al-tafra (atomism) and leaned towards Rafidism and the necessity of the text (nass) on the Imam and its establishment, i.e., the establishment of the text from the Prophet on Ali, may God be pleased with him, but Umar concealed it. And they said: Whoever betrays by theft below the nisab of zakat, for example one hundred and ninety-nine dirhams and four camels, or oppresses others by usurpation and transgression, does not become a sinner.
Source pages p. 412

Commentary
This passage enumerates the doctrines of the Nazzamiyya sect. It begins by identifying the founder, Ibrahim al-Nazzam, and notes his study of philosophy and syncretism with Mu'tazila. The first major point is that God cannot do anything harmful or not beneficial for His servants, and cannot alter reward or punishment; they thought purification from evil requires denying God power over it, which the author likens to fleeing from rain into a drain. Second, they define God's will: for His own act it is creation, for the servant's act it is command. Third, they define man as spirit with body as its instrument, and spirit is a subtle body flowing throughout. Fourth, they follow Hisham ibn al-Hakam in considering accidents to be bodies, sometimes reversing the relation. Fifth, substance is composed of accidents. Sixth, knowledge and compound ignorance, faith and disbelief are identical in essence, distinguished only by correspondence to reality. Seventh, God created all creatures at once, with priority and posteriority only in manifestation, not in existence. Eighth, the Quran's composition is not miraculous; the miracle is its predictions and God's preventing the Arabs from challenging it. Ninth, they deny the reliability of mass transmission, consensus, and analogy. Tenth, they believe in al-tafra (leap), lean toward Rafidism, and assert that the Prophet explicitly designated Ali as Imam, but Umar suppressed it. Finally, they hold that theft below the zakat threshold or oppression does not make one a sinner (fasiq).

Key Terms
روح
بدن
جسم لطيف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What analogy does al-Nazzam use for the spirit's relation to the body?
A) Fire in coal
B) Rose water in roses
C) Water in a river
D) Soul in a cage

Key Takeaway
For the Nazzamiyya, the human essence is a subtle spirit that flows through the body, which serves as its instrument.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Nazzamiyya claim your body is just a tool for your spirit. Examine your daily habits: do you more often serve your body's cravings or your spirit's higher purposes? Where does your true energy go?
?
If the spirit permeates the body like rose water in oil, then every action of your body is an expression of your spirit. Think of a recent mistake you made—was it your body acting alone, or was your spirit complicit? What does that reveal about your inner state?
?
The rose-water analogy suggests the spirit is everywhere in the body. In what areas of your life do you feel your spirit is absent? What would it take to let your spirit saturate that part of your life, starting today?

Accidents, Substances, Knowledge, and Faith in Nazzamiyya
Nazzamiyya doctrines on accidents, substance, and epistemology.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Nazzamiyya's paradoxical views that accidents are bodies, substance is composed of accidents, and knowledge is essentially like ignorance.

Core Idea
Confusion between categories: accidents are bodies, bodies are accidents.

This lesson covers several metaphysical doctrines of the Nazzamiyya. They followed Hisham ibn al-Hakam in considering accidents (colors, tastes) as bodies, and even reversed the relation. They also held that substance is composed of accidents. Finally, they claimed that knowledge and ignorance, faith and disbelief share the same essence, differing only in correspondence.

Guided Path
1
Understand the accident-body reversal
Read that accidents are bodies, and sometimes bodies are accidents.
This is unconventional.
2
Note the composition theory
Substance is composed of collected accidents.
3
Analyze the knowledge-faith identity
They say knowledge is like compound ignorance, faith like disbelief in essence.
They think the only distinction is external correspondence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النظامية : أصحاب إبراهيم بن سيار النظام وهو من شياطين القدرية طالع كتب الفلاسفة وخلط كلامهم بكلام المعتزلة، قالوا : لا يقدر الله أن يفعل بعباده في الدنيا ما لا صلاح لهم فيه، ولا ) يقدر أن يزيد ) في الآخرة ( أو ينقص من ثواب وعقاب ) لأهل الجنة والنار وتوهموا أن غاية تنزيهه تعالى الشرور والقبائح لا يكون إلا بسلب قدرته عليها، فهم في ذلك كمن هرب من المطر إلى الميزاب . ( و ) قالوا : (كونه) تعالى ( مريداً لفعله أنه خالقه ) على وفق علمه (و) كونه مريداً ( لفعل العبد أنه آمر به وقالوا الإنسان هو الروح والبدن (آلتها) وقد أخذه النظام من إلا أنه مال إلى الطبيعيين منهم فقال : الروح جسم لطيف سار في البدن سريان ماء الورد في الورد والدهن في اللبن والسمسم (و) قالوا : ( الأعراض ) كالألوان والطعوم والروائح وغيرها. (أجسام) كما هو مذهب هشام بن الحكم، فتارة يحكم بأن الأعراض أجسام وأخرى بأن الأجسام أعراض (و) قالوا: (الجوهر مؤلف من الأعراض المجتمعة ( والعلم مثل الجهل المركب ) والإيمان مثل الكفر) في تمام الماهية وأخذوا هذه المقالة من الفلاسفة حيث حكموا بأن حقيقتهما حصول الصورة في تمام القوة والامتياز بينهما بأمر خارجي هو مطابقة تلك الصورة لمتعلقها وعدم مطابقتها له . (و) قالوا: (الله خلق الخلق) أي : المخلوقات (دفعة) واحدة على ما هي عليه الآن معادناً ونباتاً وحيواناً وإنساناً وغير ذلك فلم يكن خلق آدم متقدماً على خلق أولاده إلا أنه تعالى كَمَنَ بعض المخلوقات في بعض. ( والتقدم والتأخر في الكون والظهور وهذه المقالة مأخوذة من كلام الفلاسفة القائلين بالخليط والكمون والبروز . (و) وقالوا : ( نظم القرآن ليس بمعجز) إنما المعجز إخباره بالغيب من الأمور السالفة والآتية وصرف الله العرب عن الاهتمام بمعارضته حتى لو خلاهم لأمكنهم الإتيان بمثله بل بأفصح منه، (و) قالوا : ( التواتر) الذي لا عدده ( يحتمل الكذب والإجماع والقياس ليس شيء منهما (بحجة و) قالوا : ( بالطفرة ومالوا إلى الرفض ووجوب النص على الإمام وثبوته ) أي : ثبوت النص من النبي على علي رضي الله عنه، لكن كتمه ( لكن كتمه عمر وقالوا : من خان ) بالسرقة ( ) فيما دون نصاب الزكاة كمائة وتسعة وتسعين درهماً وأربعة من الإبل مثلاً . (أو) ظلم به علی غیره بالغصب والتعدي ) لا يفسق
The Nazzamiyya: the followers of Ibrahim ibn Sayyar al-Nazzam, who was one of the devils of the Qadariyya. He read the books of the philosophers and mixed their words with the words of the Mu'tazila. They said: God cannot do for His servants in the world what is not beneficial for them, nor can He increase or decrease in the afterlife the reward and punishment of the people of Paradise and Hell. And they imagined that the ultimate purification of God from evils and abominations can only be by stripping Him of power over them. In that, they are like one who flees from rain into a drainpipe. And they said: His being willing for His act means that He is its creator according to His knowledge, and His being willing for the act of the servant means that He commands it. And they said: Man is the spirit, and the body is its instrument. Al-Nazzam took this from the [philosophers?], but he inclined to the naturalists among them, so he said: The spirit is a subtle body flowing in the body like the flow of rose water in roses and oil in milk and sesame. And they said: Accidents like colors, tastes, smells, etc. are bodies, as is the doctrine of Hisham ibn al-Hakam. Sometimes he judges that accidents are bodies, and sometimes that bodies are accidents. And they said: Substance is composed of accidents collected together. And knowledge is like compound ignorance, and faith is like disbelief in terms of complete essence. They took this statement from the philosophers, who judged that the reality of both is the acquisition of a form in the complete potential, and the distinction between them is by an external matter, namely the correspondence of that form to its object or its lack of correspondence. And they said: God created creation, i.e., creatures, all at once as they are now, minerals, plants, animals, humans, etc. So the creation of Adam was not prior to the creation of his children, except that God concealed some creatures within others. Priority and posteriority are in existence and manifestation. This statement is taken from the words of the philosophers who talk about mixture, concealment, and emergence. And they said: The composition of the Quran is not a miracle; the miracle is only its informing of the unseen from past and future matters, and God's turning away the Arabs from concerning themselves with challenging it, so that if He had left them, they could have produced something like it, indeed more eloquent than it. And they said: Mass transmission that has no number can contain lies, and consensus and analogy are not proofs. And they believed in al-tafra (atomism) and leaned towards Rafidism and the necessity of the text (nass) on the Imam and its establishment, i.e., the establishment of the text from the Prophet on Ali, may God be pleased with him, but Umar concealed it. And they said: Whoever betrays by theft below the nisab of zakat, for example one hundred and ninety-nine dirhams and four camels, or oppresses others by usurpation and transgression, does not become a sinner.
Source pages p. 412

Commentary
This passage enumerates the doctrines of the Nazzamiyya sect. It begins by identifying the founder, Ibrahim al-Nazzam, and notes his study of philosophy and syncretism with Mu'tazila. The first major point is that God cannot do anything harmful or not beneficial for His servants, and cannot alter reward or punishment; they thought purification from evil requires denying God power over it, which the author likens to fleeing from rain into a drain. Second, they define God's will: for His own act it is creation, for the servant's act it is command. Third, they define man as spirit with body as its instrument, and spirit is a subtle body flowing throughout. Fourth, they follow Hisham ibn al-Hakam in considering accidents to be bodies, sometimes reversing the relation. Fifth, substance is composed of accidents. Sixth, knowledge and compound ignorance, faith and disbelief are identical in essence, distinguished only by correspondence to reality. Seventh, God created all creatures at once, with priority and posteriority only in manifestation, not in existence. Eighth, the Quran's composition is not miraculous; the miracle is its predictions and God's preventing the Arabs from challenging it. Ninth, they deny the reliability of mass transmission, consensus, and analogy. Tenth, they believe in al-tafra (leap), lean toward Rafidism, and assert that the Prophet explicitly designated Ali as Imam, but Umar suppressed it. Finally, they hold that theft below the zakat threshold or oppression does not make one a sinner (fasiq).

Key Terms
عرض
جوهر
علم
جهل
إيمان
كفر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Nazzamiyya, what distinguishes knowledge from compound ignorance?
A) Their essence
B) The correspondence of the form to its object
C) The power of the intellect
D) Nothing, they are identical

Key Takeaway
The Nazzamiyya held paradoxical views that collapse categorical distinctions: accidents are bodies, substance is composed of accidents, and knowledge/faith differ from ignorance/disbelief only by external correspondence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You just read that the Nazzamiyya reduce the difference between faith and disbelief to a mere external correspondence. Does your own faith rest on more than just a mental form that happens to match reality? What would be left of your faith if that correspondence were broken?
?
The passage claims knowledge and ignorance are identical in essence. When you learn something new, do you treat it as a transformation of your soul or just a rearrangement of mental content? Are you truly changed by what you know?
?
If substance is nothing but a collection of accidents, what grounds your sense of personal identity? Are you just a bundle of changing attributes, or is there something deeper that holds you together?

The Nazzamiyya on Creation and the Miraculous Nature of the Quran
Nazzamiyya doctrines on creation and the Quran's miracle.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Nazzamiyya's view that God created all things at once and that the Quran's miracle lies in prophecy and prevention, not its composition.

Core Idea
Creation in one act; Quran's miracle is not its words.

This lesson covers two more Nazzamiyya doctrines. First, they believed God created all creatures simultaneously, with apparent priority only in manifestation. Second, they denied that the Quran's composition is miraculous, claiming the miracle is its prophecies and God's turning the Arabs away from challenging it. Both borrow from philosophical concepts.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the instantaneous creation theory
Read that God created everything at once, with concealment and emergence over time.
This is like the philosophical concept of 'kumun' (latency).
2
Understand their Quranic miracle view
The Quran's literary quality is not a miracle; the miracle is its news of the unseen and divine hindrance.
3
See the philosophical influence
Both ideas are traced to philosophers (mixture and latency; human ability to imitate).

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the Nazzamiyya entirely denied the miracle of the Quran.

According to the Nazzamiyya, what is the miracle of the Quran?
A) Its eloquent composition
B) Its prophecies and God's turning away the Arabs

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You claim to believe the Quran is a miracle, but is your conviction built more on its beautiful language or on the truths it reveals that no human could know? How would your faith change if you were forced to accept the Nazzamiyya's view that its literary form is not miraculous?
?
The Nazzamiyya teach that all creation happened in a single instant, and what we call 'time' is just the unfolding of what was once concealed. If that is true, then every moment of your life is not new but a journey of emergence. Does that thought comfort you or unsettle you? Why?

The Nazzamiyya on Transmission, Consensus, Analogy, and Imamate
Nazzamiyya views on transmission, consensus, analogy, and imamate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Nazzamiyya's rejection of the reliability of mass transmission, consensus, and analogy, and their view that the Prophet explicitly designated Ali as Imam.

Core Idea
Rejection of key sources of Islamic law and a Shia-leaning imamate theory.

This lesson covers the Nazzamiyya's methodological skepticism. They doubted the impossibility of lies in mass transmission, and rejected consensus and analogy as proofs. Politically, they leaned toward Rafidism, affirming an explicit text designating Ali as Imam, which they claimed was concealed by Umar.

Guided Path
1
Understand their criticism of mass transmission
Read that even a large number of transmitters can lie.
This undermines the reliability of many hadith.
2
Note rejection of consensus and analogy
They say neither is a valid proof (hujja).
3
Examine their imamate doctrine
They believe in obligatory appointment of an Imam by explicit text (nass) and that the Prophet designated Ali, but Umar suppressed it.
This aligns with Shia beliefs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(و) قالوا: (الله خلق الخلق) أي : المخلوقات (دفعة) واحدة على ما هي عليه الآن معادناً ونباتاً وحيواناً وإنساناً وغير ذلك فلم يكن خلق آدم متقدماً على خلق أولاده إلا أنه تعالى كَمَنَ بعض المخلوقات في بعض. ( والتقدم والتأخر في الكون والظهور وهذه المقالة مأخوذة من كلام الفلاسفة القائلين بالخليط والكمون والبروز . (و) وقالوا : ( نظم القرآن ليس بمعجز) إنما المعجز إخباره بالغيب من الأمور السالفة والآتية وصرف الله العرب عن الاهتمام بمعارضته حتى لو خلاهم لأمكنهم الإتيان بمثله بل بأفصح منه، (و) قالوا : ( التواتر) الذي لا عدده ( يحتمل الكذب والإجماع والقياس ليس شيء منهما (بحجة و) قالوا : ( بالطفرة ومالوا إلى الرفض ووجوب النص على الإمام وثبوته ) أي : ثبوت النص من النبي على علي رضي الله عنه، لكن كتمه ( لكن كتمه عمر وقالوا : من خان ) بالسرقة ( ) فيما دون نصاب الزكاة كمائة وتسعة وتسعين درهماً وأربعة من الإبل مثلاً . (أو) ظلم به علی غیره بالغصب والتعدي ) لا يفسق
The Nazzamiyya: the followers of Ibrahim ibn Sayyar al-Nazzam, who was one of the devils of the Qadariyya. He read the books of the philosophers and mixed their words with the words of the Mu'tazila. They said: God cannot do for His servants in the world what is not beneficial for them, nor can He increase or decrease in the afterlife the reward and punishment of the people of Paradise and Hell. And they imagined that the ultimate purification of God from evils and abominations can only be by stripping Him of power over them. In that, they are like one who flees from rain into a drainpipe. And they said: His being willing for His act means that He is its creator according to His knowledge, and His being willing for the act of the servant means that He commands it. And they said: Man is the spirit, and the body is its instrument. Al-Nazzam took this from the [philosophers?], but he inclined to the naturalists among them, so he said: The spirit is a subtle body flowing in the body like the flow of rose water in roses and oil in milk and sesame. And they said: Accidents like colors, tastes, smells, etc. are bodies, as is the doctrine of Hisham ibn al-Hakam. Sometimes he judges that accidents are bodies, and sometimes that bodies are accidents. And they said: Substance is composed of accidents collected together. And knowledge is like compound ignorance, and faith is like disbelief in terms of complete essence. They took this statement from the philosophers, who judged that the reality of both is the acquisition of a form in the complete potential, and the distinction between them is by an external matter, namely the correspondence of that form to its object or its lack of correspondence. And they said: God created creation, i.e., creatures, all at once as they are now, minerals, plants, animals, humans, etc. So the creation of Adam was not prior to the creation of his children, except that God concealed some creatures within others. Priority and posteriority are in existence and manifestation. This statement is taken from the words of the philosophers who talk about mixture, concealment, and emergence. And they said: The composition of the Quran is not a miracle; the miracle is only its informing of the unseen from past and future matters, and God's turning away the Arabs from concerning themselves with challenging it, so that if He had left them, they could have produced something like it, indeed more eloquent than it. And they said: Mass transmission that has no number can contain lies, and consensus and analogy are not proofs. And they believed in al-tafra (atomism) and leaned towards Rafidism and the necessity of the text (nass) on the Imam and its establishment, i.e., the establishment of the text from the Prophet on Ali, may God be pleased with him, but Umar concealed it. And they said: Whoever betrays by theft below the nisab of zakat, for example one hundred and ninety-nine dirhams and four camels, or oppresses others by usurpation and transgression, does not become a sinner.
Source pages p. 412

Commentary
This passage enumerates the doctrines of the Nazzamiyya sect. It begins by identifying the founder, Ibrahim al-Nazzam, and notes his study of philosophy and syncretism with Mu'tazila. The first major point is that God cannot do anything harmful or not beneficial for His servants, and cannot alter reward or punishment; they thought purification from evil requires denying God power over it, which the author likens to fleeing from rain into a drain. Second, they define God's will: for His own act it is creation, for the servant's act it is command. Third, they define man as spirit with body as its instrument, and spirit is a subtle body flowing throughout. Fourth, they follow Hisham ibn al-Hakam in considering accidents to be bodies, sometimes reversing the relation. Fifth, substance is composed of accidents. Sixth, knowledge and compound ignorance, faith and disbelief are identical in essence, distinguished only by correspondence to reality. Seventh, God created all creatures at once, with priority and posteriority only in manifestation, not in existence. Eighth, the Quran's composition is not miraculous; the miracle is its predictions and God's preventing the Arabs from challenging it. Ninth, they deny the reliability of mass transmission, consensus, and analogy. Tenth, they believe in al-tafra (leap), lean toward Rafidism, and assert that the Prophet explicitly designated Ali as Imam, but Umar suppressed it. Finally, they hold that theft below the zakat threshold or oppression does not make one a sinner (fasiq).

Key Terms
تواتر
إجماع
قياس
نص
إمامة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What did the Nazzamiyya claim about Umar with respect to the imamate?
A) He was the rightful Imam
B) He concealed the Prophet's designation of Ali
C) He invented the doctrine of nass
D) He opposed the concept of nass

Key Takeaway
The Nazzamiyya rejected the reliability of mass transmission, consensus, and analogy as proofs, and held that the Prophet explicitly designated Ali as Imam, but this was concealed by Umar.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Nazzamiyya rejected mass transmission, consensus, and analogy, but accepted a single text about Ali that was allegedly concealed. Is there any belief you hold that depends on rejecting widely accepted evidence while clinging to a single source? What would it take for you to honestly examine that?
?
The Nazzamiyya accused Umar of concealing the Prophet's supposed appointment of Ali. Have you ever assumed a cover-up to preserve a cherished belief? How does this passage challenge you to trust the collective testimony of the Muslim community over personal inclinations?
?
If you were to apply the Nazzamiyya's criteria for proof—rejecting consensus and analogy—what parts of your own faith would become uncertain? Are you willing to face that uncertainty, or do you rely on these proofs without question?

The Nazzamiyya on Minor Sins and Theft
Nazzamiyya's view on the sinfulness of minor theft and oppression.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Nazzamiyya's view that theft below the zakat threshold or oppression does not make one a sinner (fasiq).

Core Idea
Small theft or oppression is not sinful.

This final lesson from the passage covers the Nazzamiyya's lenient view on certain minor offenses. They said that if someone steals an amount below the zakat threshold (e.g., 199 dirhams) or oppresses others by usurpation, they do not become a fasiq (sinner). This likely stems from a different definition of sin or a rejection of certain jurisprudential criteria.

Guided Path
1
Read the specific examples
Notice the amounts: theft of 199 dirhams (less than nisab) and oppression by usurpation.
Nisab of zakat for silver is 200 dirhams.
2
Understand the ruling
They say such acts do not make one a fasiq.
This contradicts orthodox views.
3
Consider the implications
Think about how this affects their concept of sin and moral responsibility.

Source Text

Beliefs of the Usawariyya Sect
Describes the Usawariyya's additional doctrine.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinctive belief of the Usawariyya sect regarding God's power and human capability.

Core Idea
God's knowledge does not eliminate human power over opposites.

The Usawariyya were a Mu'tazili sub-sect that built on the Nazzamiyya. They introduced a radical limitation on divine power while affirming human freedom. This passage outlines their specific addition, which centers on the relationship between God's foreknowledge and human capacity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sect and its relation
Read the passage and note that the Usawariyya agreed with the Nazzamiyya on certain points. Identify the sect's founder and its lineage.
The Usawariyya are named after al-Usawari.
2
Understand the distinctive claim
The Usawariyya added that God cannot do what He has informed will not exist or what He knows. This is a limitation on divine power based on foreknowledge.
This contrasts with the mainstream view that God's knowledge does not limit His power.
3
Grasp the reasoning
The reasoning is that human power is equally suited to both opposites. If a person can do one thing, they can do its opposite. God's knowledge or information does not remove that capability.
This argument defends human free will against theological determinism.
4
Reflect on the theological consequence
Consider how this view impacts the concept of divine omnipotence. Does God's foreknowledge place constraints on what He can do?
The Usawariyya answer 'yes', while many other schools say 'no'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإسوارية: أصحاب الإسواري) وافقوا النظامية فيما ذهبوا إليه و ( زادوا ) عليهم ( أن الله تعالى لا يقدر على ما أخبر بعدمه أو علم علمه والإنسان قادر عليه لأن قدرة العبد صالحة للضدين على سواء، فإذا قدر على أحدهما قدر على الآخر فتعلق العلم أو الإخبار من الله تعالى بأحد الطرفين لا يمنع مقدورية الآخر للعبد
The Usawariyya: the followers of al-Usawari. They agreed with the Nazzamiyya in what they held, and added to them: that God cannot do what He has informed will not exist or what He knows, while man is capable of it, because the power of the servant is equally suited to both opposites. So if he is capable of one, he is capable of the other. The attachment of knowledge or information from God to one side does not prevent the other from being within the servant's capability.
Source pages p. 413

Commentary
This passage describes the Usawariyya sub-sect. They agreed with the Nazzamiyya (the previous sect) on the points that they held. Their distinctive addition is a claim about God's power: God cannot do something that He has informed will not happen or that He knows will not happen. Humans, however, are capable of such acts because human power is indifferent to opposites—if a person can do one thing, they can also do its opposite. God's knowledge or information that a particular act will not occur does not remove that act from the servant's power. Thus, they maintain human freedom even when God has decreed the opposite.

Key Terms
قدرة
علم
إخبار
ضدين
مقدورية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the Usawariyya denied God's power over all things, completely stripping Him of omnipotence.
Correction: The Usawariyya did not deny God's power over all things; they specifically limited it by His own knowledge and information. They affirmed divine power, but held that foreknowledge sets boundaries on what God can do.

Checkpoint
What did the Usawariyya add to the doctrines of the Nazzamiyya?
A) That God cannot oppress rational adults
B) That God cannot do what He has informed will not happen or what He knows
C) That accidents are bodies
D) That the Quran's composition is a miracle

Key Takeaway
The Usawariyya held that divine foreknowledge does not negate human capacity for opposite actions, thereby limiting God's power relative to His own knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believe that God's knowledge of your actions does not negate your freedom, where in your life have you used 'it was written' as an excuse for sin or laziness? Repent and commit to owning your choices starting today.
?
The Usawariyya argued that divine information limits God's power but not yours. Is there a decision you are avoiding because you think God has already decided the outcome? How does this lesson push you to act despite your uncertainty?
?
You claim to believe in divine foreknowledge, yet you still plan and choose. Why do you live as if your choices matter, while the Usawariyya made human capability the ultimate ground for accountability? Align your theology with your daily experience of responsibility.

The Iskafiyya on Divine Power and Oppression
Describes the Iskafiyya view on God's power to oppress.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Iskafiyya's distinctive claim that God's power to oppress is limited to non-rational beings.

Core Idea
The Iskafiyya said God can oppress children and the insane, but not rational adults.

This lesson introduces a sectarian view within Islamic theology that places a moral constraint on God's omnipotence. The Iskafiyya argued that oppression (ẓulm) is defined in relation to rational moral agency, so God's power to oppress is limited accordingly. Let's examine their exact statement.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the contrast between the two categories of beings.
The passage is short, so read it carefully.
2
Analyze the distinction
Identify the two groups: rational adults vs. children and the insane. Why does the Iskafiyya make this distinction?
Think about the definition of oppression (ẓulm) as injustice.
3
Consider the theological implication
Reflect on what this view implies about divine power. Does it deny God's omnipotence? How does it define oppression?
This sect limited God's power based on moral considerations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإسكافية : أصحاب أبي جعفر الإسكاف، قالوا : الله تعالى لا يقدر على ظلم العقلاء بخلاف ظلم الصبيان والمجانين) فإنه يقدر عليه
The Iskafiyya: the followers of Abu Ja'far al-Iskaf. They said: God cannot oppress the rational, unlike the oppression of children and the insane, for He is able to do that.
Source pages p. 413

Commentary
This passage introduces the Iskafiyya sect, followers of Abu Ja'far al-Iskaf. Their distinctive teaching is that God is incapable of oppressing (zulm) rational adults, but He is capable of oppressing children and the insane. This implies a limitation on God's power based on the nature of the recipient: oppression is defined as treating someone in a way that is unjust, and since rational adults have a claim to justice, God cannot act unjustly toward them. Children and the insane lack full moral responsibility, so God can cause them harm without that harm being considered oppression in the same sense.

Key Terms
قدرة
ظلم
عقلاء
صبيان
مجانين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the Iskafiyya denied God's ability to cause harm altogether.
Correction: They only denied God's ability to oppress rational adults; they affirmed His ability to oppress children and the insane.

Checkpoint
According to the Iskafiyya, over whom can God exercise oppression?
A) Over rational adults only
B) Over children and the insane only
C) Over all creatures
D) Over no one

Key Takeaway
The Iskafiyya held that God's power to oppress is limited to those who lack rational moral agency, i.e., children and the insane.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever assume that God is limited in what He can do to you because you consider yourself rational and deserving of justice? How does the Iskafiyya's view challenge or affirm your understanding of God's justice and power in your own life?
?
When you consider the suffering of children or the insane, do you struggle with the idea of God's role? How does this passage's distinction between rational and non-rational affect how you think about God's justice in the face of innocent suffering?
?
Are there areas in your life where you feel God has treated you unjustly? How might the Iskafiyya's teaching that oppression is impossible for God change your perspective on your own trials?

Beliefs of the Ja'fariyya Sect
Describes the Ja'fariyya additions to the Iskafiyya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinctive doctrinal additions of the Ja'fariyya sect, particularly their views on sinners, consensus, and the relationship between minor sins and faith.

Core Idea
The Ja'fariyya considered some sinners worse than heretics and rejected consensus not based on revealed text.

The Ja'fariyya sect, named after Ja'far ibn Mubashshir and Ibn Harb, expanded on the teachings of the Iskafiyya. This passage highlights three key additions: the extreme condemnation of certain sinners, the rejection of consensus for punishment where a revealed text exists, and the claim that a thief of a single grain loses faith. These positions reflect their rigorous approach to faith and sin.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the three additions
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it, then read the translation. Note the three distinct additions the Ja'fariyya made beyond the Iskafiyya.
Pay attention to the structure: after stating agreement, they added 'that...' three times.
2
Understand the first addition: some sinners are worse than heretics
The passage states that among the sinners (fussaq) of the community, there are those worse than heretics (zanadiqa) and Magians (majus). Consider the gravity of this claim.
3
Examine the second addition: consensus on punishment for drinking is wrong
They argued that the consensus (ijma') regarding the hadd punishment for drinking alcohol is erroneous because the true basis for any punishment must be a revealed text (nass), not consensus.
This rejects the validity of that particular consensus.
4
Consider the third addition: a thief of a grain is stripped of faith
They held that a thief who steals even a single grain (below the nisab) is a sinner (fasiq) who has divested himself of faith (munkhali' 'an al-iman), implying loss of faith for minor theft.
This contrasts with standard Islamic law where theft requires a minimum amount for the hadd punishment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الجعفرية : أصحاب (الجعفرين جعفر بن مبشر وابن حرب ) وافقوا الإسكافية و ( زادوا عليهم متابعة لابن المبشِّر ) أن في فساق الأمة من هو شر من الزنادقة والمجوس، والإجماع من الأمة ( على حد الشرب خطأ، لأن المعتبر في الحد هو النص ( وسارق الحبة ) فاسق ( منخلع عن الإيمان
The Ja'fariyya: the followers of the two Ja'fars: Ja'far ibn Mubashshir and Ibn Harb. They agreed with the Iskafiyya and added to them, following Ibn al-Mubashshir, that among the sinners of the community there are those who are worse than the heretics and the Magians, and that the consensus of the community on the punishment for drinking is wrong, because the basis in punishment is the text (nass), and the thief of a grain is a sinner stripped of faith.
Source pages p. 413

Commentary
This passage describes the Ja'fariyya sect, named after two figures: Ja'far ibn Mubashshir and Ibn Harb. They agreed with the previous sect (Iskafiyya) but added several points based on the teaching of Ibn al-Mubashshir. First, some sinners within the Muslim community are worse than heretics (zanadiqa) and Magians. Second, the consensus (ijma') of the community regarding the punishment (hadd) for drinking alcohol is erroneous because the correct basis for any punishment must be a revealed text (nass), not consensus. Third, a thief who steals even a single grain (below the nisab) is considered a sinner (fasiq) who has divested himself of faith, implying that such minor theft causes loss of faith.

Key Terms
فساق
زنادقة
مجوس
إجماع
حد
نص
سارق
إيمان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Ja'fariyya rejected all consensus of the community.
Correction: They only rejected consensus on the punishment for drinking because they insisted on a revealed text; they did not reject all consensus.

Checkpoint
What did the Ja'fariyya consider wrong regarding the punishment for drinking alcohol?
A) The punishment itself is too harsh
B) The consensus of the community on it is incorrect because the true basis is a revealed text
C) The punishment should be based on the Prophet's practice only
D) The punishment only applies to non-Muslims

Key Takeaway
The Ja'fariyya held extreme views on sin, considering some sinners worse than non-believers, rejecting non-textual consensus for punishments, and deeming even minor theft as grounds for loss of faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In this lesson, the Ja'fariyya considered some sinners worse than heretics. Have you ever judged a fellow Muslim's sin as putting them beyond the pale? What does your willingness to do so reveal about your own heart? Will you repent from such judgment and commit to seeing every believer as capable of faith?
?
The Ja'fariyya rejected a consensus because it was not based on revealed text. Think of a religious practice you follow that relies on tradition or consensus. Are you willing to question it if you cannot find clear textual evidence? Or are you content to follow without certainty? What would it cost you to seek the text?
?
The Ja'fariyya said the thief of a grain is stripped of faith. This is an extreme view, but it reminds us that sin can weaken faith. Reflect on a 'small' sin you habitually commit. How has it affected your closeness to Allah? Are you ready to take it seriously and repent?

The Bashariyya Sect and the Doctrine of Generated Acts
Introduces Bishr ibn al-Mu'tamir and defines tawallud.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand who Bishr ibn al-Mu'tamir was and the Mu'tazili doctrine of tawallud (generated acts), which holds that accidents can be produced in a body from the act of another.

Core Idea
Tawallud: accidents can be generated in one body from another's act.

The Bashariyya sect, founded by Bishr ibn al-Mu'tamir, introduced a unique theory of causality known as tawallud. This lesson explains the founder and the core idea of generated accidents.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage: Bishr and tawallud
Read the Arabic passage introducing Bishr and defining tawallud. Notice the parenthetical glosses.
The term 'توليد' is key.
2
Identify key terms
Look for توليد, أعراض, إدراكات, and متولدة. Understand how they relate.
3
Reflect on causality
Consider how tawallud differs from direct divine creation. Does this give humans a form of causal power?
This connects to broader kalam debates.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
البشرية : هو بشر بن المعتمر كان من أفاضل علماء المعتزلة وهو الذي أحدث القول بالتوليد ( قالوا : الأعراض من الألوان والطعوم والروائح وغيرها كالإدراكات من السمع والرؤية ( تقع ) أي يجوز أن تحصل (متولدة) في الجسم من فعل الغير كما إذا كان أسبابها من فعله، قالوا : (القدرة ) والاستطاعة ( سلامة البنية ) والجوارح عن الآفات (و) قالوا : الله قادر على تعذيب الطفل ) ولو عذبه لكان ( ظالماً ) لكنه لا يستحسن أن يقال في حقه ذلك، بل يجب أن يقال : ( ولو عذبه لكان ( الطفل بالغاً ( عاقلاً عاصياً) مستحقاً للعقاب ) وفيه تناقض)، إذ حاصله أن الله يقدر أن يظلم ولو ظلم لكان عادلاً
The Bashariyya: he is Bishr ibn al-Mu'tamir, who was among the most virtuous scholars of the Mu'tazila, and he was the one who originated the doctrine of generation (tawallud). They said: Accidents like colors, tastes, smells, etc., and perceptions like hearing and seeing, occur, i.e., it is permissible that they come about as generated (mutawallida) in the body from the act of another, just as if their causes are from his act. They said: Power and capacity are the soundness of the bodily structure and limbs from defects. And they said: God is able to punish a child, but if He punished him, He would be an oppressor. However, it is not appropriate to say that of Him; rather, one must say: If He punished him, the child would be an adult, rational, disobedient, deserving of punishment. This contains a contradiction, because its import is that God is able to oppress, and if He oppressed, He would be just.
Source pages p. 413

Commentary
This passage describes the Bashariyya sect, founded by Bishr ibn al-Mu'tamir, a leading Mu'tazili scholar who originated the theory of tawallud (generated actions). They held that accidents such as colors, tastes, smells, and perceptions like seeing and hearing can occur as generated effects in a body from the act of another being, meaning that an action can produce a separate effect in another subject without direct agency. They also defined power (qudra) and capacity (istita'a) as the soundness of the body and limbs from defects, a physicalist view. Regarding God's punishment of a child, they said: God is able to punish a child, but if He did so, He would be an oppressor; yet it is not fitting to say that about God. Instead, they assert that if God punished a child, the child would be considered an adult, rational, and disobedient, thus deserving punishment. The author points out the contradiction: God can oppress, but if He oppresses He is considered just, which is contradictory.

Key Terms
توليد
أعراض
إدراكات
متولدة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Bashariyya denied all causality.
Correction: They affirmed generated causality between created acts and their effects, while still attributing ultimate power to God.

Checkpoint
What does 'tawallud' refer to in the Bashariyya doctrine?
A) God's direct creation of all actions
B) The generation of accidents from the act of another
C) The soundness of the body
D) The punishment of children

Key Takeaway
The Bashariyya originated the concept of tawallud, where accidents are generated in one body from the act of another, providing a causal link between created actions and their effects.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you often attribute the good or bad outcomes of your actions directly to yourself, forgetting that they are generated through a chain of causes upheld by God? How might acknowledging tawallud change your sense of humility and dependence on Allah?
?
If every accident you cause in another person—like a word that hurts or a kindness that comforts—is generated from your act, how does that deepen your sense of responsibility for your actions? Will you now pause before speaking or acting, knowing the effects you generate?
?
The Mu'tazila used tawallud to explain how humans can be morally accountable for their acts. Have you ever struggled to reconcile God's complete control with your own responsibility? After learning this doctrine, what assumption about your own causality do you need to examine in your heart?

The Bashariyya Concept of Power and Capacity
Defines power and capacity as soundness of body.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Bashariyya's physicalist definition of power (qudra) and capacity (istita'a) as the soundness of the bodily structure and limbs.

Core Idea
Power is nothing but soundness of the body.

The Bashariyya offered a minimalist definition of human capability: power and capacity are simply the body being free from defects. This lesson examines this view and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the short passage
Read the definition of power and capacity. Note that it is a single sentence.
2
Compare with other views
How does this differ from other theological schools that consider power a distinct accident?
3
Reflect on agency
If power is just bodily soundness, what does that imply about human choice?

The Bashariyya on God's Punishment of a Child
States Bashariyya position on punishing a child and the contradiction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Bashariyya's paradoxical position that God is able to punish a child but if He did so, the child would be considered an adult sinner, and the resulting contradiction.

Core Idea
God can punish a child, but that would make the child an adult sinner.

The Bashariyya faced a theological dilemma: can God punish a child? Their answer leads to a redefinition of the child's status and an apparent contradiction. This lesson unpacks their reasoning and the criticism leveled by the author.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage on punishing a child. Note the three parts: ability, injustice, redefinition.
2
Identify the claims
Identify the three claims: God can punish, but it would be unjust, but then the child becomes an adult sinner.
3
Notice the author's comment
Look for the phrase 'وفيه تناقض' (this contains a contradiction). Understand why.
4
Reflect on the contradiction
Why is it contradictory to say God can oppress and that oppression would be just?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This lesson reveals the Bashariyya's desperate attempt to avoid calling God unjust. When you face a situation where God's actions seem difficult to reconcile with justice, do you find yourself twisting your understanding to protect your image of God, or do you humbly submit to His wisdom even when it confuses you? What is your heart's default response when you cannot explain God's decree?
?
The Bashariyya's position led to a logical contradiction because they refused to accept that God's justice might be beyond human categories. Are there areas in your life where you are trying to force God's actions into your own box of what is 'fair'? Will you now release that demand and trust that His justice is perfect even when you cannot comprehend it?
?
Consider the innocent child in this argument. How does your heart react to the possibility of a child's suffering? Do you trust that God is just even when you see such suffering, or do you secretly accuse Him? This lesson calls you to examine whether you truly believe God is 'just' in His own definition, not yours.

Beliefs of the Muzdariyya Sect
Describes the Muzdariyya's beliefs on God's power and human creativity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the extreme positions held by the Muzdariyya sect regarding God's ability to lie and oppress, their acceptance of generation (tawallud), and their claim that humans can produce a text comparable to the Quran.

Core Idea
The Muzdariyya claimed God could lie and oppress, and that humans could surpass the Quran.

This lesson introduces the Muzdariyya sect, a fringe group within the Mu'tazila. Their teachings on God's power and the Quran were considered heretical even by mainstream Mu'tazila. We will examine their most controversial claims as recorded by the author.

Guided Path
1
Context of al-Muzdar
Learn about the founder: he was a student of Bishr al-Mu'tamir and known for asceticism.
He was called 'the monk of the Mu'tazila'.
2
First claim: God lies and oppresses
Read al-Muzdar's statement that God is able to lie and oppress, and if He did, He would be a lying, oppressive god. Note the author's immediate refutation.
This view was considered blasphemous.
3
Second claim: Generation (tawallud)
Understand his acceptance that an act can occur from two agents by generation, not directly.
This was a debated concept among the Mu'tazila.
4
Third claim: Imitability of the Quran
Consider his assertion that people can produce something like the Quran or even better in composition and eloquence.
This echoes the view of al-Nazzam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المزدارية هو أبو موسى عيسى بن صبيح المزدار) هذا لقبه وهو من الافتعال من الزيادة (وهو تلميذ بشر) أخذ العلم عنه وتزهد حتى سمي راهب المعتزلة قال الله قادر علي أن يكذب ويظلم ولو فعل لكان إلهاً كاذباً ظالماً، تعالى الله عما قاله علواً كبيراً ، ( ويجوز أن يقع فعل من فاعلين تولداً) لا مباشرة، ( وقال : الناس قادرين على مثل القرآن وأحسن منه نظماً) وبلاغة كما قاله النظام وهو باب
The Muzdariyya: he is Abu Musa 'Isa ibn Subayh al-Muzdar; this is his nickname, derived from 'al-ziyada' (increase). He was a student of Bishr, took knowledge from him, and became ascetic until he was called the monk of the Mu'tazila. He said: God is able to lie and oppress, and if He did, He would be a lying, oppressive god. Exalted is God above what he said, a great exaltation. And it is permissible that an act occur from two agents by generation, not directly. And he said: People are able to produce something like the Quran and better than it in composition and eloquence, as al-Nazzam said. And it is a door (bāb).
Source pages p. 413

Commentary
This passage describes the Muzdariyya sect, named after Abu Musa al-Muzdar, a student of Bishr al-Mu'tamir who was known for his asceticism. His statements on God's power are blasphemous: he claimed God can lie and oppress, and if He did, He would be a lying oppressive god—which the author refutes by exalting God above such claims. Additionally, al-Muzdar accepted the doctrine of generation (tawallud) to the extent that an act can be produced by two agents jointly, not directly. He also asserted, like al-Nazzam, that humans can produce a text equivalent to the Quran or even superior in composition and eloquence. The passage ends with 'وهو باب' which may be the beginning of another section.

Key Terms
كذب
ظلم
توليد
قرآن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the Muzdariyya were simply mainstream Mu'tazila.
Correction: Their view that God can lie and oppress was considered extreme even by other Mu'tazila, and the author strongly refutes it.

Checkpoint
What did al-Muzdar claim about God's ability to lie and oppress?
A) God cannot lie or oppress under any circumstances
B) God is able to lie and oppress, and if He did, He would be a lying, oppressive god
C) God can only lie but not oppress
D) Such attributes are impossible for God

Key Takeaway
The Muzdariyya sect held three controversial positions: that God can lie and oppress, that acts can be generated by two agents, and that humans can produce a text superior to the Quran.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read that al-Muzdar claimed God could lie, does it shake your trust in God's perfection? What thoughts arise in your heart, and how do you combat them with the author's exclamation 'Exalted is God above what he said'? Commit to reciting that phrase whenever doubts about God's attributes creep in.
?
Al-Muzdar believed that an act could be generated by two agents. Think of a recent success you achieved. Did you subconsciously attribute part of it to your own effort separate from God? How does this lesson push you to acknowledge God as the sole creator of all actions? Today, consciously thank God for every act you perform.
?
The Muzdariyya claimed humans could produce something better than the Quran. Have you ever felt that the Quran's language or rulings are outdated or less than perfect? If so, what does this lesson reveal about the arrogance of such thoughts? Take a moment to repent and recite the Quran with the conviction that it is beyond human imitation.

Extremism and the Createdness of the Quran
Ruling on extremism in the createdness of the Quran

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the extreme positions on the createdness of the Quran and how they deviate from Sunni orthodoxy.

Core Idea
Exaggeration in theology leads to false rulings, not truth.

This passage closes the fourth observation with a ruling on extremism. It quotes a figure who overstates the doctrine of the Quran's createdness, making claims that are not accepted in mainstream Islam. Understanding this helps you spot and avoid sectarian distortions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic once, then the English translation. Notice the strong language: 'disbeliever' and exclusion from inheritance.
This passage is a direct quote from an extremist, not the author's own view.
2
Identify the two extremist claims
The passage lists two positions: 1) associating with the ruler makes one a disbeliever, 2) saying actions are created by vision makes one a disbeliever. Recognize that these are presented as exaggerated.
Neither of these is mainstream Sunni belief.
3
Understand the ruling on inheritance
The extremist says that such a person 'does not inherit nor is he inherited from.' This is a legal consequence based on the false claim of disbelief.
Sunni law does not excommunicate based on association with rulers.
4
Contrast with authentic Sunni doctrine
Sunni orthodoxy holds that belief in the createdness of the Quran is not a condition of faith, and excommunication is only for clear denial of essentials.
5
Reflect on the danger of extremism
Consider how taking a valid doctrine too far can lead to false rulings and division. This passage warns against such exaggeration.
The commentary clarifies that these are exaggerated positions condemned by Sunni orthodoxy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنعقد خاتمة للمرصد الرابع الذي بالغ في حدوث القرآن وكفر القائل بقدمه قال : ( ومن لابس السلطان كافر لا يوارث) أي لا يرث ولا يورث منه ، وكذا من قال بخلق الأعمال بالرؤية ) كافراً أيضاً .
A conclusion is held for the fourth observation: he who exaggerated in the createdness of the Quran and declared the one who says it is eternal a disbeliever said: 'And whoever associates with the ruler is a disbeliever; he does not inherit nor is he inherited from.' Likewise, whoever says that actions are created by vision is also a disbeliever.
Source pages p. 414

Commentary
This passage introduces the conclusion (khātimah) of the fourth observation by quoting an extreme figure who went beyond bounds in asserting the createdness of the Quran, even excommunicating those who believe it is eternal. This figure also made a radical political and theological claim: that anyone who associates with the ruler becomes a disbeliever and is excluded from inheritance. The passage further states that holding the belief that actions are created by vision (al-ru'ya) also renders one a disbeliever. The commentary explains that these are exaggerated positions condemned by Sunni orthodoxy.

Key Terms
حدوث القرآن
كفر
لابس السلطان
خلق الأعمال بالرؤية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that the passage represents the Sunni position on these matters.
Correction: The quote is from a specific extremist, not a Sunni ruling; Sunnis do not excommunicate based on association with rulers or on the belief that actions are created by vision.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on someone who says actions are created by vision?
A) They are a disbeliever
B) They are excused
C) They are a sinner
D) They are a believer

Key Takeaway
Extremist positions on the Quran's createdness, such as excommunicating those who associate with rulers or who hold certain beliefs, are not part of Sunni orthodoxy.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever felt that holding a strong theological opinion justified you in judging or even distancing yourself from others who disagree? Reflect on how this lesson warns against such exaggeration and consider one instance in your life where you might have crossed the line from conviction to extremism in thought or action.
?
The extremist in the passage excommunicated those who associate with rulers. Are there people in your life—friends, family, community leaders—whom you have distanced yourself from due to a perceived religious or theological difference? How does this lesson challenge you to reconsider that separation?
?
This passage shows how one exaggeration leads to another, piling false rulings upon false rulings. Where in your own religious practice or thinking have you found yourself slipping from a sound principle into a series of unwarranted conclusions? What is one step you will take today to realign yourself with the broader Sunni ethos of balance and avoiding extremism?

Denial of Divine Names: al-Wakīl and Bringing Hearts Together
Refutes two denials of divine names and actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Hishāmiyya denial of the name al-Wakīl and the concept of God bringing hearts together contradicts the Quran and sound theology.

Core Idea
Denying divine names rebels against Quranic revelation.

The Hishāmiyya sect held extreme views about God's attributes, rejecting certain names and actions explicitly mentioned in the Quran. This lesson examines two of their denials: the name al-Wakīl and the notion that God brings hearts together. We will see how their reasoning fails and how the Quran affirms both.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on al-Wakīl
Read the Arabic text where they refuse to use the name al-Wakīl for God, and the refutation citing Quran 42:6.
Notice they objected because it implies a principal (muwakkil).
2
Understand the refutation
The author explains that al-Wakīl among God's names means al-Ḥafīẓ (the Guardian), not a needy agent.
3
Examine the denial of God bringing hearts together
Read the second part where they forbid saying 'God brought hearts together' despite Quran 8:63.
This denial directly opposes a clear Quranic statement.
4
Reflect on the implications
Consider why denying divine names and actions leads to distorting God's attributes as revealed in the Quran.
This connects to the broader Islamic principle of affirming God's names and attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الهشامية : وهو هشام بن عمر (الغوطي) الذي كان مبالغاً في القدر أكثر من مبالغة سائر المعتزلة ( قالوا : لا يطلق اسم الوكيل على الله مع وروده في القرآن ( لاستدعائه موكلاً)، ولم يعلموا أن الوكيل في أسمائه بمعنى الحفيظ كما في قوله تعالى : وما أنت عليهم بوكيل ﴾ [الشورى : ٦ ] ، ( ولا يقال ألف الله بين القلوب ) مع أنه مخالف لقوله تعالى : ما ألفت بين قلوبهم ولكنَّ الله ألف بينهم ﴾ [الأنفال : ٦٣]، (و) قالوا : ( الأعراض لا تدل على الله (ولا ) على ( رسوله ) أي هي لا تدل على كونه تعالى خالقاً لها، ولا تصلح دلالة على صدق مدعي الرسالة إنما الدال هو الأجسام، ويلزمهم على ذلك أن فلق البحر وقلب العصا حية وإحياء الموتى لا يكون دليلاً على صدق من ظهر على يده (و) قالوا : ( لا دلالة في القرآن على حلال وحرام، والإمامة لا مع الاختلاف) بل لا بد من اتفاق الكل قيل : ومقصودهم الطعن في إمامة أبي بكر إذ كانت بيعته بلا اتفاق من جميع الصحابة لأنه بقي في كل طرف طائفة على خلافه ( والجنة والنار لم تخلقا بعد ) إذ لا فائدة في وجودها الآن ( ولم يحاصر عثمان ولم يقتل) مع كونه متواتراً ( ومن أفسد صلاة في أخرها وقد (افتتحها أولاً) بشروطها ( فأول صلاته معصية منهي عنه مع كونه مخالفاً للإجماع.
The Hishamiyya: he is Hishām b. ʿAmr al-Ghūṭī who was more extreme in [belief in] predestination than the rest of the Muʿtazila. They said: The name al-Wakīl is not applied to God despite its occurrence in the Quran, because it necessitates a principal (muwakkil). They did not know that al-Wakīl among His names means al-Ḥafīẓ (the Guardian), as in His saying: 'And you are not over them a wakīl' (Q. 42:6). And [they said] one should not say 'God brought hearts together' despite this contradicting His saying: 'You did not bring their hearts together, but God brought them together' (Q. 8:63). And they said: Accidents do not indicate God nor His messenger, meaning they do not indicate that He is their Creator, nor are they suitable as evidence for the truthfulness of a claimant to prophethood; only bodies indicate. This entails for them that the splitting of the sea, the turning of the staff into a serpent, and the reviving of the dead would not be evidence for the truthfulness of the one through whom they occurred. And they said: There is no indication in the Quran of lawful and unlawful, and the imamate is not [established] with disagreement; rather, consensus of all is necessary. It is said: Their intent was to impugn the imamate of Abū Bakr, since his pledge was without consensus of all companions because a group in each faction remained in opposition to him. And [they said] Paradise and Hell have not been created yet, since there is no benefit in their existence now. And [they said] ʿUthmān was not besieged nor killed, despite it being mutawātir. And [they said] whoever corrupts a prayer at its end, having begun it correctly with its conditions, then the beginning of his prayer is disobedience forbidden, despite it being contrary to consensus.
Source pages p. 414

Commentary
This passage enumerates the deviant beliefs of the Hishāmiyya sect, founded by Hishām b. ʿAmr al-Ghūṭī, who was more extreme in qadar (predestination) than other Muʿtazila. The text first refutes their denial of applying the name al-Wakīl to God, noting that it occurs in the Quran and means 'Guardian.' Next, it mentions their rejection of the phrase 'God brought hearts together' despite its occurrence in the Quran (Q. 8:63). Then it discusses their claim that accidents (aʿrāḍ) do not indicate God or His messenger, meaning they do not serve as proof of creation or prophethood; the author points out that this would negate miracles like the splitting of the sea. They also deny that the Quran indicates lawful and unlawful, and they reject the imamate if there is any disagreement, targeting Abū Bakr's election. They claim Paradise and Hell are not yet created, deny the siege and murder of ʿUthmān, and hold a strange view about prayer nullification.

Key Terms
الهشامية
الوكيل
الحفيظ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Hishāmiyya thought that applying the name al-Wakīl to God implies He has a principal or needs delegation, and that saying 'God brought hearts together' is impermissible.
Correction: Al-Wakīl in God's names means the Guardian, not a deputized agent, and the Quran explicitly states that God brought hearts together (Q. 8:63).

Checkpoint
Why did the Hishāmiyya reject the name al-Wakīl for God?
A) It is not found in the Quran
B) It necessitates a principal (muwakkil)
C) It implies weakness in God
D) It is a synonym for 'helper'

Key Takeaway
The Quran itself affirms the names and actions that the Hishāmiyya denied, proving their position is untenable.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Hishāmiyya rejected a divine name because it seemed to them to imply a flaw in God. Have you ever subtly doubted a divine attribute because your own logic found it difficult to accept? What will you do to submit your intellect to the Quran when it clashes with your reasoning?
?
They also forbade saying 'God brought hearts together' despite the clear Quranic statement. Is there any teaching in your heart that you resist because it doesn't fit your personal experience of God? Will you now surrender that resistance and let the Quran speak?
?
The Hishāmiyya were learned and pious, yet they fell into error by prioritizing their own analogies over revelation. What intellectual pride do you harbor that could lead you to the same mistake? How will you actively guard against it starting today?

Denial of Miracles: Accidents Do Not Indicate God or His Messenger
Refutes the claim that accidents do not indicate God or His messenger.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Hishāmiyya's claim that accidents do not indicate God or His messenger leads to the denial of miracles and prophethood.

Core Idea
Rejecting miracles as evidence undermines the proof of prophethood.

The Hishāmiyya held a peculiar view that accidents (aʿrāḍ) do not indicate God or His messenger. This lesson unpacks their argument and shows its absurd consequence: that clear miracles like the splitting of the sea and reviving the dead would not prove prophethood. The author points out this logical flaw.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on accidents
Read the Arabic text where they claim accidents do not indicate God or His messenger.
Notice they specify accidents do not show God is their Creator nor serve as evidence for prophethood.
2
Identify the consequence
The author draws the necessary implication: if accidents don't indicate, then miracles would not be evidence for the prophet through whom they occurred.
Examples given: splitting the sea, staff turning into serpent, reviving the dead.
3
Reflect on the contradiction
Consider that miracles are precisely accidents that prove prophethood. Denying their indicative power destroys the very basis for believing in prophets.
This shows the Hishāmiyya's position is self-defeating.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

?
If accidents (like miracles) could not point to truth, then every sign of God's power in your life—every answered prayer, every provision, every moment of guidance—would be meaningless. Do you treat these 'accidents' as mere coincidences, or as clear signs pointing you to your Creator? What would it take for you to start seeing them as evidence, not just events?
?
The Hishāmiyya claimed that only bodies indicate, not accidents. But miracles are accidents—temporary, extraordinary events. Have you ever dismissed a spiritual experience or a clear sign from Allah because it was 'just a feeling' or 'just a coincidence' rather than a solid, permanent thing? Repent today for undervaluing His signs.
?
This lesson shows that rejecting accidents as evidence leads to denying the proofs of prophethood. Are you willing to follow the logical consequences of your beliefs, even if they are uncomfortable? Or do you hold opinions that, if fully carried out, would undermine your faith? Commit to abandoning any thought that contradicts the clear evidence Allah has placed in His creation.

Denial of Quranic Guidance and Imamate Conditions
Refutes denial of Quranic legal indication and extreme imamate condition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Hishāmiyya's denial that the Quran indicates lawful and unlawful, and their extreme condition for the imamate requiring complete consensus.

Core Idea
Rejecting Quranic authority and requiring perfect consensus undermines Islamic law and leadership.

In this lesson, we examine two more radical views of the Hishāmiyya: their claim that the Quran provides no indication of what is lawful and unlawful, and their insistence that the imamate is not valid unless there is unanimous agreement from all Muslims. The author notes that the latter aimed to challenge Abu Bakr's caliphate.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on Quranic indication
Read the Arabic where they say the Quran has no indication of halal and haram.
This position denies a fundamental function of the Quran.
2
Read the passage on imamate
Read their condition that the imamate requires complete consensus (no disagreement).
The author suggests this was a tactic to invalidate Abu Bakr's election.
3
Analyze the target
Understand that requiring absolute consensus is impractical and historically targeted Abu Bakr's caliphate, which had some opposition.
This reveals their sectarian motive.

According to the Hishāmiyya, what condition is necessary for the imamate to be valid?
A) Majority vote

D) Selection by the Quraysh

Key Takeaway
Denying Quranic legal guidance and imposing an impossible condition for leadership are tools to undermine established Islamic authority.

?

?
The Hishāmiyya used an impossible condition to reject legitimate authority. Are you guilty of setting impossible standards for yourself or others to avoid obeying Allah? What is one area where you need to lower your guard and accept truth?
?
The ulterior motive behind the Hishāmiyya's claim was political. Is there a belief you hold that actually serves your ego or worldly interests rather than sincere submission? How can you purify your intention today?

beginner
