Denial of Creation of Paradise, Hell, and Uthman's Siege
Refutes denial of created Paradise/Hell and historical siege of Uthman.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Hishāmiyya's denial that Paradise and Hell have been created and their denial of the historical siege and murder of Uthman.

Core Idea
Denying created Paradise and Hell and historical events contradicts clear Quranic and transmitted evidence.

The Hishāmiyya held that Paradise and Hell have not yet been created, claiming no benefit in their existence now. They also denied the well-known historical events of the siege and murder of Caliph Uthman. This lesson examines these denials and their inconsistency with the Quran and mutawātir reports.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on Paradise and Hell
Read the Arabic where they claim Paradise and Hell are not yet created, giving a reason.
Their reason: no benefit in their existence now.
2
Read the denial of Uthman's siege
Read their denial that Uthman was besieged and killed, despite it being mutawātir.
Note that 'mutawātir' means widely transmitted, making denial impossible.
3
Reflect on the pattern
Observe a pattern: rejecting what is established by revelation or reliable history.
This shows a tendency to contradict consensus (ijmāʿ) and clear evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الهشامية : وهو هشام بن عمر (الغوطي) الذي كان مبالغاً في القدر أكثر من مبالغة سائر المعتزلة ( قالوا : لا يطلق اسم الوكيل على الله مع وروده في القرآن ( لاستدعائه موكلاً)، ولم يعلموا أن الوكيل في أسمائه بمعنى الحفيظ كما في قوله تعالى : وما أنت عليهم بوكيل ﴾ [الشورى : ٦ ] ، ( ولا يقال ألف الله بين القلوب ) مع أنه مخالف لقوله تعالى : ما ألفت بين قلوبهم ولكنَّ الله ألف بينهم ﴾ [الأنفال : ٦٣]، (و) قالوا : ( الأعراض لا تدل على الله (ولا ) على ( رسوله ) أي هي لا تدل على كونه تعالى خالقاً لها، ولا تصلح دلالة على صدق مدعي الرسالة إنما الدال هو الأجسام، ويلزمهم على ذلك أن فلق البحر وقلب العصا حية وإحياء الموتى لا يكون دليلاً على صدق من ظهر على يده (و) قالوا : ( لا دلالة في القرآن على حلال وحرام، والإمامة لا مع الاختلاف) بل لا بد من اتفاق الكل قيل : ومقصودهم الطعن في إمامة أبي بكر إذ كانت بيعته بلا اتفاق من جميع الصحابة لأنه بقي في كل طرف طائفة على خلافه ( والجنة والنار لم تخلقا بعد ) إذ لا فائدة في وجودها الآن ( ولم يحاصر عثمان ولم يقتل) مع كونه متواتراً ( ومن أفسد صلاة في أخرها وقد (افتتحها أولاً) بشروطها ( فأول صلاته معصية منهي عنه مع كونه مخالفاً للإجماع.
The Hishamiyya: he is Hishām b. ʿAmr al-Ghūṭī who was more extreme in [belief in] predestination than the rest of the Muʿtazila. They said: The name al-Wakīl is not applied to God despite its occurrence in the Quran, because it necessitates a principal (muwakkil). They did not know that al-Wakīl among His names means al-Ḥafīẓ (the Guardian), as in His saying: 'And you are not over them a wakīl' (Q. 42:6). And [they said] one should not say 'God brought hearts together' despite this contradicting His saying: 'You did not bring their hearts together, but God brought them together' (Q. 8:63). And they said: Accidents do not indicate God nor His messenger, meaning they do not indicate that He is their Creator, nor are they suitable as evidence for the truthfulness of a claimant to prophethood; only bodies indicate. This entails for them that the splitting of the sea, the turning of the staff into a serpent, and the reviving of the dead would not be evidence for the truthfulness of the one through whom they occurred. And they said: There is no indication in the Quran of lawful and unlawful, and the imamate is not [established] with disagreement; rather, consensus of all is necessary. It is said: Their intent was to impugn the imamate of Abū Bakr, since his pledge was without consensus of all companions because a group in each faction remained in opposition to him. And [they said] Paradise and Hell have not been created yet, since there is no benefit in their existence now. And [they said] ʿUthmān was not besieged nor killed, despite it being mutawātir. And [they said] whoever corrupts a prayer at its end, having begun it correctly with its conditions, then the beginning of his prayer is disobedience forbidden, despite it being contrary to consensus.
Source pages p. 414

Commentary
This passage enumerates the deviant beliefs of the Hishāmiyya sect, founded by Hishām b. ʿAmr al-Ghūṭī, who was more extreme in qadar (predestination) than other Muʿtazila. The text first refutes their denial of applying the name al-Wakīl to God, noting that it occurs in the Quran and means 'Guardian.' Next, it mentions their rejection of the phrase 'God brought hearts together' despite its occurrence in the Quran (Q. 8:63). Then it discusses their claim that accidents (aʿrāḍ) do not indicate God or His messenger, meaning they do not serve as proof of creation or prophethood; the author points out that this would negate miracles like the splitting of the sea. They also deny that the Quran indicates lawful and unlawful, and they reject the imamate if there is any disagreement, targeting Abū Bakr's election. They claim Paradise and Hell are not yet created, deny the siege and murder of ʿUthmān, and hold a strange view about prayer nullification.

Key Terms
الجنة
النار
الخلق
عثمان
متواتر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Paradise and Hell are not created yet; Uthman was not besieged or killed.
Correction: The Quran indicates Paradise and Hell are already created (e.g., 3:133, 3:131), and the siege of Uthman is a historical fact transmitted by many reliable sources.

Checkpoint
What reason did the Hishāmiyya give for denying the creation of Paradise and Hell?
A) They are spiritual states
B) No benefit in their existence now
C) They are only metaphors
D) They will be created after Judgment

Key Takeaway
Denying the creation of the afterlife realms and established historical events undermines both revelation and reliable testimony.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read that the Hishamiyya denied the creation of Paradise and Hell because they saw 'no benefit in their existence now', do you find yourself ever treating the afterlife as distant or irrelevant to your daily choices? How would your life change if you truly believed Paradise and Hell are already created and waiting?
?
The Hishamiyya denied the siege of Uthman despite it being mutawātir. Are there any parts of Islamic history or teachings that you find yourself hesitant to accept? What does this lesson demand of you regarding trust in the collective transmission of the Ummah?
?
If you were to apply the same skepticism to a well-established sunnah or aqeedah principle as the Hishamiyya did to these two matters, where would that lead you? Are you willing to submit to what is certain, even when it challenges your personal reasoning?

Perverse Ruling on Prayer Nullification
Refutes a ruling that retroactively invalidates the beginning of a prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Hishāmiyya's ruling that corrupting the end of a prayer makes the entire beginning of the prayer sinful, and why this is contrary to scholarly consensus.

Core Idea
Invalidating the whole prayer due to a later corruption contradicts sound fiqh principles.

The final doctrine of the Hishāmiyya listed here concerns a ruling about prayer. They claimed that if someone corrupts the end of a prayer after having started it correctly, then the entire beginning part becomes an act of disobedience. This lesson unpacks this strange ruling and shows how it violates the consensus of scholars that each part of prayer is evaluated independently unless nullified by a condition.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on prayer
Read the Arabic text concerning the person who corrupts the end of a prayer after starting correctly.
Notice their conclusion: the beginning of the prayer becomes sin.
2
Understand the implication
They are retroactively declaring the valid parts as sinful, which is unjust and inconsistent with usual fiqh principles.
Normally, only the invalid action affects the later parts, not the earlier valid parts.
3
Note the consensus
The author states this is against ijmāʿ (consensus).
Scholars agree that valid actions remain valid unless a nullifier occurs before completion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If the end of a prayer is corrupted, the entire prayer from the beginning becomes sinful.

A) It remains valid

The Hishāmiyya's prayer ruling is an example of legal extremism that contradicts the consensus of Muslim scholars.

?

?

?
If a mistake in your worship later made you feel that your entire earlier devotion was worthless, what would you remind yourself using this lesson? How does knowing that the valid beginning remains valid affect your trust in Allah's acceptance of your efforts?

The Ṣāliḥiyya Sect: Disallowed Views on Attributes and Substance
Lists the deviant beliefs of the followers of al-Ṣāliḥī.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two key doctrines of the Ṣāliḥiyya sect and their theological implications for Ashʿarī thought.

Core Idea
The Ṣāliḥiyya claimed attributes can subsist in the dead, undermining divine uniqueness.

In this passage, al-Ījī introduces the Ṣāliḥiyya, a sect that held two extreme positions. First, they asserted that attributes like knowledge and power can exist in a dead person. Second, they believed a substance could be completely free of accidents. Both views violate core Ashʿarī principles about the nature of attributes and life.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the literal translation. Let the author's words set the stage.
Notice the compact style: two doctrines stated concisely.
2
Identify the two doctrines
Find the two distinct positions: (1) permitting attributes to subsist in the dead, and (2) permitting a substance to be devoid of all accidents. Write them down.
Doctrine (1) is about attributes; doctrine (2) is about substance and accidents.
3
Examine the logical entailment
The author points out that if attributes can be in the dead, then it follows that people could be dead while having attributes, and that God might not be living. Reflect on why this is problematic.
This entailment shows the absurdity of the first doctrine.
4
Connect to Sunni theology
Consider why Ashʿarīs reject these views: life is a necessary attribute for the subject of attributes like knowledge and power; only Allah is necessarily living.
Also, substances always have accidents in the Ashʿarī framework.
5
Test your understanding
Answer the checkpoint question to confirm your grasp of the main point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الصالحية: أصحاب الصالحي ) ومن مذهبهم أنهم ) جوزوا قيام العلم والقدرة والإرادة والسمع والبصر بالميت، ويلزمهم جواز أن يكون الناس مع اتصافهم بهذه الصفات أمواتاً وأن لا يكون الباري تعالى حيا (و) جوزوا ( خلو الجوهر عن الأعراض كلها. )
The Ṣāliḥiyya: the followers of al-Ṣāliḥī. Among their doctrines is that they permitted the subsistence of knowledge, power, will, hearing, and sight in the dead. This entails for them the possibility that people, while being described with these attributes, could be dead, and that the Creator (al-Bārī) might not be living. And they permitted the substance (jawhar) to be devoid of all accidents.
Source pages p. 414

Commentary
This passage describes the Ṣāliḥiyya sect, followers of al-Ṣāliḥī. They held an extreme view that attributes like knowledge, power, will, hearing, and sight could subsist in a dead person. The author notes the logical consequence: if attributes can exist in the dead, then people could be dead while having these attributes, and conversely, the Creator might not be living. Additionally, they claimed that a substance could exist without any accidents, which contradicts the standard Ashʿarī view that substances are always accompanied by accidents.

Key Terms
الصالحية
قيام الصفات بالميت
الجوهر
الأعراض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: It is possible for attributes like knowledge and power to subsist in a dead person.
Correction: In Sunni theology, attributes require a living subject; only God is necessarily living, and His attributes are inseparable from His essence.

Checkpoint
What did the Ṣāliḥiyya permit regarding attributes?
A) Only knowledge in the dead
B) Subsistence of knowledge, power, will, hearing, and sight in the dead
C) Attributes only in living beings
D) None of the above

Key Takeaway
The Ṣāliḥiyya's views on attributes and substance were rejected because they blur the distinction between the living Creator and His creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you believed that attributes like knowledge and power could exist independently of life, how would that affect your trust that God alone is the source of all knowledge and power? Have you ever acted as if you own your abilities without needing the One who gives them moment by moment? This week, consciously remind yourself every morning that every quality you have is a gift from the ever-living God.
?
The Ṣāliḥiyya claimed that a substance could be devoid of all accidents. If a thing has no qualities at all, what distinguishes it from nothing? When you look at your own life, do you ever feel like you are just going through the motions, empty of meaning? That feeling is a sign that you are a contingent being in need of constant divine filling. Resolve today to ask Allah to fill your 'substance' with the 'accidents' of faith and good deeds.
?
This lesson reveals that some sects blurred the line between Creator and creation by allowing attributes in the dead. How often do you blur that line in your daily thoughts—for example, by fearing a human more than Allah, or by seeking knowledge from a source that does not ultimately come from Allah? Commit to checking your heart each night: where have I placed something created in the position that only the Creator should hold?

The Habitiyya Sect: Two Gods and Misinterpretation
Lists the deviant beliefs of Aḥmad b. Ḥābiṭ and his followers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the deviant beliefs of the Habitiyya sect, including their doctrine of two gods and their misinterpretation of scriptural texts.

Core Idea
The Habitiyya claimed there are two gods: an eternal God and a temporal Messiah.

This passage introduces the Habitiyya sect, followers of Aḥmad b. Ḥābiṭ, who held extreme beliefs about the nature of God and Christ. They claimed the world has two gods and interpreted Quranic verses about God's coming as referring to Christ. Al-Āmidī refuted them as disbelievers and polytheists.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sect and its founder
Read the first part of the passage to learn who Aḥmad b. Ḥābiṭ was and his connection to al-Naẓẓām.
Note that the sect is named after his father.
2
Understand the two-god doctrine
Focus on the statement that the world has two gods: an eternal one (God) and a temporal one (the Messiah). Recognize the deviance of this belief.
This is a clear violation of tawḥīd.
3
Examine their scriptural misinterpretations
Look at how they interpret Quranic verses and hadith to support their claim that the Messiah is the one who comes in judgment, creates bodies, etc.
Compare their interpretations with orthodox understanding.
4
Review the refutation by al-Āmidī
Note that al-Āmidī declares them disbelievers and polytheists, showing the gravity of their error.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحابطية : هو أحمد بن حابط نسب أتباعه إلى أبيه وهو ( من أصحاب النظام قالوا للعالم إلهان قديم هو الله تعالى ومحدث هو المسيح، والمسيح ( هو الذي : يحاسب الناس في الآخرة) وهو المراد بقوله : وجاء ربك والملك صفاً صفاً الفجر : ۲۲ ] ، وهو الذي يأتي في ظلل من الغمام ﴾ [البقرة : ٢١٠ ] ، وهو المعني بقوله عليه السلام: إن الله خلق آدم على صورته، وقوله : « يضع الجبار قدمه في النار وإنما سمي المسيح لأنه أبدع الأجسام وأحدثها قال الآمدي : وهؤلاء كفار مشركون .
The Ḥābiṭiyya: he is Aḥmad b. Ḥābiṭ, his followers attributed to his father, and he was among the followers of al-Naẓẓām. They said: The world has two gods: an eternal one, God Most High, and a temporal one, the Messiah. The Messiah is the one who will judge people in the Hereafter, and he is meant by His saying: 'And your Lord comes, and the angels, rank upon rank' (Q. 89:22), and he is the one who comes in 'shades of clouds' (Q. 2:210), and he is meant by his saying (peace be upon him): 'Indeed God created Adam in His image,' and his saying: 'The Almighty will place His foot in the Fire.' He was called the Messiah because he innovated bodies and originated them. al-Āmidī said: These are disbelievers and polytheists.
Source pages p. 414

Commentary
This passage presents the Ḥābiṭiyya sect, followers of Aḥmad b. Ḥābiṭ, a student of al-Naẓẓām. They believed in two gods: an eternal one (God) and a temporal one (the Messiah, Jesus). They claimed the Messiah will judge people on the Last Day, interpreting Quranic verses about God's coming and the angels as referring to the Messiah. They also interpreted the hadith about Adam being created in God's image and the 'foot in the Fire' as referring to the Messiah. Al-Āmidī responded by declaring them disbelievers and polytheists.

Key Terms
الحابطية
إلهان
المسيح
الآخرة
كفار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The belief that the Messiah (Jesus) is a temporal god who will judge humanity, and that Quranic verses about God's coming actually refer to the Messiah.
Correction: In orthodox Islam, there is only one eternal God, and the Messiah is a prophet, not a deity. The verses about God's coming refer to God Himself, not to any created being.

Checkpoint
According to the Ḥābiṭiyya, who is the temporal god?
A) The Holy Spirit
B) The Messiah
C) The Prophet Muhammad
D) The angel Gabriel

Key Takeaway
The Ḥābiṭiyya sect was condemned for associating a partner with God by elevating Christ to a temporal deity, a clear violation of tawḥīd.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read that the Ḥābiṭiyya attributed the coming of Allah on the Day of Judgment to the Messiah, are there any verses you have subtly reinterpreted to avoid submitting to their clear meaning? What would it cost you to accept them as they are?
?
The Ḥābiṭiyya gave the Messiah the power to judge and create. Is there any created being in your life whose approval or judgment you fear more than Allah's? How can you realign your heart to fear Him alone?
?
Al-Āmidī declared them disbelievers without hesitation. If you were in his place, would you have the courage to call such a deviation by its true name, even if it meant opposing others? Examine your own attachments to people or opinions that might cloud your commitment to tawḥīd.

The Ḥadathiyya Sect: Reincarnation and Divine Testing
Lists the deviant beliefs of Faḍl al-Ḥadathī, including reincarnation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the doctrine of the Ḥadathiyya sect, including their belief in reincarnation and the moral responsibility of animals.

Core Idea
The Ḥadathiyya believed animals are reincarnated souls being tested for past sins.

The Ḥadathiyya sect, named after its founder Faḍl al-Ḥadathī, adopted the beliefs of the Ḥābiṭiyya but added two distinctive doctrines: reincarnation (al-tanāsukh) and the moral responsibility of animals. Their complex cosmology explains how souls are reborn in different forms based on their deeds. Let us examine their views as presented in the text.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage carefully along with the English translation. Notice the structure: the author begins by naming the sect and its founder, then states their addition to the Ḥābiṭiyya doctrine, and then elaborates their cosmology.
Pay attention to the three categories of beings based on obedience.
2
Identify the three groups of creation
The passage describes that God created rational animals in another realm, tested them, and then divided them into three groups: the fully obedient (kept in bliss), the fully disobedient (sent to hell), and the partially obedient (sent to this world in various forms).
This is the core of their belief.
3
Understand the cycle of reincarnation
The partially obedient group undergoes reincarnation: they are given different bodies (human, animal) according to the degree of their sins. The cycle continues until all sins are expiated. The author concludes this is exactly reincarnation.
This contradicts Islamic eschatology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحدثية : هو فضل الحدثي ) ومذهبهم مذهب الحابطية إلا أنهم ) زادوا التناسخ وأن كل حيوان مكلف فإنهم قالوا : إن الله سبحانه وتعالى أبدع الحيوانات عقلاء بالغين في دار سوى هذه الدار وخلق فيهم معرفته والعلم به وأسبغ عليهم نعمه ثم ابتلاهم وكلفهم شكر نعمته فأطاعه بعض فأقرهم في دار النعيم التي ابتدأهم فيها وعصاه بعض في الجميع فأخرجهم من تلك الدار إلى دار العذاب وهي النار، وأطاعه بعض في البعض دون البعض فأخرجهم إلى دار الدنيا وكساهم هذه الأجساد الكثيفة على صور مختلفة كصورة الإنسان وسائر الحيوانات، وابتلاهم بالبأساء والضراء والآلام واللذات على مقادير ذنوبهم، فمن كان معاصيه أقل وطاعاته أكثر كانت صورته أحسن وآلامه أقل، ومن كان بالعكس فبالعكس ولا يزال يكون الحيوان في الدنيا في صورة بعد صورة ما دامت معه ذنوبه وهذا عين القول بالتناسخ .
The Ḥadathiyya: he is Faḍl al-Ḥadathī. Their doctrine is the doctrine of the Ḥābiṭiyya except that they added reincarnation (al-tanāsukh) and that every animal is morally responsible. They said: God, glorified and exalted, originated animals as rational, mature beings in an abode other than this world, and created in them knowledge of Him and awareness of Him, and lavished His blessings on them, then tested them and charged them with gratitude for His blessing. Some obeyed Him, so He kept them in the abode of bliss in which He had originally placed them. Some disobeyed Him completely, so He removed them from that abode to the abode of punishment, which is the Fire. And some obeyed Him partially and disobeyed partially, so He removed them to the world of this life, and clothed them with these dense bodies in various forms like the form of humans and other animals. He tested them with hardship, harm, pains, and pleasures according to the extent of their sins. So whoever had fewer sins and more obedience had a better form and less pain, and whoever had the opposite had the opposite. The animal continues in the world in one form after another as long as sins remain with it. This is exactly the doctrine of reincarnation.
Source pages p. 414

Commentary
This passage describes the Ḥadathiyya sect, followers of Faḍl al-Ḥadathī, who adopted the beliefs of the Ḥābiṭiyya but added reincarnation (al-tanāsukh) and the idea that all animals are morally accountable. They held a complex cosmology: God first created rational animals in another realm, tested them, and then based on their obedience or disobedience, either kept them in bliss, sent them to hell, or placed them in the world as humans or animals in different forms according to their sins. The cycle of rebirth continues until sins are expiated. The author concludes that this is precisely the doctrine of reincarnation, which is rejected in Islam.

Key Terms
الحدثية
التناسخ
التكليف
الحيوان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That reincarnation is compatible with Islamic teachings of resurrection and judgment.
Correction: Classical Sunni Islam holds that souls are judged once after death and then consigned to Paradise or Hell. Reincarnation, as believed by the Ḥadathiyya, is a rejected innovation.

Checkpoint
What did the Ḥadathiyya add to the Ḥābiṭiyya doctrine?
A) Belief in two gods
B) Reincarnation and moral responsibility of animals
C) Denial of the afterlife
D) That God is not all-powerful

Key Takeaway
The Ḥadathiyya sect believed animals are reincarnated souls being tested for past sins, a doctrine rejected in Islam.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you witness suffering in animals, does your heart immediately seek refuge in the finality of Allah's judgment, or do you find yourself tempted to question His justice as the Ḥadathiyya did? What does your reaction reveal about the depth of your trust in His wisdom?
?
The Ḥadathiyya believed that partial obedience earns a better form in the next life. In what ways do you secretly treat your obedience to Allah as a transaction for worldly gain, forgetting that your final abode rests on His mercy, not on a cycle of deeds?

The Mu'ammariyya Sect: Denial of God's Creation of Bodies
Presents the Mu'ammariyya's denial of God's creation of bodies and their theory of accident causation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'ammariyya's view that God did not create bodies and that bodies themselves invent accidents, as well as the logical inconsistency in their position.

Core Idea
Mu'ammariyya claimed bodies create their own accidents—contradicting their own view of bodies as originated.

The Mu'ammariyya sect, founded by Mu'ammar b. 'Abbad al-Sulami, held extreme views on causality. They denied that God creates bodies, instead attributing the origination of accidents to bodies themselves. This lesson examines their claim and the internal contradiction noted by scholars.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on bodies and accidents
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Note the two modes of accident production and the objection.
Pay attention to the words 'طبعاً' and 'اختياراً'.
2
Identify the two types of accident production
The passage states bodies invent accidents either by nature (like fire burning) or by choice (like animals producing colors). Understand the distinction.
3
Analyze the logical inconsistency
The author points out that the origination and annihilation of bodies are themselves accidents according to Mu'ammar. Ask: how can a body cause its own origination if it doesn't yet exist?
This reveals a contradiction in their theory.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المعمرية : هو معمر بن عباد السلمي قالوا : الله لم يخلق شيئاً من الأجسام، أما الأعراض فتخترعها الأجسام إما طبعاً كالنار للإحراق والشمس للحرارة، وإما اختياراً كالحيوان للألوان قيل : ومن العجب أن حدوث الأجسام وفناءها عند معمر من الأعراض فكيف يقول : إنها من فعل الأجسام، (و) قالوا : ( لا يوصف) الله (بالقدم) لأنه يدل على التقادم الزماني والله سبحانه ليس بزماني ) ولا يعلم الله نفسه وإلا اتحد العالم والمعلوم وهو ممتنع ) والإنسان لا فعل له غير (الإرادة مباشرة كانت أو توليداً بناء على ما ذهبوا إليه من مذهب الفلاسفة في حقيقة الإنسان.
The Muʿammariyya: he is Muʿammar b. ʿAbbād al-Sulamī. They said: God did not create any of the bodies. As for accidents, bodies invent them, either by nature, like fire for burning and the sun for heat, or by choice, like animals for colors. It is said: Among the wonders is that, according to Muʿammar, the origination and annihilation of bodies are accidents, so how can he say that they are the actions of bodies? And they said: God is not described with pre-eternity (al-qidam) because it indicates temporal priority, and God is not temporal. And God does not know Himself, otherwise the knower and the known would be one, which is impossible. And man has no act other than will, whether directly or by generation (tawlīd), based on what they adopted from the philosophers' doctrine regarding the reality of man.
Source pages p. 415

Commentary
This passage presents the Muʿammariyya sect, followers of Muʿammar b. ʿAbbād al-Sulamī. They held that God did not create bodies; rather, bodies themselves invent accidents, either naturally or by choice. The author points out an inconsistency: if the origination and annihilation of bodies are accidents (as Muʿammar claims), then bodies cannot be the doers of those accidents since they would need to exist before the accidents. They also denied that God is described as 'pre-eternal' (qadīm) because that implies temporal priority, whereas God is not temporal. They denied God's knowledge of Himself on the grounds that it would result in the unity of knower and known (a philosophical argument). Finally, they reduced human action to mere will (irāda), following the philosophers' view of human nature.

Key Terms
المعمرية
الأجسام
الأعراض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that bodies can create their own accidents independently of God.
Correction: Sunni theology holds that God is the sole creator of all substances and accidents.

Checkpoint
According to the Mu'ammariyya, who or what creates accidents?
A) God
B) Bodies
C) Angels
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
The Mu'ammariyya's claim that bodies create accidents contradicts their own view that bodies' existence is itself an accident.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever held onto a belief about God that, upon deeper reflection, you realized was self-contradictory? What did you do when you saw the inconsistency? Are you willing to abandon a comfortable but flawed understanding of God for the sake of truth?
?
This passage exposes the danger of intellectual pride—Mu'ammar denied God's creation to uphold his own theory. In what area of your life might you be resisting a clear truth from revelation because it conflicts with your own reasoning or desires? What would it cost you to submit?
?
The source shows that even a small inconsistency in theology can unravel the entire system. Consider your own understanding of tawhid: is it built on the firm foundation of revelation, or on human speculation that might contain hidden contradictions? What step will you take today to strengthen your foundation?

The Mu'ammariyya Sect: Denial of Divine Pre-Eternity and Self-Knowledge
Lists the Mu'ammariyya's denials of divine pre-eternity, self-knowledge, and their theory of human will.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'ammariyya's rejection of God's attribute of pre-eternity (al-qidam) and His knowledge of Himself, along with their view on human action.

Core Idea
Mu'ammariyya denied God's pre-eternity and self-knowledge, and reduced human action to mere will.

Beyond denying God's creation of bodies, the Mu'ammariyya also rejected other essential divine attributes. They argued that describing God as 'pre-eternal' (qadīm) implies temporal priority, which is inappropriate for God, and that God cannot know Himself because it would entail unity of knower and known. This lesson examines these claims and their view that human action is nothing but will.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on divine attributes and human action
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Identify the three distinct claims made by the Mu'ammariyya.
2
Analyze the denial of pre-eternity
They argue that 'qadīm' implies temporal priority, which does not apply to God. Understand why this is a misunderstanding of the term in theology.
Sunnis use 'qadīm' to mean 'eternal without beginning', not temporally prior.
3
Examine the denial of self-knowledge
Their argument: if God knows Himself, the knower and known are one, which they deem impossible. Reflect on why this reasoning is flawed according to Sunni theology.
4
Consider the reduction of human action
They claim man's only act is will, following philosophers. Note how this limits human responsibility.
This view is similar to occasionalism but with a different emphasis.

Finally, they reduced human action to mere will (irāda), following the philosophers' view of human nature.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: It is often thought that God cannot be described as 'qadīm' because it implies time.
Correction: Sunni scholars affirm that God is qadīm in the sense of being eternal without beginning, not temporally prior.

What reason did the Mu'ammariyya give for denying that God knows Himself?

B) It would unite the knower and the known, which is impossible
C) God only knows universals, not particulars

Key Takeaway
The Mu'ammariyya's denial of God's pre-eternity and self-knowledge stems from a misunderstanding of divine attributes, and their view of human action follows philosophical determinism.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you describe Allah as 'Pre-eternal', do you ever unconsciously imagine Him as existing within time? What steps will you take to purify your understanding of Allah's timelessness?
?
The Mu'ammariyya denied that Allah knows Himself. Do you truly believe that Allah knows Himself perfectly, and how does that belief shape your confidence that He knows you?
?
Do you ever live as though your will alone determines your actions, forgetting that Allah is the Creator of your deeds? In one specific area this week, how will you affirm your dependence on Allah's power?

The Thumāmiyya's Denial of Agency for Generated Acts
Thumāma's argument that generated acts have no agent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Thumāmiyya's argument that generated acts have no agent and why Sunni theologians reject it.

Core Idea
According to the Thumāmiyya, generated acts have no agent—neither human nor divine.

The Thumāmiyya sect, founded by Thumāma b. Ashras, held a radical view on causality. They argued that so-called 'generated acts' (such as the arrow hitting its target after the archer's death) cannot be attributed to any agent. This lesson examines their reasoning and the theological implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice how Thumāma's argument unfolds in two parts: first against human agency, then against divine agency.
2
Identify the two halves of the argument
The argument uses a dilemma: if attributed to a human agent, the agent might be dead; if attributed to God, God would be responsible for evil.
3
Consider the Sunni response
Reflect on why this view contradicts Sunni beliefs about God's omnipotence and human moral responsibility.
Sunni scholars affirm that all acts are from God as Creator, but humans acquire them.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثمامية: هو ثمامة بن أشرس (النميري) كان جامعاً بين سخافة الدين وخلاعة النفس، قالوا : الأفعال المتولدة لا ( فاعل لها إذ لا يمكن إسنادها إلى فاعل لاستلزامه إسناد الفعل إلى الميت فيما إذا رمى سهما إلى شخص ومات قبل وصوله إليه ولا إلى الله تعالى لاستلزامه صدور القبيح عنه ( والمعرفة متولدة من النظر وإنها واجبة قبل الشرع واليهود والنصارى والمجوس والزنادقة يصيرون في الآخرة ( تراباً لا يدخلون جنة ولا ناراً وكذا البهائم والأطفال، والاستطاعة سلامة الآلة وهي قبل الفعل ( ومن لا يعلم خالقه الكفار معذور والمعارف كلها ضرورية ولا فعل للإنسان غير الإرادة وما عداها حادث بلا محدث والعالم فعل الله بطبعه كأنهم أرادوا به ما يقوله الفلاسفة من الإيجاب ويلزمه قدم العالم، وكان ثمامة في زمان المأمون وله عنده منزلة
The Thumāmiyya: he is Thumāma b. Ashras al-Numayrī. He combined religious frivolity and dissolute character. They said: Generated acts (al-afʿāl al-mutawallada) have no agent, because it is impossible to attribute them to an agent: attributing them to the agent would entail attributing the act to a dead person if he shot an arrow at someone and died before it reached him, and attributing them to God would entail the occurrence of evil from Him. And knowledge is generated from reflection (al-naẓar) and it is obligatory before revelation. The Jews, Christians, Magians, and heretics will become dust in the Hereafter; they will not enter Paradise or Hell, and likewise animals and children. And capability (al-istiṭāʿa) is soundness of instrument (salāmat al-āla) and it is before the act. And whoever does not know his Creator among the disbelievers is excused. And all cognitions are necessary. And man has no act other than will (al-irāda); what is other than it is originated without an originator. And the world is God's act by nature (bi-ṭabʿihi), as if they intended by this what the philosophers say about emanation (al-ījāb), which entails the pre-eternity of the world. Thumāma was in the time of al-Ma'mūn and had a status with him.
Source pages p. 415

Commentary
This passage describes the Thumāmiyya sect, followers of Thumāma b. Ashras al-Numayrī, characterized as combining religious frivolity and dissolute character. Their major claim is that 'generated acts' (al-afʿāl al-mutawallada) have no agent, using two arguments: if attributed to a human, the person might die before the act completes; if attributed to God, He would be the author of evil. They also held that knowledge is generated from reflection and is obligatory before revelation. They claimed that non-Muslims and even animals become dust in the afterlife without punishment or reward. They defined capability as soundness of instruments prior to the act. They excused disbelievers who do not know their Creator. They asserted that all cognitions are necessary. They reduced human action to will only, claiming everything else is originated without an originator. They believed the world is God's act by nature (bi-ṭabʿihi), akin to the philosophers' emanation theory, which implies the pre-eternity of the world. The passage ends with a biographical note that Thumāma was favored by Caliph al-Ma'mūn.

Key Terms
الثمامية
الأفعال المتولدة
الفاعل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that generated acts have no agent at all.
Correction: Sunni theology holds that God is the Creator of all acts, including generated ones, and humans are responsible for their acquisitions.

Checkpoint
According to the Thumāmiyya, why can generated acts not be attributed to a human agent?
A) Because humans lack the power to cause them
B) Because the human may be dead when the act occurs
C) Because humans are not responsible
D) Because they are directly from God

Key Takeaway
The Thumāmiyya argued that generated acts have no agent, but Sunni scholars affirm that all acts originate from God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When an action of yours resulted in harm you never intended, did you consider yourself responsible? The Thumāmiyya argued that such acts have no agent. In light of this lesson, how do you reconcile your sense of responsibility with God's absolute creation of all actions? Are you willing to accept full accountability while acknowledging that God alone creates the act?
?
Have you ever hesitated to attribute a misfortune to God's decree because it seemed 'evil'? The Thumāmiyya used that very reasoning to deny God's role in generated acts. Examine your heart: do you truly believe that God is not the author of evil, yet everything happens by His will? What changes in your relationship with God when you embrace both truths?
?
The Thumāmiyya's argument concluded that generated acts have no agent. If you live as if some of your actions are not truly yours, how does that affect your repentance and striving to improve? What would it look like to live with the conviction that every act—even the unintended ones—is created by Allah and that you are fully responsible for your intentions and efforts?

Thumāmiyya on Knowledge, Obligation, and the Afterlife
Thumāmiyya on knowledge, obligation, and afterlife.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Thumāmiyya's claims that knowledge is generated from reflection, that it is obligatory before revelation, and that disbelievers become dust in the afterlife.

Core Idea
The Thumāmiyya held that knowledge from reflection is obligatory even before revelation, and non-Muslims become dust with no punishment.

The Thumāmiyya extended their rationalist approach to knowledge and the afterlife. They argued that knowledge is generated from reflection and that humans are obligated to seek God through reason even without prophets. They also denied eternal punishment for disbelievers, claiming they become dust like animals and children.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the three claims: knowledge from reflection, obligation before revelation, and the fate of disbelievers.
2
Analyze the claim about knowledge
They say knowledge is generated (mutawallida) from reflection (naẓar). This echoes Mu'tazili epistemology.
Sunni scholars hold that knowledge is granted by God, not merely generated.
3
Examine the afterlife claim
They say non-Muslims become dust, no paradise or hell. This negates eternal punishment.
4
Compare with Sunni view
Sunnis affirm eternal punishment for disbelievers and reward for believers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Commentary
This passage describes the Thumāmiyya sect, followers of Thumāma b. Ashras al-Numayrī, characterized as combining religious frivolity and dissolute character. Their major claim is that 'generated acts' (al-afʿāl al-mutawallada) have no agent, using two arguments: if attributed to a human, the person might die before the act completes; if attributed to God, He would be the author of evil. They excused disbelievers who do not know their Creator. They asserted that all cognitions are necessary. They reduced human action to will only, claiming everything else is originated without an originator. They believed the world is God's act by nature (bi-ṭabʿihi), akin to the philosophers' emanation theory, which implies the pre-eternity of the world. The passage ends with a biographical note that Thumāma was favored by Caliph al-Ma'mūn.

Key Terms

النظر
الوجوب
الآخرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe that non-Muslims will not be punished in the afterlife.
Correction: Sunni Islam teaches that disbelievers who have received the message and rejected it will be punished eternally.

Checkpoint
According to the Thumāmiyya, what happens to Jews and Christians in the Hereafter?
A) They enter Paradise
B) They are punished in Hell
C) They become dust without Paradise or Hell
D) They are reincarnated

Key Takeaway
The Thumāmiyya claimed knowledge from reason is obligatory before revelation and denied eternal punishment for non-Muslims, contradicting core Sunni doctrine.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you had been born in a time or place with no prophets, would your own reason have led you to the truth? Or would you have followed the beliefs of your society? What does your honest answer reveal about your reliance on revelation?
?
The Thumāmiyya say non-Muslims become dust with no punishment. Does that make you less motivated to call people to Islam? Or does the belief in eternal punishment drive your da‘wah? Reflect on your true motivation.
?
If you truly believed that knowledge from reflection is obligatory before revelation, how would your daily habits change? Would you spend more time contemplating God’s existence and attributes, or do you neglect reflection because you already have revelation?

Thumāmiyya on Capability, Excuse, Human Action, and Creation
Thumāmiyya on capability, excuse, human action, and world.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Thumāmiyya's views on capability as soundness of instrument, their excuse for ignorant disbelievers, their reduction of human action to will, and their claim that the world is God's act by nature.

Core Idea
The Thumāmiyya defined capability as mere physical capacity, excused all ignorant disbelievers, and believed the world emanates from God necessarily.

The Thumāmiyya held several heterodox positions on human responsibility and the nature of creation. They defined capability (istiṭāʿa) as mere soundness of bodily instruments, excused disbelievers who do not know their Creator, reduced human action to will alone, and claimed the world is God's act by nature, akin to the philosophers' emanationism.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the four distinct claims: capability, excuse, human act, and world's nature.
2
Analyze capability
They say capability is soundness of instrument and precedes the act. This resembles the Mu'tazili view.
Sunnis say capability is with the act.
3
Analyze the excuse
They excuse anyone who does not know their Creator. This undermines the culpability of polytheists.
4
Examine the nature of human action
They say man has no act other than will; everything else happens without an originator.
This denies human responsibility for actions.
5
Reflect on the world's nature
They say the world is God's act by nature, implying emanation and pre-eternity, contradicting creation ex nihilo.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثمامية: هو ثمامة بن أشرس (النميري) كان جامعاً بين سخافة الدين وخلاعة النفس، قالوا : الأفعال المتولدة لا ( فاعل لها إذ لا يمكن إسنادها إلى فاعل لاستلزامه إسناد الفعل إلى الميت فيما إذا رمى سهما إلى شخص ومات قبل وصوله إليه ولا إلى الله تعالى لاستلزامه صدور القبيح عنه ( والمعرفة متولدة من النظر وإنها واجبة قبل الشرع واليهود والنصارى والمجوس والزنادقة يصيرون في الآخرة ( تراباً لا يدخلون جنة ولا ناراً وكذا البهائم والأطفال، والاستطاعة سلامة الآلة وهي قبل الفعل ( ومن لا يعلم خالقه الكفار معذور والمعارف كلها ضرورية ولا فعل للإنسان غير الإرادة وما عداها حادث بلا محدث والعالم فعل الله بطبعه كأنهم أرادوا به ما يقوله الفلاسفة من الإيجاب ويلزمه قدم العالم، وكان ثمامة في زمان المأمون وله عنده منزلة
The Thumāmiyya: he is Thumāma b. Ashras al-Numayrī. He combined religious frivolity and dissolute character. They said: Generated acts (al-afʿāl al-mutawallada) have no agent, because it is impossible to attribute them to an agent: attributing them to the agent would entail attributing the act to a dead person if he shot an arrow at someone and died before it reached him, and attributing them to God would entail the occurrence of evil from Him. And knowledge is generated from reflection (al-naẓar) and it is obligatory before revelation. The Jews, Christians, Magians, and heretics will become dust in the Hereafter; they will not enter Paradise or Hell, and likewise animals and children. And capability (al-istiṭāʿa) is soundness of instrument (salāmat al-āla) and it is before the act. And whoever does not know his Creator among the disbelievers is excused. And all cognitions are necessary. And man has no act other than will (al-irāda); what is other than it is originated without an originator. And the world is God's act by nature (bi-ṭabʿihi), as if they intended by this what the philosophers say about emanation (al-ījāb), which entails the pre-eternity of the world. Thumāma was in the time of al-Ma'mūn and had a status with him.
Source pages p. 415

Commentary
This passage describes the Thumāmiyya sect, followers of Thumāma b. Ashras al-Numayrī, characterized as combining religious frivolity and dissolute character. Their major claim is that 'generated acts' (al-afʿāl al-mutawallada) have no agent, using two arguments: if attributed to a human, the person might die before the act completes; if attributed to God, He would be the author of evil. They also held that knowledge is generated from reflection and is obligatory before revelation. They claimed that non-Muslims and even animals become dust in the afterlife without punishment or reward. They defined capability as soundness of instruments prior to the act. They excused disbelievers who do not know their Creator. They asserted that all cognitions are necessary. They reduced human action to will only, claiming everything else is originated without an originator. They believed the world is God's act by nature (bi-ṭabʿihi), akin to the philosophers' emanation theory, which implies the pre-eternity of the world. The passage ends with a biographical note that Thumāma was favored by Caliph al-Ma'mūn.

Key Terms
الاستطاعة
المعذور
الإرادة
الإيجاب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Disbelievers who are ignorant of God are not culpable.
Correction: Sunnis hold that all humans naturally know God through fitra and are accountable.

Checkpoint
What does the Thumāmiyya claim about man's actions other than will?
A) They are created by God
B) They are originated without an originator
C) They are generated by humans
D) They are illusions

Key Takeaway
The Thumāmiyya denied human agency beyond will, excused all ignorant disbelievers, and claimed the world emanates from God eternally.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you remain willfully ignorant of some obligation, do you excuse yourself as if you didn't know, even though you have access to the truth? How does the Thumāmiyya's excuse of disbelievers expose the danger of using ignorance as a shield?
?
The Thumāmiyya reduced your act to mere will, not the deed itself. In your life, do you sometimes distance yourself from your sins by claiming 'I didn't mean it' or 'it was just a mistake'? What would it mean to own your actions fully in light of this lesson?
?
If the world were a necessary emanation from God, your existence would be accidental and purposeless. But you believe God created you with a purpose. Are you living as if that purpose matters, or do you act as if your choices and accountability are illusions?

The Khayyāṭiyya on Human Agency (Qadar)
The first belief: human agency (qadar).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Khayyāṭiyya's view that actions are attributed to servants (human agency) and how this relates to divine decree.

Core Idea
The Khayyāṭiyya placed real human agency in the hands of servants.

The Khayyāṭiyya sect, following Abū al-Ḥusayn al-Khayyāṭ, held controversial positions on predestination and human responsibility. The first of their beliefs concerns qadar – the attribution of actions to human beings. This lesson examines their precise claim and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Begin by reading the Arabic and English translation of the Khayyāṭiyya's statement on qadar.
Notice that the phrase 'attributing actions to servants' is central.
2
Clarify the meaning of qadar
In this context, qadar means 'predestination' but they specifically mean that actions are really done by humans, not just acquired.
3
Consider Sunni opposition
Reflect on how this view contrasts with the Sunni doctrine of kasb, where actions are created by God and acquired by humans.
The Khayyāṭiyya were a Mu'tazili subsect, and this position affirms free will.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخياطية: أصحاب أبي الحسين بن أبي عمر والخياطية قالوا : (بالقدر) أي إسناد الأفعال إلى العباد ( وتسمية المعدوم شيئاً ) أي ثابتاً متقرراً في حال العدم ( وجوهراً وعرضاً ) أي الذوات الثابتة متصفة بصفات الأجناس حالة العدم، ( وإن إرادة الله كونه ) قادراً ( غير مكره ولا كاره (وهي أي إرادته تعالى ( في أفعال نفسه الخلق) أي كونه خالقاً لها، ( وفي أفعال عباده الأمر بها وكونه سميعاً بصيراً) معناه أنه عالم بمتعلقهما، وكونه يرى ذاته أو غيره ) معناه ) أنه يعلمه ) ،
The Khayyāṭiyya: the followers of Abū al-Ḥusayn b. Abī ʿUmar al-Khayyāṭ. They said: [affirming] predestination (al-qadar), meaning attributing actions to servants; and naming the non-existent (al-maʿdūm) as a thing, i.e., established and determined in the state of non-existence, and as a substance and accident, i.e., the established essences described with the attributes of genera in the state of non-existence. And that God's will is His being powerful, not compelled nor unwilling; and it – i.e., His will – in His own acts is [His] creating (al-khalq), i.e., His being their Creator; and in the acts of His servants it is commanding them; and His being Hearing, Seeing means He is knowledgeable of their objects; and His seeing Himself or others means He knows them.
Source pages p. 415

Commentary
This passage presents the Khayyāṭiyya sect, followers of Abū al-Ḥusayn al-Khayyāṭ. They affirmed human agency (al-qadar) by attributing actions to servants. They held that non-existent things (al-maʿdūm) are 'things' – established and determined in the state of non-existence, and can be described as substances and accidents with generic attributes. They defined God's will as His being powerful without compulsion; in relation to His own acts, will is creating (khalq); in relation to servants' acts, will is commanding. They interpreted God's attributes of Hearing and Seeing as knowledge of the objects of hearing and sight, and His seeing as knowing.

Key Terms
الخياطية
القدر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the Khayyāṭiyya denied predestination entirely.
Correction: They affirmed qadar but redefined it as human agency, not divine determinism.

Checkpoint
According to the Khayyāṭiyya, what does qadar mean?
A) Divine decree controlling all events
B) Attributing actions to servants
C) Creating actions for humans
D) Denying human responsibility

Key Takeaway
The Khayyāṭiyya upheld human agency by attributing actions directly to servants.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you instinctively blame your circumstances or upbringing instead of owning your choice? This lesson shows a sect that placed full agency on servants. Can you honestly face your own responsibility without shifting blame, starting with the next small misstep you catch yourself making today?
?
The Khayyāṭiyya wanted to protect God's justice by insisting your actions are yours. But what if God's justice is not like human fairness? Will you let go of demanding that God 'must' reward you and instead trust His mercy, even when you fail? Try this week to thank Him for His mercy before you ask for anything.
?
If you truly believed every action is your own—not written by fate or influenced by others—would you prepare for prayer with more focus? This week, before each prayer, pause and say: 'This action is mine. I choose to stand before my Lord.' What changes in your heart?

The Khayyāṭiyya on Non-Existent Entities
The second belief: non-existent things as established entities.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Khayyāṭiyya's claim that non-existent things are established entities with attributes.

Core Idea
Non-existent things are real, established entities in the state of non-existence.

The second belief of the Khayyāṭiyya concerns the status of non-existent things (al-ma'dum). They claimed that non-existent things are 'things' – established, determined, and even describable as substances and accidents. This lesson explores this metaphysical position.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation focusing on the description of non-existent things.
Key terms: 'ثابت', 'مقرر', 'جوهر', 'عرض'.
2
Analyze the claim
The passage says non-existent things are established (thābit) and determined (muqarrar) in the state of non-existence.
This is a Mu'tazili view that non-existent quiddities have a kind of reality.
3
Consider implications
If non-existent things have attributes, then creation is merely giving existence to pre-existing essences.
This contrasts with the Sunni view that things only come into existence at creation.

?

?
Your future actions are 'non-existent' yet established in Allah's knowledge. Does this make you feel trapped by destiny or more aware that your choices are already accounted for? Examine your heart: are you indifferent or proactive?
?
The Khayyāṭiyya say non-existent things are 'things' with generic attributes. Reflect on your own assumptions: do you treat your future hopes and plans as merely nothing, or as fixed realities that demand action? What would change if you truly believed they are 'established' before Allah?

The Khayyāṭiyya on God's Will
The third belief: God's will as power, with distinct operations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Khayyāṭiyya distinguished God's will in His own acts versus servants' acts.

Core Idea
God's will is His power, but its effect differs: creating in His own acts, commanding in servants' acts.

The third belief of the Khayyāṭiyya concerns the nature of divine will (irāda). They defined it as God's being powerful without compulsion, and then explained its relation to different types of acts. This lesson deciphers their nuanced position.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation to see the definition and distinction of God's will.
Notice the terms 'قادراً', 'غير مكره ولا كاره'.
2
Understand the definition
God's will is equated with His being powerful (qādir), not compelled or unwilling. This identifies will with power.
3
Distinguish the two contexts
In His own acts (e.g., creating), will is creating (khalq). In servants' acts, will is commanding (amr).
This avoids attributing evil acts to God's will directly.

The Khayyāṭiyya: the followers of Abū al-Ḥusayn b. Abī ʿUmar al-Khayyāṭ. ?

?

?
Since God's will for His own acts is creating, every good thing in your life is directly from Him. Has your gratitude been directed to Him as the Creator of those blessings, or have you taken them for granted? Make a specific intention to thank Him for one blessing today.

The Khayyāṭiyya on Divine Attributes as Knowledge
The fourth belief: attributes interpreted as knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Khayyāṭiyya's interpretation of God's attributes of Hearing, Seeing, and Seeing as knowledge.

Core Idea
God's attributes of hearing, seeing, and seeing are reduced to knowledge of their objects.

The final belief of the Khayyāṭiyya listed in this passage concerns the divine attributes of Hearing (samīʿ), Seeing (baṣīr), and the act of seeing (ru'ya). They interpreted these as mere knowledge of the corresponding objects. This lesson examines this reductionist approach.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation focusing on the interpretation of 'Hearing' and 'Seeing'.
The text uses the construct 'معناه أنه عالم بمتعلقهما'.
2
Understand the reduction
The Khayyāṭiyya say that being Hearing and Seeing means God knows the objects of hearing and sight.
This denies that God has distinct faculties of hearing and sight beyond knowledge.
3
Extend to seeing (ru'ya)
Similarly, God's seeing Himself or others is interpreted as His knowing them.
This eliminates a separate attribute of vision.

The Khayyāṭiyya: the followers of Abū al-Ḥusayn b. Abī ʿUmar al-Khayyāṭ. They said: [affirming] predestination (al-qadar), meaning attributing actions to servants; and naming the non-existent (al-maʿdūm) as a thing, i.e., established and determined in the state of non-existence, and as a substance and accident, i.e., the established essences described with the attributes of genera in the state of non-existence. They held that non-existent things (al-maʿdūm) are 'things' – established and determined in the state of non-existence, and can be described as substances and accidents with generic attributes. They defined God's will as His being powerful without compulsion; in relation to His own acts, will is creating (khalq); in relation to servants' acts, will is commanding. They interpreted God's attributes of Hearing and Seeing as knowledge of the objects of hearing and sight, and His seeing as knowing.

Key Terms
سميع
بصير
عالم
معلقهما

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the Khayyāṭiyya denied all attributes.
Correction: They affirmed the names but interpreted them as knowledge, not as separate attributes.

Checkpoint
According to the Khayyāṭiyya, what does 'God sees Himself' mean?
A) He has a visual faculty
B) He knows Himself
C) He is visible to others
D) He creates sight

Key Takeaway
The Khayyāṭiyya reduced God's sensory attributes to His knowledge of their objects.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever treat God's hearing and sight as mere intellectual facts, forgetting that He is constantly aware of every word you speak and every action you do? How can you transform this knowledge into a living sense of accountability starting today?
?
If someone told you that God's attributes are only His knowledge, would your worship feel less personal? Reflect: Does knowing that God sees you exactly as He knows you bring you closer to Him? Will you pause now and ask Him to make His presence real in your life?

The Jahiziyya: Denial of Free Will
Lists the deviant beliefs of ʿAmr b. Baḥr al-Jāḥiẓ and his followers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the core doctrines of the Jāḥiẓiyya sect regarding cognition and will, and how they challenge mainstream Islamic theology.

Core Idea
The Jāḥiẓiyya denied free will, reducing will to mere awareness.

This lesson introduces the Jāḥiẓiyya, a sect that held extreme views on human cognition and will. Their denial of voluntary acquisition and reduction of will to absence of forgetfulness directly contradicts the Sunni position. The passage presents their two main claims, attributed to their founder ʿAmr b. Baḥr al-Jāḥiẓ.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without focusing on details. Then read the literal translation to grasp the overall meaning.
Notice the biographical note on al-Jāḥiẓ and his association with philosophers.
2
Identify the two doctrines
The passage lists two key beliefs: all cognitions are necessary, and there is no real will in humans. Underline or note them in your mind.
3
Analyze the second doctrine
The text says that 'will' is nothing but the absence of forgetfulness (ʿadam al-sahw). Reflect on what this implies about human agency.
This reduces will to a state of knowledge, not a separate faculty.
4
Connect to Sunni theology
Consider why Sunni scholars reject this view: if all cognitions are necessary, then reflection and acquisition of knowledge would be meaningless. Similarly, if will is mere awareness, then moral responsibility collapses.
5
Test your understanding
Answer the checkpoint question to ensure you grasp the definition of 'will' according to the Jāḥiẓiyya.
The answer is based directly on the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الجاحظية : هو عمر بن بحر الجاحظ ) من الفضلاء البلغاء في أيام المعتصم والمتوكل وقد طالع كتب الفلاسفة كثيراً من مقالاتهم بعباراته البليغة اللطيفة (قالوا : المعارف كلها ضرورية ولا إرادة في الشاهد ( أي في الواحد منا ( إنما هي ( إرادته لفعله ( عدم السهو) أي كونه عالماً
The Jāḥiẓiyya: he is ʿAmr b. Baḥr al-Jāḥiẓ, one of the virtuous eloquent men in the days of al-Muʿtaṣim and al-Mutawakkil. He studied the books of the philosophers extensively, [conveying] many of their doctrines with his eloquent, refined expressions. They said: All cognitions are necessary. And there is no will in the witnessed world (i.e., in any one of us); rather, [a person's] will for his action is only the absence of forgetfulness (ʿadam al-sahw), i.e., his being knowledgeable.
Source pages p. 415

Commentary
This passage describes the Jāḥiẓiyya sect, followers of the famous literary figure ʿAmr b. Baḥr al-Jāḥiẓ, who was known for his eloquence and study of philosophy. Their primary doctrines as listed here are: all cognitions (maʿārif) are necessary (ḍarūriyya), meaning they cannot be acquired through choice. Additionally, they denied that humans have a real will; what is called 'will' is merely the absence of forgetfulness or being knowledgeable. This reduces human agency to mere cognition and eliminates free will.

Key Terms
الجاحظية
المعارف
ضرورية
الإرادة
السهو

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people think that will is merely a state of knowledge or awareness, and that there is no real free choice in human actions.
Correction: Sunni scholars affirm that will is a real attribute distinct from knowledge. Humans have genuine choice and responsibility, contrary to the Jāḥiẓiyya reduction of will to absence of forgetfulness.

Checkpoint
According to the Jāḥiẓiyya, what is a person's will (irāda) for an action?
A) A real choice
B) Absence of forgetfulness or being knowledgeable
C) A divine decree
D) An accident

Key Takeaway
The Jāḥiẓiyya believed all knowledge is necessary and that human will is merely the absence of forgetfulness, effectively denying free will.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you fail to do what you know is right, do you ever catch yourself thinking 'I just wasn't aware enough' rather than admitting you chose not to act? How does that excuse mirror the Jāḥiẓiyya's reduction of will to mere knowledge?
?
The Jāḥiẓiyya eliminated free will to avoid complexity. Are there areas of your life—repentance, patience, or seeking knowledge—where you functionally act as if you have no choice, just to escape the weight of responsibility?
?
If will is only 'not being forgetful,' then sin is simply ignorance. Where have you used the excuse 'I didn't know' to avoid confronting your own willful disobedience? What would change if you fully owned that you knew better?

Conclusion of the Fourth Observation: Doctrine of Reincarnation
Describes the doctrine of reincarnation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the doctrine of reincarnation as described in this passage and how it is distinguished from Islamic resurrection.

Core Idea
Reincarnation teaches cyclical rebirth based on sins, not a single resurrection.

This passage concludes the fourth observation by presenting a heretical doctrine—reincarnation. It describes how souls are reborn into different forms (human or animal) based on their deeds. This concept directly contradicts Islamic teachings on resurrection, making it a key error to identify and refute.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to get a sense of the author's description of reincarnation.
Notice that the author calls it 'the very doctrine of reincarnation'.
2
Identify the key components
Look for the elements: bodies being clothed, different forms, testing according to sins, and the cycle continuing as long as sins remain.
3
Understand the error
Reflect on why this doctrine is considered heretical in Islam. The passage is setting up a contrast with the correct belief in resurrection.
This connects to the common misunderstanding that resurrection is similar to reincarnation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خاتمة للمرصد الرابع بعض في البعض دون البعض فأخرجهم إلى دار الدنيا وكساهم هذه الأجساد الكثيفة على صور مختلفة كصورة الإنسان وسائر الحيوانات، وابتلاهم بالبأساء والضراء والآلام واللذات على مقادير ذنوبهم، فمن كان معاصيه أقل وطاعاته أكثر كانت صورته أحسن وآلامه أقل، ومن كان بالعكس فبالعكس ولا يزال يكون الحيوان في الدنيا في صورة بعد صورة ما دامت معه ذنوبه وهذا عين القول بالتناسخ .
Conclusion of the fourth observation: Some among them are taken out to the abode of this world, and they are clothed with these dense bodies in various forms, like the form of humans and all animals, and He tests them with adversity and harm, pains and pleasures according to the measures of their sins. Whoever has fewer sins and more obedience, his form is better and his pains are fewer. Whoever is the opposite, the opposite. And the animal continues in this world from form to form as long as his sins remain with him. This is exactly the doctrine of reincarnation (التناسخ).
Source pages p. 415

Commentary
This passage is a conclusion to the fourth observation (المرصد الرابع) in the book, describing a heretical doctrine—reincarnation (التناسخ). It states that some people are brought into the world clothed with dense bodies in various forms (human, animal) differing based on their sins and obedience. Those with fewer sins and more obedience have better forms and fewer pains; the opposite holds for the opposite. The soul continues changing forms as long as sins remain. This is identified as the exact doctrine of reincarnation, which the author is refuting or discussing.

Key Terms
تناسخ
ذنوب
صور
أجساد كثيفة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Reincarnation is similar to Islamic resurrection.
Correction: Islamic resurrection is a one-time event where bodies are raised from the dead, not a cyclical rebirth into different forms based on sins.

Checkpoint
What is the main doctrine described in this passage?
A) The eternity of the world
B) Reincarnation (التناسخ)
C) The creation of bodies by God
D) The necessity of prophethood

Key Takeaway
This passage defines reincarnation as the cyclical rebirth of souls into various forms based on sins, directly contrasting with Islamic resurrection.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believed that your soul could be reborn as an animal due to your sins, how would that change the way you view your current life and the urgency of repentance?
?
The passage describes reincarnation as a hopeless cycle of suffering. Contrast that with the Islamic promise of forgiveness for a single sincere repentance. Are you living as if you have unlimited chances, or are you taking advantage of the one life you have to turn back to Allah?
?
When you think about the Day of Judgment, do you feel a sense of final accountability that moves you to action, or does the idea of reincarnation (even subconsciously) make you complacent? What steps will you take today to prepare for that one, definitive reckoning?

Muammariyya on Bodies and Accidents
Lists the Muammariyya view on God, bodies, and accidents.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Muammariyya doctrine that God did not create bodies, but bodies themselves produce accidents.

Core Idea
Bodies, not God, are the source of accidents.

The Muammariyya sect held a distinctive view about creation. They believed that God did not create physical bodies at all; instead, bodies themselves generate accidents. This lesson explores that view and the internal contradiction noted by later scholars.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on bodies and accidents
Read the Arabic passage carefully. Notice the claim that God did not create any bodies, and that bodies invent accidents either by nature or by choice.
The author gives examples: fire burning, sun heating, animals producing colors.
2
Identify the two types of accident production
The passage states that bodies produce accidents in two ways: by nature (like fire burning) or by choice (like animals producing colors). Identify these two categories.
3
Note the internal contradiction
The author points out a contradiction: if the origination and annihilation of bodies are accidents, how can bodies be the source of those accidents? Reflect on this critique.
This shows that the Muammariyya position was considered inconsistent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المعمرية : هو معمر بن عباد السلمي قالوا : الله لم يخلق شيئاً من الأجسام، أما الأعراض فتخترعها الأجسام إما طبعاً كالنار للإحراق والشمس للحرارة، وإما اختياراً كالحيوان للألوان قيل : ومن العجب أن حدوث الأجسام وفناءها عند معمر من الأعراض فكيف يقول : إنها من فعل الأجسام، (و) قالوا : ( لا يوصف) الله (بالقدم) لأنه يدل على التقادم الزماني والله سبحانه ليس بزماني ) ولا يعلم الله نفسه وإلا اتحد العالم والمعلوم وهو ممتنع ) والإنسان لا فعل له غير (الإرادة مباشرة كانت أو توليداً بناء على ما ذهبوا إليه من مذهب الفلاسفة في حقيقة الإنسان.
The Muammariyya: He is Muammar ibn Abbad al-Sulami. They said: God did not create anything from bodies. As for accidents (الأعراض), bodies invent them—either by nature, like fire for burning and the sun for heat, or by choice, like animals for colors. It was said: Among the wonders is that the origination and annihilation of bodies according to Muammar are accidents. So how can he say they are from the act of bodies? And they said: God is not described with pre-eternity (القدم) because it indicates temporal priority, and God—exalted is He—is not temporal. And God does not know His own self, otherwise the knower and the known would be united, which is impossible. And man has no act other than will (الإرادة), whether direct or generated, based on their adoption of the philosophers' doctrine regarding the reality of man.
Source pages p. 415

Commentary
This passage defines the Muammariyya sect, named after Muammar ibn Abbad al-Sulami. It lists several of their doctrines: (1) God did not create any bodies—bodies themselves generate accidents (الأعراض) either by nature (fire burns, sun heats) or by choice (animals produce colors). The author notes a contradiction: Muammar considers the origination and annihilation of bodies to be accidents, yet claims they come from bodies. (2) God is not described as pre-eternal (قدم) because that implies temporal priority, which does not apply to a non-temporal God. (3) God does not know His own self, otherwise knower and known would unite, which is impossible. (4) Man has no action except will (الإرادة), whether direct or generated, following the philosophers' view of human reality.

Key Terms
أجسام
أعراض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Muammariyya deny that God created anything at all.
Correction: They deny only that God created bodies; they affirm that God created the spiritual world and perhaps other things, but bodies are self-originating in terms of accidents.

Checkpoint
According to the Muammariyya, what is the source of accidents like heat and color?
A) God directly
B) The bodies themselves
C) Angels
D) Human souls

Key Takeaway
The Muammariyya held that God did not create bodies; bodies themselves produce all accidents, a view that was criticized as contradictory.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever act as if the things around you have independent power to affect you, forgetting that all power belongs to Allah? Reflect on a habit where you rely on natural causes as if they were ultimate agents. What would it take to shift that reliance to Allah alone?
?
The Muammariyya were criticized for a logical inconsistency in their view. Are there inconsistencies in your own belief in divine power and your daily actions? Consider a time when you acted as if your own efforts were the sole cause of success, without acknowledging Allah's role. How can you make tawhid more consistent in your life?
?
The passage highlights that even the existence of bodies is an accident - a contingent property. How does this reshape your understanding of your own existence? Are you truly contingent on Allah every moment, or do you feel self-sufficient? What practical step can you take today to live in constant awareness of your dependence on Him?

Muammariyya on God's Attributes
States the Muammariyya denial of God's pre-eternity and self-knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Muammariyya denied that God is pre-eternal and that God knows His own self.

Core Idea
God cannot be called pre-eternal or know Himself.

The Muammariyya held unconventional views about God's attributes. They argued that describing God as 'pre-eternal' implies temporal priority, which is not applicable to a timeless being. They also claimed that if God knew Himself, that would lead to an impossible union of knower and known. This lesson explores these two denials.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on God's attributes
Read the Arabic passage about God not being described as pre-eternal and not knowing Himself. Note the reasoning given.
The passage uses parentheses, likely direct quotes from the sect.
2
Analyze the denial of pre-eternity
Understand their argument: the term 'pre-eternal' (قدم) implies temporal priority, but God is beyond time. Therefore, the attribute is inappropriate.
This shows a strict literal interpretation of the term.
3
Analyze the denial of self-knowledge
Consider their reasoning: if God knew Himself, then the knower and the known would be identical, which they consider impossible. This is a philosophical argument against divine self-knowledge.
This view is criticized by other Muslim theologians.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المعمرية : هو معمر بن عباد السلمي قالوا : الله لم يخلق شيئاً من الأجسام، أما الأعراض فتخترعها الأجسام إما طبعاً كالنار للإحراق والشمس للحرارة، وإما اختياراً كالحيوان للألوان قيل : ومن العجب أن حدوث الأجسام وفناءها عند معمر من الأعراض فكيف يقول : إنها من فعل الأجسام، (و) قالوا : ( لا يوصف) الله (بالقدم) لأنه يدل على التقادم الزماني والله سبحانه ليس بزماني ) ولا يعلم الله نفسه وإلا اتحد العالم والمعلوم وهو ممتنع ) والإنسان لا فعل له غير (الإرادة مباشرة كانت أو توليداً بناء على ما ذهبوا إليه من مذهب الفلاسفة في حقيقة الإنسان.
The Muammariyya: He is Muammar ibn Abbad al-Sulami. They said: God did not create anything from bodies. As for accidents (الأعراض), bodies invent them—either by nature, like fire for burning and the sun for heat, or by choice, like animals for colors. It was said: Among the wonders is that the origination and annihilation of bodies according to Muammar are accidents. So how can he say they are from the act of bodies? And they said: God is not described with pre-eternity (القدم) because it indicates temporal priority, and God—exalted is He—is not temporal. And God does not know His own self, otherwise the knower and the known would be united, which is impossible. And man has no act other than will (الإرادة), whether direct or generated, based on their adoption of the philosophers' doctrine regarding the reality of man.
Source pages p. 415

Commentary
This passage defines the Muammariyya sect, named after Muammar ibn Abbad al-Sulami. It lists several of their doctrines: (1) God did not create any bodies—bodies themselves generate accidents (الأعراض) either by nature (fire burns, sun heats) or by choice (animals produce colors). The author notes a contradiction: Muammar considers the origination and annihilation of bodies to be accidents, yet claims they come from bodies. (2) God is not described as pre-eternal (قدم) because that implies temporal priority, which does not apply to a non-temporal God. (3) God does not know His own self, otherwise knower and known would unite, which is impossible. (4) Man has no action except will (الإرادة), whether direct or generated, following the philosophers' view of human reality.

Key Terms
قدم
اتحاد العالم والمعلوم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Muammariyya deny that God is eternal or that He has knowledge.
Correction: They only deny the specific attribute of 'pre-eternity' (due to temporal connotation) and self-knowledge (due to identity problem). They do not necessarily deny other forms of eternality or knowledge.

Checkpoint
