Bahshamiyya on Divine Knowledge and States (Ahwal)
Bahshamiyya on divine knowledge and states, and al-Amidi's critique.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Bahshamiyya's views on divine knowledge and the theory of states (ahwal), as well as al-Amidi's critique of that theory.

Core Idea
The Bahshamiyya theory of divine states leads to a logical contradiction according to al-Amidi.

Abu Hashim al-Jubba'i also proposed a theory of divine attributes as states (ahwal) that are neither existent nor non-existent, neither known nor unknown. This passage explains his view on divine knowledge and states, and presents al-Amidi's incisive critique, which exposes a fatal flaw in the theory.

Guided Path
1
Read the claim about divine knowledge
Note Abu Hashim's statement that a single act of knowledge cannot relate to two known things in detail. This is a specific epistemological claim.
2
Understand the theory of states (ahwal)
Examine the description of divine states as neither known nor unknown, neither eternal nor originated. This is a core doctrine of the Bahshamiyya.
These states are supposed to be the underlying reality of God's attributes.
3
Analyze al-Amidi's critique
Al-Amidi points out a contradiction: 'originated' is defined as 'not eternal', and 'unknown' as 'not known', making the definition of states circular and unintelligible. He also deems affirming an unknown state for God impossible.
This critique undermines the coherence of the ahwal theory.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
البهمشمية : انفرد أبو هاشم عن أبيه بإمكان استحقاق الذم والعقاب بلا معصية مع كونه مخالفاً للإجماع والحكمة، وبأنه لا توبة عن كبيرة مع الإصرار على غيرها عالما بقبحه ويلزمه أن لا يصح إعلام الكافر مع أدنى ذنب أصر عليه ولا توبة مع عدم القدرة فلا تصح توبة الكاذب عن كذبه بعدما صار أخرس، ولا توبة الزاني عن زناه بعدما جب ولا يتعلق علم واحد بمعلومين على التفصيل ولله أحوال لا معلومة ولا مجهولة ولا قديمة ولا حادثة قال الآمدي : هذا تناقض إذ لا معنى لكون الشيء حادثاً إلا أنه ليس قديماً ولا معنى لكونه مجهولاً إلا أنه ليس معلوماً على أن إثبات حالة له غير معلومة مما لا سبيل إليه
Al-Bahshamiyya: Abu Hashim differed from his father in [holding] the possibility of deserving blame and punishment without sin, despite it being contrary to consensus and wisdom; and that there is no repentance from a major sin while persisting in another sin while knowing its ugliness, and it follows that informing the disbeliever is not valid with the slightest sin he persists in; and there is no repentance with lack of ability, so the repentance of a liar from his lie after he becomes mute is not valid, nor the repentance of a fornicator from his fornication after he is castrated; and a single knowledge does not relate to two known things in detail; and for God there are states (ahwal) that are neither known nor unknown, neither eternal nor originated. Al-Amidi said: This is a contradiction, for there is no meaning to a thing being originated except that it is not eternal, and no meaning to it being unknown except that it is not known. Moreover, affirming a state that is unknown for Him is something impossible.
Source pages p. 416

Commentary
This passage describes the Bahshamiyya sect, named after Abu Hashim al-Jubba'i, and his distinctive views that separate him from his father Abu 'Ali. Abu Hashim held: 1. It is possible to deserve blame and punishment without committing a sin, which the author notes is contrary to consensus and wisdom. 2. Repentance from a major sin is not accepted if one persists in another sin while knowing its ugliness. Consequently, informing a disbeliever is invalid if he persists in even a minor sin. 3. Repentance is not valid when one lacks the ability to commit the sin again (e.g., a liar who becomes mute cannot repent from lying, a fornicator who is castrated cannot repent from fornication). 4. A single act of knowledge cannot encompass two known things in detail. 5. For God, there exist states (ahwal) that are not known, not unknown, not eternal, and not originated. Al-Amidi criticizes this as a contradiction: 'originated' means 'not eternal' and 'unknown' means 'not known', so the definition is circular. Furthermore, affirming an unknown state for God is impossible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Bahshamiyya concept of divine states (ahwal) is a coherent metaphysical theory.
Correction: Al-Amidi shows it is self-contradictory because the definitions are circular and it is impossible to affirm an unknown state for God.

Checkpoint
What criticism does al-Amidi make against Abu Hashim's concept of 'states' (ahwal)?
A) They are impossible because God cannot have attributes.
B) They are self-contradictory because they are defined by negations that are circular.
C) They are heretical because they deny God's omniscience.
D) They are meaningless because they have no practical effect.

Key Takeaway
Al-Amidi's critique exposes a logical flaw in the Bahshamiyya theory of divine states, showing that it is self-contradictory.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Amidi shows that claiming a state that is 'neither known nor unknown' is a contradiction. Are there aspects of your own belief about Allah that you hold without checking if they are logically coherent? Will you commit to examining your theological assumptions for consistency, even if it feels uncomfortable?
?
This lesson teaches that even learned scholars like the Bahshamiyya can fall into self-contradiction. How does this humble you in your own speech about Allah? Do you accept that your understanding may be flawed, and are you willing to correct it when faced with clear evidence?
?
Al-Amidi insists that affirming an unknown state for God is 'impossible'. Reflect: Do you ever justify unclear or contradictory beliefs by saying 'Allah knows best' without first trying to resolve the contradiction? How can you balance trust in Allah's transcendence with your responsibility to think clearly about His attributes?

The Shi'a Sect and the Extremist Sabai'iyya
Introduces the Shi'a sect and details the extremist Sabai'iyya sub-sect.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the defining beliefs of the Shi'a as presented by the author, including the role of nass and taqiyya, and the specific extremist doctrines of the Sabai'iyya sub-sect.

Core Idea
The Sabai'iyya deified 'Ali and believed him to be alive in the clouds—an extreme example of Shi'a ghuluww.

The author introduces the Shi'a as a major Islamic sect defined by their support for 'Ali and belief in his designated Imamate. After outlining their general framework, he delves into the extremist Ghulat branch, focusing on the Sabai'iyya, whose doctrines illustrate how far some groups deviated into exaggeration.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Shi'a definition
Read the opening lines identifying the Shi'a by their support for 'Ali and belief in nass (explicit or implicit designation).
Notice the emphasis on nass and taqiyya as key Shi'a concepts.
2
Note the sub-sects and branches
Recognize that there are 22 Shi'a sub-sects, some excommunicating others, and that they trace to three main branches: Ghulat, Zaydiyya, Imamiyya.
The Ghulat are further divided into 18 sub-sects, starting with Sabai'iyya.
3
Examine the Sabai'iyya beliefs
Read about 'Abdullah ibn Saba's claim that 'Ali is God, his Jewish background, and the doctrines that 'Ali did not die, is in the clouds, and will return.
Note the connection to thunder and lightning.
4
Reflect on the implications
Consider how these beliefs represent an extreme form of ghuluww (exaggeration) and differ from mainstream Shi'a views.
This guards against the misconception that all Shi'a hold such views.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفرقة الثانية : من كبار الفرق الإسلامية الشيعة : أي الذين شايعوا عليا وقالوا : إنه الإمام بعد رسول الله بالنص إما جليا وإما خفيا، واعتقدوا أن الإمامة لا تخرج عنه وعن أولاده وإن خرجت فإما بظلم يكون من غيرهم وإما بتقية منه أو من أولاده وهم اثنتان وعشرون فرقة يكفر بعضهم بعضا ، أصولهم ثلاث فرق : غلاة، وزيدية وإمامية . أما الغلاة : فثمانية عشر السبائية : قال عبد الله بن سباء لعلي : أنت الإله حقا فنفاه علي إلى المدائن، وقيل: إنه كان يهوديا فأسلم وكان في اليهودية يقول في يوشع بن نون وصي موسى مثل ما قال في علي وهو أول من أظهر القول بوجوب إمامة علي ومنه تشعبت أصناف الغلاة وقال ابن سبأ : وإنه لم يمت علي ولم يقتل وإنما قتل ابن ملجم شيطانا تصور بصورة علي وعلي في السحاب، والرعد صوته، والبرق سوطه وإنه ينزل بعد هذا إلى الأرض ويملؤها عدلا. وهؤلاء يقولون عند سماع الرعد : عليك السلام يا أمير المؤمنين
The second group: from the major Islamic sects: the Shi'a: that is, those who supported 'Ali and said that he is the Imam after the Messenger of God by explicit or implicit designation, and they believed that the Imamate does not leave him and his children, and if it leaves, it is either by injustice from others or by dissimulation (taqiyya) from him or his children. They are twenty-two sects, some excommunicating others. Their origins are three groups: Ghulat (extremists), Zaydiyya, and Imamiyya. As for the Ghulat, they are eighteen. Al-Saba'iyya: 'Abdullah ibn Saba' said to 'Ali: 'You are truly the god.' So 'Ali exiled him to al-Mada'in. It is said that he was a Jew and embraced Islam, and in Judaism he used to say about Joshua bin Nun, the successor of Moses, similar to what he said about 'Ali. He is the first to openly declare the obligation of 'Ali's Imamate, and from him branched the varieties of Ghulat. Ibn Saba' said: 'Ali did not die and was not killed; rather, Ibn Muljam killed a devil that appeared in the form of 'Ali, while 'Ali is in the clouds, thunder is his voice, lightning is his whip, and he will descend to the earth and fill it with justice.' These people say when hearing thunder: 'Peace be upon you, O Commander of the Faithful.'
Source pages p. 416

Commentary
This passage introduces the Shi'a as the second major division of Islamic sects (after the Mu'tazila). It defines the Shi'a as those who supported 'Ali and believed in his Imamate by divine designation (nass) either explicit or implicit, and that the Imamate remains in his lineage. There are 22 Shi'a sub-sects, some excommunicating others. The three main branches are the Ghulat (extremists), Zaydiyya, and Imamiyya. The passage then focuses on the first Ghulat sub-sect: the Sabai'iyya, followers of 'Abdullah ibn Saba'. Key beliefs: (1) Ibn Saba' declared 'Ali to be God incarnate, leading to his exile. (2) Ibn Saba' was originally a Jew who applied the same concepts to 'Ali as he had to Joshua. (3) He first openly advocated for the obligatory Imamate of 'Ali. (4) He claimed that 'Ali did not die; rather, a devil resembling him was killed, and 'Ali is alive in the clouds, with thunder as his voice and lightning as his whip, and he will return to fill the earth with justice. (5) His followers greet thunder as speaking to 'Ali.

Correction: The Sabai'iyya are an extremist fringe; mainstream Shi'a (Zaydiyya, Imamiyya) do not hold these beliefs. The passage distinguishes the Ghulat from other Shi'a groups.

Key Takeaway
The Sabai'iyya represent an extreme exaggeration within the Shi'a spectrum, deifying 'Ali and believing him to be alive and in control of natural phenomena.

The Sabai'iyya believed that 'Ali controls thunder and lightning. The Kamilia Ghulat Sub-Sect
Describes the Kamilia sect's views on the Companions, 'Ali, and metempsychosis.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the extreme views of the Kamilia sect regarding the Companions, 'Ali, and the concept of metempsychosis.

Core Idea
The Kamilia sect condemned both the Companions and 'Ali, and believed in soul transmigration.

In the study of heretical sects, the Kamilia represent an extreme faction that deviated from mainstream Islam. This passage introduces their founder Abu Kamil and his radical doctrines, which include declaring the Companions and even 'Ali as disbelievers, and a belief in metempsychosis. Understanding these views highlights the boundaries of Islamic orthodoxy.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation to get the author's own words before interpreting.
Pay attention to the structure: three main claims.
2
Identify the three key doctrines
Find the three main teachings: the status of the Companions, the status of 'Ali, and the theory of metempsychosis and the transmigrating light of Imamate.
These are the core elements of Kamilia belief.
3
Reflect on the radical departure from orthodoxy
Consider how these views contradict Sunni beliefs about the Companions, the infallibility of prophets, and the nature of prophethood and imamate.
Notice the double condemnation: both Companions and 'Ali.
4
Understand the term tanasukh
Note that metempsychosis (tanasukh) is the belief in the transfer of souls after death, which is a key heresy in Islamic theology.
Contrast with Islamic belief in resurrection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكاملية : قال أبو كامل بكفر الصحابة بترك بيعة علي وبكفر علي بترك طلب الحق ، و قال بالتناسخ في الأرواح عند الموت وأن الإمامة نور يتناسخ أي ينتقل من شخص إلى آخر وقد تصير في شخص نبوة بعدما كانت في شخص آخر إمامة
Al-Kamilia: Abu Kamil declared the Companions disbelievers for abandoning the pledge of allegiance to 'Ali, and declared 'Ali a disbeliever for abandoning the pursuit of the truth. He affirmed metempsychosis (tanasukh) of spirits at death, and that the Imamate is a light that transmigrates (yatanasakh), i.e., transfers from one person to another, and it may become prophethood in a person after having been Imamate in another.
Source pages p. 417

Commentary
This passage describes the Kamilia sect, named after Abu Kamil. He held two extreme positions: first, that all the Companions (except 'Ali) were disbelievers for not giving the pledge of allegiance to 'Ali; second, that 'Ali himself was a disbeliever for not insisting on his right to the caliphate. Additionally, he believed in tanasukh (transmigration of souls), where spirits move from one body to another at death. He also taught that the Imamate is a light that migrates from person to person, and that this light can even become the light of prophethood in someone who previously held only the Imamate.

Key Terms

التناسخ
الإمامة
النبوة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Kamilia sect only criticized the Companions and revered 'Ali.
Correction: In fact, Abu Kamil declared both the Companions and 'Ali as disbelievers.

Checkpoint
According to Abu Kamil, what happens to the Imamate after a person's death?
A) It ceases to exist.
B) It is inherited by his son.
C) It transfers to another person like a light.
D) It returns to God.

Key Takeaway
The Kamilia sect represents an extreme that deviated from mainstream Islam by condemning the Companions and 'Ali and by adopting the doctrine of metempsychosis.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The Kamilia believed the light of Imamate could become prophethood. How does this belief strike at the heart of Islam's finality? Do you truly submit to the completeness of Muhammad's message, or do you sometimes wish for a 'new light' to guide you? What does your answer reveal about your faith?

The Bayaniyya: Anthropomorphism and Spirit Transmigration
Al-Taftazani describes the anthropomorphic and incarnationist beliefs of the Bayaniyya sect.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the extreme anthropomorphic and incarnationist beliefs of the Bayaniyya sect, as described by al-Taftazani in Sharh al-Mawaqif.

Core Idea
The Bayaniyya believed God has a human form and a spirit migrates through individuals.

This passage introduces the Bayaniyya, a subgroup of the Ghulat (extremist Shia) known for radical anthropomorphism and belief in the transmigration of spirits. Al-Taftazani summarizes their creed in a few lines, highlighting two key doctrines: that God is in the form of a human being, and that a divine spirit successively inhabited certain Imams and eventually their own leader, Bayan. Understanding these beliefs helps distinguish mainstream Islamic theology from extreme positions.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text aloud once, noticing the names and the structure. The passage is a brief statement of the sect's core beliefs.
2
Identify the two key claims
Underline or note two things: (1) the anthropomorphic description of God, and (2) the sequence of spirit indwelling (hulul).
The spirit is said to have come into Ali, then his son, then grandson, then Bayan.
3
Understand the term 'Bayan'
Bayan is the founder. The sect is named after him. Note that he is the final recipient of the spirit.
This shows the sect's self-justification for leadership.
4
Reflect on why this is considered extreme
Think about how these beliefs contradict the Islamic concept of tawhid and the transcendence of God.
Mainstream Islam rejects any physical form for God and the idea of souls migrating.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
البيانية : قال بيان سمعان بن التميمي النهدي اليمني : الله على صورة إنسان ويهلك كله إلا وجهه وروح حلت في علي ثم في ابنه محمد بن الحنفية ثم في ابنه أبي هاشم ثم في بيان
Al-Bayaniyya: Bayan Sam'an al-Tamimi al-Nahdi al-Yamani said: God is in the form of a human, and everything of Him perishes except His face. A spirit settled in 'Ali, then in his son Muhammad ibn al-Hanafiyya, then in his son Abu Hashim, then in Bayan.
Source pages p. 417

Commentary
This passage describes the Bayaniyya sect, followers of Bayan Sam'an al-Tamimi. Their beliefs are highly anthropomorphic: they assert that God is in the form of a human being, and that everything of God will perish except His face (an interpretation of Quran 28:88 perhaps). Additionally, they believe that a spirit (ruh) that was in 'Ali then successively resided in his son Muhammad ibn al-Hanafiyya, then in his grandson Abu Hashim, and finally in Bayan himself. This is a form of incarnation (hulul) and metempsychosis.

Key Terms
البيانية
بيان
صورة إنسان
روح
حلول

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think Bayaniyya teachings are metaphorical or symbolic.
Correction: The passage clearly presents literal anthropomorphism: God is said to be on the form of a human (صورة إنسان) and that a spirit physically resides in individuals. This is not metaphorical but literal transmigration.

Checkpoint
According to the Bayaniyya, where did the spirit reside after Muhammad ibn al-Hanafiyya?
A) In 'Ali
B) In Abu Hashim
C) In Bayan
D) In God directly

Key Takeaway
The Bayaniyya sect combined extreme anthropomorphism with a belief in spirit transmigration through a lineage of Imams.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Bayaniyya believed a spirit settled in a chain of people, granting them authority. Is there any person, scholar, or leader in your life whose authority you accept without critically examining their teachings? What would it take for you to verify that their guidance truly aligns with the Quran and Sunnah?
?
They interpreted 'everything perishes except His face' literally to mean God has a physical face that remains. Are there any verses of the Quran that you interpret in a way that suits your desires rather than how the righteous predecessors understood them? How can you train yourself to submit to the correct interpretation even when it is difficult?

The Mughiriyya's Anthropomorphic God and Cosmogony
Mughira's cosmogony: God's form, creation via the Greatest Name, sweat, two seas, and heavenly bodies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mughiriyya's extreme anthropomorphic description of God and their mythological account of the creation of two seas and the heavenly bodies.

Core Idea
The Mughiriyya described God as a man of light who sweated out two seas.

The Mughiriyya sect, followers of Mughira ibn Sa'id al-'Ijli, held wildly anthropomorphic and mythological beliefs about God and creation. This lesson presents their account of God's form, His speaking the Greatest Name, and the origin of the two seas from His sweat. The passage also explains how the sun and moon were created from God's reflection.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text describing God's form and the creation from the Greatest Name and sweat. Notice the anthropomorphic details.
The sect interprets Quran 87:1 as referring to the Greatest Name becoming a crown.
2
Identify the key elements
List the stages: God's form (man of light with crown and wisdom), speaking the Grand Name, writing deeds, sweating, formation of two seas.
3
Examine the creation of sun and moon
Note how God sees His reflection in the luminous sea, snatches part to create sun and moon, and destroys the rest to avoid a partner.
This shows their extreme anthropomorphism and fear of shirk.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المغيرية : قال مغيرة بن سعيد العجلي : الله على صورة إنسان بل رجل من نور على رأسه تاج من نور وقلبه منبع الحكمة ولما أراد أن يخلق الخلق تكلم بالاسم الأعظم فطار فوقع تاجا على رأسه وذلك قوله تعالى: ﴿سبح اسم ربك الأعلى الذي خلق فسوى﴾ [الأعلى : ١]، ثم إنه كتب على كفه أعمال العباد فغضب من المعاصي فعرق فحصل منه أي من عرقه بحران أحدهما ملح مظلم والآخر حلو نير، ثم اطلع في البحر النير فأبصر فيه ظله فانتزعه أي انتزع بعضا من ظله فجعل وخلق منه الشمس والقمر وأفنى الباقي من الظل نفيا للشريك وقال : لا ينبغي أن يكون معي إله آخر ثم خلق الخلق من البحرين، فالكفر أي الكفار من المظلم، والإيمان أي المؤمنين من النير، ثم أرسل محمدا والناس في ضلالة وعرض الأمانة وهي منع علي عن الإمامة على السماوات والأرض والجبال فأبين أن يحملنها وأشفقن منها وحملها الإنسان وهو أبو بكر حملها بأمر عمر حين ضمن أن يعينه على ذلك بشرط أن يجعل أبو بكر الخلافة بعده له، وقوله تعالى: ﴿كمثل الشيطان﴾ [الحشر : ١٦] الآية نزلت في حق أبي بكر وعمر. هؤلاء يقولون : الإمام المنتظر هو زكريا بن محمد بن علي بن الحسين بن علي وهو حي مقيم في جبل حاجر إلى أن يؤمر بالخروج وقيل المغيرة فإنه لما قتل اختلف أصحابه فقال بعضهم بانتظاره وقال آخرون بانتظار زكريا كما كان به
Al-Mughiriyya: Mughira ibn Sa'id al-'Ijli said: God is in the form of a human, rather a man of light, on his head a crown of light, and his heart is the source of wisdom. When He wanted to create creation, He spoke the Greatest Name, and it flew and placed itself as a crown on His head. That is His saying: 'Exalt the name of your Lord, the Most High, who created and proportioned' (87:1). Then He wrote the deeds of the servants on His palm, and became angry at the sins, so He sweated, and from his sweat came two seas, one salty dark and the other sweet luminous. Then He looked into the luminous sea and saw His reflection, so He snatched it (i.e., snatched some of His reflection) and made from it the sun and the moon, and annihilated the rest of the reflection to negate any partner, saying: 'There should not be with me another god.' Then He created the creation from the two seas: unbelief (i.e., the unbelievers) from the dark sea, and faith (i.e., the believers) from the luminous sea. Then He sent Muhammad while people were in misguidance. And He presented the trust—which is preventing 'Ali from the Imamate—to the heavens, earth, and mountains, but they refused to bear it and were afraid of it, and man bore it, and he is Abu Bakr. He bore it by the command of 'Umar when he guaranteed to assist him in that, on condition that Abu Bakr make the caliphate after him for him (i.e., 'Umar). And His saying: 'Like the example of Satan' (59:16) the verse was revealed concerning Abu Bakr and 'Umar. These people say: The awaited Imam is Zakariyya ibn Muhammad ibn 'Ali ibn al-Husayn ibn 'Ali, and he is alive, residing in Mount Hajir until he is commanded to emerge. And it is said (it is) al-Mughira, for when he was killed, his companions differed: some said they await him, others said they await Zakariyya as before.
Source pages p. 417

Commentary
This long passage describes the Mughiriyya sect, followers of Mughira ibn Sa'id al-'Ijli. Their beliefs are extremely mythological and anthropomorphic: 1. God is in human form, a man of light with a crown, his heart the source of wisdom. 2. To create, He spoke the Greatest Name, which became a crown. The Quranic verse 'سبح اسم ربك الأعلى' is interpreted as describing this event. 3. He wrote deeds on His palm, became angry, sweated, and from sweat produced two seas: dark salty (for unbelievers) and bright sweet (for believers). 4. He saw His reflection in the bright sea, snatched part to create sun and moon, and destroyed the rest to avoid a partner. 5. Creation of humans from the two seas: unbelievers from the dark, believers from the light. 6. Muhammad was sent when people were in error. 7. The 'trust' (amanah) mentioned in Quran 33:72 is reinterpreted as preventing 'Ali from the caliphate. This trust was offered to the heavens, earth, mountains, but they refused; it was borne by 'man' (Abu Bakr), who did so by 'Umar's order with a promise that the caliphate would return to 'Umar. 8. Quran 59:16 is claimed to be about Abu Bakr and 'Umar. 9. Their awaited Imam is either Zakariyya (a descendant) or al-Mughira himself, with disagreement among followers after his death.

Key Terms
المغيرية
مغيرة
الاسم الأعظم
بحر
ظل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mughiriyya believe God has a physical form like a human.
Correction: Mainstream Islam affirms that God is not like any created thing; He has no body, form, or physical attributes.

Checkpoint
According to Mughira, what did God speak to create?
A) The word 'Kun'
B) The Greatest Name
C) A command to the angels
D) A magical formula

Key Takeaway
The Mughiriyya's cosmogony is a clear example of ghuluw (extremism) in anthropomorphism.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever pictured God in your mind as having human-like features, even unintentionally? How can this lesson help you purify your understanding of Allah from any form of anthropomorphism?
?
Mughira's myth shows how the desire to explain creation can lead to absurd claims. Do you ever find yourself relying on speculative explanations for matters of the unseen, rather than accepting the limits of human knowledge? What is one step you can take to submit more fully to what Allah has revealed?
?
The Mughiriyya thought they were protecting tawhid by destroying the reflection, yet they fell into ghuluw. Reflect: Is there any belief or practice you hold that you think protects tawhid but might actually contradict it? How can you ensure your faith remains within the boundaries of the Quran and Sunnah?

Mughiriyya's Creation of Believers and Unbelievers
Mughira's classification of humans based on origin from the two seas and the sending of Muhammad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Mughiriyya derived the origin of believers and unbelievers from the two seas, and their view on the state of mankind before Muhammad's mission.

Core Idea
Believers come from a sweet sea, unbelievers from a dark sea.

After describing the creation of the two seas from God's sweat, the Mughiriyya held that all of humanity was created from these seas. This lesson covers how the sect assigned believers to the luminous sweet sea and unbelievers to the dark salty sea, and their belief that Muhammad was sent when people were still in error.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic text about the creation of humanity from the two seas and the sending of Muhammad.
Note the direct correlation: faith from luminous sea, unbelief from dark.
2
Analyze the two categories
Identify the two categories: 'kufr' from dark sea, 'iman' from luminous sea. This implies a deterministic origin.
3
Consider the historical claim
The passage says Muhammad was sent while people were in misguidance (ضلالة). This aligns with the sect's view that mankind was already in error before his mission.
It may imply that the trust (discussed next) was offered before Muhammad? Actually, the trust is later.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المغيرية : قال مغيرة بن سعيد العجلي : الله على صورة إنسان بل رجل من نور على رأسه تاج من نور وقلبه منبع الحكمة ولما أراد أن يخلق الخلق تكلم بالاسم الأعظم فطار فوقع تاجا على رأسه وذلك قوله تعالى: ﴿سبح اسم ربك الأعلى الذي خلق فسوى﴾ [الأعلى : ١]، ثم إنه كتب على كفه أعمال العباد فغضب من المعاصي فعرق فحصل منه أي من عرقه بحران أحدهما ملح مظلم والآخر حلو نير، ثم اطلع في البحر النير فأبصر فيه ظله فانتزعه أي انتزع بعضا من ظله فجعل وخلق منه الشمس والقمر وأفنى الباقي من الظل نفيا للشريك وقال : لا ينبغي أن يكون معي إله آخر ثم خلق الخلق من البحرين، فالكفر أي الكفار من المظلم، والإيمان أي المؤمنين من النير، ثم أرسل محمدا والناس في ضلالة وعرض الأمانة وهي منع علي عن الإمامة على السماوات والأرض والجبال فأبين أن يحملنها وأشفقن منها وحملها الإنسان وهو أبو بكر حملها بأمر عمر حين ضمن أن يعينه على ذلك بشرط أن يجعل أبو بكر الخلافة بعده له، وقوله تعالى: ﴿كمثل الشيطان﴾ [الحشر : ١٦] الآية نزلت في حق أبي بكر وعمر. هؤلاء يقولون : الإمام المنتظر هو زكريا بن محمد بن علي بن الحسين بن علي وهو حي مقيم في جبل حاجر إلى أن يؤمر بالخروج وقيل المغيرة فإنه لما قتل اختلف أصحابه فقال بعضهم بانتظاره وقال آخرون بانتظار زكريا كما كان به
Al-Mughiriyya: Mughira ibn Sa'id al-'Ijli said: God is in the form of a human, rather a man of light, on his head a crown of light, and his heart is the source of wisdom. When He wanted to create creation, He spoke the Greatest Name, and it flew and placed itself as a crown on His head. That is His saying: 'Exalt the name of your Lord, the Most High, who created and proportioned' (87:1). Then He wrote the deeds of the servants on His palm, and became angry at the sins, so He sweated, and from his sweat came two seas, one salty dark and the other sweet luminous. Then He looked into the luminous sea and saw His reflection, so He snatched it (i.e., snatched some of His reflection) and made from it the sun and the moon, and annihilated the rest of the reflection to negate any partner, saying: 'There should not be with me another god.' Then He created the creation from the two seas: unbelief (i.e., the unbelievers) from the dark sea, and faith (i.e., the believers) from the luminous sea. Then He sent Muhammad while people were in misguidance. And He presented the trust—which is preventing 'Ali from the Imamate—to the heavens, earth, and mountains, but they refused to bear it and were afraid of it, and man bore it, and he is Abu Bakr. He bore it by the command of 'Umar when he guaranteed to assist him in that, on condition that Abu Bakr make the caliphate after him for him (i.e., 'Umar). And His saying: 'Like the example of Satan' (59:16) the verse was revealed concerning Abu Bakr and 'Umar. These people say: The awaited Imam is Zakariyya ibn Muhammad ibn 'Ali ibn al-Husayn ibn 'Ali, and he is alive, residing in Mount Hajir until he is commanded to emerge. And it is said (it is) al-Mughira, for when he was killed, his companions differed: some said they await him, others said they await Zakariyya as before.
Source pages p. 417

Commentary
This long passage describes the Mughiriyya sect, followers of Mughira ibn Sa'id al-'Ijli. Their beliefs are extremely mythological and anthropomorphic: 1. God is in human form, a man of light with a crown, his heart the source of wisdom. 2. To create, He spoke the Greatest Name, which became a crown. The Quranic verse 'سبح اسم ربك الأعلى' is interpreted as describing this event. 3. He wrote deeds on His palm, became angry, sweated, and from sweat produced two seas: dark salty (for unbelievers) and bright sweet (for believers). 4. He saw His reflection in the bright sea, snatched part to create sun and moon, and destroyed the rest to avoid a partner. 5. Creation of humans from the two seas: unbelievers from the dark, believers from the light. 6. Muhammad was sent when people were in error. 7. The 'trust' (amanah) mentioned in Quran 33:72 is reinterpreted as preventing 'Ali from the caliphate. This trust was offered to the heavens, earth, mountains, but they refused; it was borne by 'man' (Abu Bakr), who did so by 'Umar's order with a promise that the caliphate would return to 'Umar. 8. Quran 59:16 is claimed to be about Abu Bakr and 'Umar. 9. Their awaited Imam is either Zakariyya (a descendant) or al-Mughira himself, with disagreement among followers after his death.

Key Terms
مؤمن
كافر
بحر
نير
مظلم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mughiriyya believed that believers and unbelievers are different substances.
Correction: Mainstream Islam teaches that all humans are created from the same origin (clay), and belief or unbelief is a matter of choice and guidance, not material composition.

Checkpoint
From which sea are believers created according to Mughira?
A) The dark sea
B) The luminous sea
C) Both seas
D) From God's reflection

Key Takeaway
The Mughiriyya believed in a material determinism of faith and unbelief, derived from the two seas.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever catch yourself thinking that your faith is just 'the way you were born' or something fixed? This passage claims that the Mughiriyya believed faith comes from a physical substance. But you know better. Where does your faith really come from, and what are you doing this week to nurture it as a gift from Allah, not a given?
?
The Mughiriyya said that when Muhammad was sent, people were in misguidance—meaning everyone was lost. In your own life, have you ever used the excuse that 'everyone is doing it' to justify a sin or neglect of duty? Muhammad came as a mercy even to a misguided world. What excuse are you still holding onto that you know is wrong?
?
If you genuinely believed that your eternal destiny was sealed by the matter you are made from, would you strive to change? You don't believe that. So what is your excuse for not striving harder to please Allah? When is the last time you begged Him for guidance with tears?

Mughiriyya's Historical Revisionism: The Trust and the Awaited Imam
Mughira's reinterpretation of Quranic trust story and the awaited imam doctrine.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mughiriyya's reinterpretation of the Quranic 'trust' as the caliphate of 'Ali, their claim that Abu Bakr and 'Umar conspired, and their belief in an awaited Imam.

Core Idea
The Mughiriyya saw the caliphate as a trust that was wrongfully given to Abu Bakr.

The Mughiriyya sect not only held mythic views about creation but also revised early Islamic history. They reinterpreted Quran 33:72 (the trust) to refer to the imamate of 'Ali. This lesson presents their claim that the trust was offered to the heavens, earth, and mountains but they refused; it was then borne by 'Abu Bakr' (the 'man' in the verse) who acted on 'Umar's orders. The lesson also covers their belief in an awaited imam, either Zakariyya or al-Mughira himself.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic text about the trust and the awaited imam.
Notice how they reinterpret a well-known Quranic verse.
2
Deconstruct the trust narrative
Identify the claimed meaning: 'amanah' = preventing Ali from imamate; 'man' = Abu Bakr; 'Umar's role; and the condition for caliphate return.
3
Analyze the awaited imam
The sect splits after Mughira's death: some await his return, others await Zakariyya. Note the location: Mount Hajir.

?

?
The Mughiriyya placed their hope in an awaited imam hiding in a mountain, postponing their responsibility. Is there an area of your life where you are waiting for a miraculous intervention instead of acting on the clear commands Allah has already given? What is one step you can take right now, without waiting for anyone else?
?
The sect slandered Abu Bakr by claiming he bore the trust unjustly. Have you ever spread a false narrative about someone to elevate your own position? Repent sincerely, and if possible, correct the harm you have caused by speaking the truth or apologizing.

The Saba'iyya: Deification of Ali
Describes the Saba'iyya sect's beliefs about Ali's divinity and return.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the beliefs of the Saba'iyya sect, their deification of Ali, denial of his death, and their unique ritual practices.

Core Idea
A sect that deified Ali and awaits his return from the clouds.

The Saba'iyya represent the earliest extreme Ghulat sect in Islamic history. Founded by a Jewish convert, they elevated Ali to divinity and denied his death, teaching that he is alive in the clouds and will return to fill the earth with justice. This passage from al-Mawaqif outlines their core beliefs and their strange ritual practice of greeting Ali when hearing thunder.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation once to get the overall narrative of the sect's origins and beliefs.
Pay attention to the sequence: founder, background, claims, practice.
2
Identify the founder
Notice that Abdullah ibn Saba' is the founder. See his background as a Jewish convert and his previous claims about Joshua.
This helps understand the sect's heterodox origins.
3
Analyze the core beliefs
Focus on the three main claims: Ali is divine, Ali did not die but a satan impersonated him, Ali is in the clouds and will return.
These beliefs directly contradict Islamic monotheism and the historical death of Ali.
4
Examine the ritual practice
Note that followers greet Ali when hearing thunder, identifying thunder as his voice and lightning as his whip.
This illustrates how beliefs translate into action.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السبائية : قال عبد الله بن سباء لعلي : أنت الإله حقاً فنفاه علي إلى المدائن، وقيل : إنه كان يهودياً فأسلم وكان في اليهودية يقول في يوشع بن نون وصي موسى مثل ما قال في علي وهو أول من أظهر القول بوجوب إمامة علي ومنه تشعبت أصناف الغلاة. وقال ابن سبأ : وإنه لم يمت علي ولم يقتل وإنما قتل ابن ملجم شيطاناً تصور بصورة علي وعلي في السحاب، والرعد صوته، والبرق سوطه وإنه ينزل بعد هذا إلى الأرض ويملؤها عدلاً. وهؤلاء يقولون عند سماع الرعد : عليك السلام يا أمير المؤمنين.
The Saba'iyya: Abdullah ibn Saba' said to Ali: 'You are truly God.' So Ali exiled him to al-Madain. It is said that he was a Jew who converted and used to say in Judaism about Joshua bin Nun, the successor of Moses, similar to what he said about Ali. He was the first to manifest the claim of the obligation of Ali's Imamate, and from him branched the various kinds of extremists. And Ibn Saba' said: 'Ali did not die and was not killed; rather, Ibn Muljim killed a satan that had taken the form of Ali. Ali is in the clouds, thunder is his voice, lightning is his whip, and he will descend after this to the earth and fill it with justice.' These people say when hearing thunder: 'Peace be upon you, O Commander of the Faithful.'
Source pages p. 417

Commentary
This passage describes the Saba'iyya sect, the earliest Ghulat group founded by Abdullah ibn Saba'. It outlines their core beliefs: the deification of Ali, denial of his death, belief in his return, and his identification with natural phenomena. The passage also notes their practice of greeting Ali when hearing thunder. The text follows the author's order: first naming the sect and its founder, then recounting its origin from Ibn Saba' who was exiled, then detailing his beliefs that Ali is alive in the clouds, and finally their ritual greeting.

Key Terms
السبائية
ابن سبأ
الغلاة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the Saba'iyya's beliefs represent mainstream Shia Islam.
Correction: The Saba'iyya deified Ali and denied his death, which are rejected by Twelver Shia and all orthodox Muslims.

Checkpoint
What did the Saba'iyya believe about Ali's death?
A) He was killed by Ibn Muljim
B) He did not die, but a satan in his form was killed
C) He died naturally and will not return
D) He was killed but will be resurrected

Key Takeaway
The Saba'iyya sect, founded by Abdullah ibn Saba', held extreme beliefs that Ali is divine, did not die, and is present in natural phenomena, awaiting his return to establish justice.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were to hear thunder right now, what would your immediate thought be? Would it be of Allah's power, or could you be influenced by such legends? What does your reaction reveal about the purity of your tawheed? Commit today to always say 'Subhanallah' when you hear thunder, not the greeting of the Saba'iyya.
?
Ali exiled the one who called him God rather than accept the flattery. Would you have the courage to reject praise that compromises your faith? Is there any person in your life you admire so much that you might cross the line from love to worship? Repent now and affirm that only Allah deserves worship.
?
The Saba'iyya believed Ali did not die but is hidden in the clouds. Do you ever hold onto false hopes about someone, preferring fantasy over the truth revealed by Allah? What relationship or belief have you been clinging to that contradicts clear Islamic teaching? Let go of it today for the sake of Allah.

The Bayaniyya: Anthropomorphism and Indwelling Spirit
Bayaniyya beliefs in anthropomorphism and spirit transmission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Bayaniyya's anthropomorphic conception of God and their belief in a spirit dwelling in a succession of imams.

Core Idea
The Bayaniyya believed God is human-like and His spirit moved through a chain of imams.

The Bayaniyya, founded by Bayan al-Tamimi, held extreme views about God's form and the indwelling of a divine spirit. This passage outlines two key doctrines: a literal anthropomorphism and the transmission of a spirit through a specific lineage. Let's examine the text and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation to get a literal sense of the beliefs described.
Notice the chain of names: Ali, his son, his grandson, and finally Bayan.
2
Identify the two key beliefs
The passage presents two distinct beliefs: an anthropomorphic view of God and the indwelling of a spirit in successive figures. Find where each is mentioned.
The first belief includes a Quranic allusion: 'all perishes except His face.'
3
Trace the spirit's chain
List the figures in whom the spirit dwells according to the Bayaniyya. Understand that this chain legitimizes Bayan's authority.
The chain is: Ali → Muhammad ibn al-Hanafiyya → Abu Hashim → Bayan.
4
Reflect on significance
Consider why mainstream Islam rejects these views. Anthropomorphism (tashbih) and incarnation (hulul) are major theological deviations.
This passage helps you recognize extreme sectarian positions in early Islamic history.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
البيانية : قال بيان سمعان بن التميمي النهدي اليمني : الله على صورة إنسان ويهلك كله إلا وجهه، وروح حلت في علي ثم في ابنه محمد بن الحنفية ثم في ابنه أبي هاشم ثم في بيان.
The Bayaniyya: Bayan Sam'an al-Tamimi al-Nahdi al-Yamani said: God is in the form of a human, and all of Him perishes except His face, and a spirit dwelled in Ali, then in his son Muhammad ibn al-Hanafiyya, then in his son Abu Hashim, then in Bayan.
Source pages p. 417

Commentary
This passage describes the Bayaniyya sect founded by Bayan al-Tamimi. It presents two key beliefs: first, an anthropomorphic view of God—God is in human form, and only His face remains after perishing (possibly referencing Quranic verse 'everything perishes except His face'). Second, the belief in an indwelling spirit that moved from Ali through his descendants to the founder Bayan himself. The author lists the chain: Ali, Muhammad ibn al-Hanafiyya, Abu Hashim, and Bayan.

Key Terms
البيانية
بيان
صورة إنسان
روح حلت

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the Bayaniyya concept of spirit is the same as the Holy Spirit in Christianity or a separate entity.
Correction: The 'spirit' here is a Ghulat concept of a divine spirit that passes through and indwells imams; it is not a transcendent, independent spirit but a form of incarnation (hulul).

Checkpoint
According to the Bayaniyya, where did the spirit dwell after leaving Ali?
A) In the Prophet Muhammad
B) In Muhammad ibn al-Hanafiyya
C) In Abu Bakr
D) In the angel Gabriel

Key Takeaway
The Bayaniyya represents an extreme anthropomorphic and incarnationist sect within early Islamic thought.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think of God, do you ever unconsciously picture a form or shape? This lesson shows a belief that literally describes God as a human. Read the Arabic again: 'الله على صورة إنسان'. Now search your heart—have you ever, even briefly, imagined God in a way similar to creation? Commit to purifying your conception of God by only using the names and attributes He reveals in the Quran. What is one step you will take today to remove any mental image of God?
?
The Bayaniyya believed a spirit moved from Ali through a chain to their founder. Do you ever seek spiritual authority or enlightenment through a human chain or charismatic leader? Could there be any person or group you are relying on for guidance more than the Quran and Sunnah? This lesson warns against elevating humans to a divine role. Identify one relationship or influence where you might be putting too much trust in a person, and decide to realign your reliance back to Allah alone.

The Mughiriyya: Creation Myth and Eschatology
Describes the Mughiriyya's elaborate cosmogony, anthropomorphism, and views on the Imamate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinctive and highly anthropomorphic creation myth of the Mughiriyya sect, their peculiar reinterpretation of the Quranic trust, and their eschatological expectations regarding the awaited Imam.

Core Idea
The Mughiriyya imagined God as a luminous human and creation as emerging from His sweat and shadow.

The Mughiriyya, founded by Mughira ibn Sa'id al-Ijli, represent an extreme anthropomorphic and gnostic strand within early Shi'ite thought. This passage presents their unique cosmogony, which blends divine anthropomorphism, magic (the Greatest Name), and a dualistic creation from two seas. It also includes a controversial reinterpretation of the Quranic trust narrative and their belief in an awaited imam. Let's examine their system as recorded by the author.

Guided Path
1
Read the full passage
Read the Arabic text and English translation carefully to get an overall sense of the narrative.
2
Identify the anthropomorphic descriptions
Note how God is described as a luminous human with a crown, and how He produces the world through physical processes like sweating.
3
Trace the creation sequence
Follow the order: speaking the name, writing deeds, sweating to produce two seas, taking part of a shadow to make sun and moon, then creating believers and disbelievers from the two seas.
4
Analyze the trust narrative
Observe how they reinterpret the Quranic 'trust' (amanah) as the denial of Ali's Imamate, and their polemic against Abu Bakr and Umar.
5
Understand the eschatology
Note the belief in the awaited Imam Zakariyya or the return of Mughira himself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المغيرية : قال مغيرة بن سعيد العجلي : الله على صورة إنسان بل رجل من نور على رأسه تاج من نور وقلبه منبع الحكمة. ولما أراد أن يخلق الخلق تكلم بالاسم الأعظم فطار فوقع تاجاً على رأسه وذلك قوله تعالى : {سبح اسم ربك الأعلى الذي خلق فسوى} [الأعلى : ١]. ثم إنه كتب على كفه أعمال العباد فغضب من المعاصي فعرق فحصل منه أي من عرقه بحران أحدهما ملح مظلم والآخر حلو نير. ثم اطلع في البحر النير فأبصر فيه ظله فانتزعه أي انتزع بعضاً من ظله فجعل وخلق منه الشمس والقمر وأفنى الباقي من الظل نفياً للشريك. وقال : لا ينبغي أن يكون معي إله آخر. ثم خلق الخلق من البحرين، فالكفر أي الكفار من المظلم، والإيمان أي المؤمنين من النير. ثم أرسل محمداً والناس في ضلالة وعرض الأمانة وهي منع علي عن الإمامة على السماوات والأرض والجبال فأبين أن يحملنها وأشفقن منها وحملها الإنسان وهو أبو بكر حملها بأمر عمر حين ضمن أن يعينه على ذلك بشرط أن يجعل أبو بكر الخلافة بعده له. وقوله تعالى : {كمثل الشيطان} [الحشر : ١٦] الآية نزلت في حق أبي بكر وعمر. هؤلاء يقولون : الإمام المنتظر هو زكريا بن محمد بن علي بن الحسين بن علي وهو حي مقيم في جبل حاجر إلى أن يؤمر بالخروج. وقيل المغيرة فإنه لما قتل اختلف أصحابه فقال بعضهم بانتظاره وقال آخرون بانتظار زكريا كما كان به.
The Mughiriyya: Mughira ibn Sa'id al-Ijli said: God is in the form of a human, rather a man of light, on his head a crown of light, and his heart is the source of wisdom. When He wanted to create creation, He spoke with the Greatest Name, and it flew and became a crown on His head, and that is His saying: 'Exalt the name of your Lord, the Most High, who created and proportioned' (Quran 87:1). Then He wrote on His palm the deeds of the servants, and He became angry at sins and sweated, so from His sweat came two seas, one salty and dark, the other sweet and luminous. Then He looked into the luminous sea and saw His shadow, so He took part of His shadow and from it He created the sun and the moon, and annihilated the rest of the shadow to negate a partner. He said: 'It is not fitting that there be another god with me.' Then He created creation from the two seas: disbelief—i.e., the disbelievers—from the dark, and faith—i.e., the believers—from the luminous. Then He sent Muhammad while people were in error, and He presented the trust—which is preventing Ali from the Imamate—to the heavens, earth, and mountains, but they refused to carry it. Man carried it—i.e., Abu Bakr—carried it by the command of 'Umar, when he guaranteed to help him on that, on condition that Abu Bakr makes the caliphate after him for 'Umar. And His saying: 'like the example of Satan' (Quran 59:16) was revealed concerning Abu Bakr and 'Umar. These people say: The awaited Imam is Zakariyya ibn Muhammad ibn Ali ibn al-Husayn ibn Ali, and he is alive, residing in Mount Hajir until he is commanded to emerge. And it is said: Mughira—for when he was killed, his followers disagreed: some said they await him, others said they await Zakariyya as they had done with him.
Source pages p. 417

Commentary
This passage describes the Mughiriyya sect founded by Mughira ibn Sa'id al-Ijli. It presents a complex creation myth: God as a luminous human with a crown, using the Greatest Name to create a crown, sweating to produce two seas, and creating from them the world and mankind. It includes a narrative about the trust (amanah) being offered to heaven and earth but only Abu Bakr carrying it, with a negative interpretation of Quranic verses. Finally, it discusses their eschatology: the awaited imam is Zakariyya (or Mughira himself) who is alive in a mountain. The author details each step in the order given.

Key Terms
المغيرية
مغيرة بن سعيد
الاسم الأعظم
الأمانة
الإمام المنتظر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mughiriyya's beliefs might be considered a legitimate interpretation of Islam.
Correction: This passage shows how their views deviate drastically from core Islamic monotheism and orthodoxy, especially in anthropomorphism and slander of the Companions.

Checkpoint
According to the Mughiriyya, from what did the sun and moon originate?
A) From God's sweat
B) From a part of God's shadow
C) From the two seas
D) From the crown of light

Key Takeaway
The Mughiriyya myth exemplifies extreme anthropomorphism and gnostic dualism, reflecting the radicalization of certain early Shi'ite circles.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Mughiriyya created a god in their own imagination, complete with human form and emotions. In what subtle ways do you also shape God to fit your preferences—perhaps imagining He approves of your habits or overlooks your sins? Write down one specific way you have remade God in your own image and a step you will take to worship Him as He is, not as you wish He were.
?
They twisted Quranic verses to justify their political agenda, claiming 59:16 was about Abu Bakr and Umar. When you read the Quran, do you ever bend its meaning to support your views, even if that means ignoring clear context? Think of a verse you have struggled to accept because it challenges your lifestyle. What will you do to let it change you instead of explaining it away?
?
The sect placed their hope in a hidden imam waiting in a cave. Where do you place your deepest hope? Is it in a leader, a movement, a financial plan, or your own efforts? Confess one thing you are relying on more than God, and commit to a concrete act of trust in Him alone this week.

The Janahiyya Sect: Transmigration of the Spirit of God
Describes the Janahiyya's beliefs in transmigration and antinomianism.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the heretical beliefs of the Janahiyya sect regarding the transmigration of God's spirit and their rejection of Islamic teachings on resurrection and morality.

Core Idea
The Janahiyya believed God's spirit passed through prophets and imams and is now hidden in a mountain.

The Janahiyya were a Shiite extremist sect with distinctive ideas about the transmigration of the divine spirit. This lesson presents their core doctrines as recorded by al-Iji in al-Mawaqif. Understanding these deviant views clarifies orthodox Islamic positions on the spirit, resurrection, and moral law.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice how the author lists the beliefs sequentially.
The passage is short but dense with doctrinal points.
2
Identify the transmigration chain
Trace the path of the Spirit of God from Adam through prophets and imams to Abdullah. Note the names mentioned.
The chain ends with Abdullah ibn Muawiya, the founder.
3
Understand the hidden imam claim
The Janahiyya believe Abdullah is still alive in a mountain in Isfahan and will emerge. This is similar to other Shiite occultation beliefs.
This is a form of ghayba (occultation) doctrine.
4
Reflect on the moral implications
They denied the resurrection and permitted major sins. Consider how this contradicts Islamic fundamentals.
Antinomianism often accompanies extreme esoteric doctrines.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الجناحية : قال عبد الله بن معاوية بن عبد الله بن جعفر ذي الجناحين : الأرواح تتناسخ، وكان روح الله في آدم ثم في شيث ثم الأنبياء والأئمة حتى انتهت إلى علي وأولاده الثلاثة ثم إلى عبد الله. هذا، وقالت الجناحية : هو عبد الله حي مقيم بجبل بأصفهان وسيخرج، وأنكروا القيامة واستحلوا المحرمات من الخمر والميتة والزنا وغيرها.
The Janahiyya: Abdullah ibn Muawiya ibn Abdullah ibn Ja'far Dhi al-Janahayn said: Souls transmigrate, and the Spirit of God was in Adam, then in Seth, then in the prophets and imams until it ended with Ali and his three sons, then to Abdullah. This, and the Janahiyya said: He, Abdullah, is alive, residing in a mountain in Isfahan and will emerge. And they denied the resurrection and permitted forbidden things like wine, carrion, and adultery, and others.
Source pages p. 417

Commentary
This passage describes the Janahiyya sect, named after its founder Abdullah ibn Muawiya. It first explains their core doctrine of metempsychosis: souls transmigrate, specifically the Spirit of God that passed from Adam through Seth, prophets, imams, to Ali, his three sons, and finally to Abdullah. Then it states their belief that Abdullah is still alive in a mountain in Isfahan and will emerge. Finally, it mentions their rejection of bodily resurrection and their permissibility of major sins. The author lists these points in order.

Key Terms
الجناحية
عبد الله بن معاوية
روح الله
التناسخ
القيامة
المحرمات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think 'Spirit of God' here refers to the Holy Spirit (Jibril) or a divine attribute.
Correction: In the Janahiyya context, 'Spirit of God' is a divine essence that transmigrates through human bodies, not the angel Jibril or an attribute.

Checkpoint
Where do the Janahiyya believe their founder Abdullah is now?
A) In heaven
B) Dead and buried
C) Living in a mountain in Isfahan
D) Reincarnated as another person

Key Takeaway
The Janahiyya combined transmigration of the divine spirit with antinomianism, a heretical departure from Islamic teachings.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Janahiyya claimed that because the Spirit of God was in them, they could disregard divine law. Are there areas in your life where you have used a sense of spiritual privilege or special knowledge as an excuse to disobey clear commands of Allah?
?
They denied the resurrection and lived as if this world was all that mattered. In what ways do your daily priorities reflect a belief (or lack of belief) in the Day of Judgment?
?
The Janahiyya permitted wine, carrion, and adultery. Reflect on any small compromises you have made in your own practice, thinking they are insignificant. How have you justified actions that you know are forbidden?

The Mansuriyya: Ascension and Allegorical Interpretation
Describes the Mansuriyya's beliefs and allegorical exegesis.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the extreme allegorical hermeneutics of the Mansuriyya sect and their claim of Abu Mansur's ascension.

Core Idea
The Mansuriyya turned Quranic terms into symbols for their leaders.

The Mansuriyya sect represents an extreme form of allegorical interpretation (ta'wil) that reinterprets fundamental Islamic concepts—Paradise, Hell, obligations, and prohibitions—as references to specific individuals. This lesson examines their founder Abu Mansur al-Ijli, his claim of a heavenly ascension, and how he identified himself with a Quranic verse.

Guided Path
1
Meet Abu Mansur al-Ijli
Learn about the founder of the Mansuriyya and his background. He originally attributed himself to Imam al-Baqir before claiming Imamate for himself.
2
The ascension claim
Read about their belief that Abu Mansur ascended to heaven and was anointed by God. They identify him with the 'falling piece' (kisf) in Quran 52:44.
3
Allegorical reinterpretation
Examine how they reinterpret Paradise, Hell, obligations, and prohibitions as persons. Their goal is to reach these persons to escape religious duty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المنصورية : هو أبو منصور العجلي عزا نفسه إلى أبي جعفر محمد الباقر فلما تبرأ منه وطرده ادعى الإمامة لنفسه. قالوا : الإمامة صارت لمحمد ابن علي بن الحسين ثم انتقلت عنه إلى أبي منصور، وزعموا أن أبا منصور عرج إلى السماء ومسح الله رأسه بيده وقال : يا بني اذهب فبلغ عني، ثم أنزله إلى الأرض، وهو الكسف المذكور في قوله تعالى : {وإن يروا كسفاً من السماء ساقطاً يقولوا سحاب مركوم} [الطور : ٤٤]. وكان قبل ادعائه الإمامة لنفسه يقول : الكسف علي ابن أبي طالب. وقالوا : الرسل لا تنقطع أبداً، والجنة رجل أمرنا بموالاته وهو الإمام، والنار بالضد أي رجل أمرنا ببغضه وهو ضده أي ضد الإمام وخصمه كأبي بكر. وكذا الفرائض والمحرمات، فإن الفرائض أسماء رجال أمرنا بموالاتهم، والمحرمات أسماء رجال أمرنا بمعادتهم. ومقصودهم بذلك أن من ظفر برجل منهم فقد ارتفع عنه التكليف والخطاب لوصوله إلى الجنة.
The Mansuriyya: He is Abu Mansur al-Ijli. He attributed himself to Abu Ja'far Muhammad al-Baqir, but when he disassociated from him and expelled him, he claimed the Imamate for himself. They said: The Imamate went to Muhammad ibn Ali ibn al-Husayn (al-Baqir), then it transferred from him to Abu Mansur. They claimed that Abu Mansur ascended to heaven, and God wiped his head with His hand and said: 'O my son, go and convey from me.' Then He sent him down to earth, and he is the 'falling piece' (kisf) mentioned in His saying: {And if they see a falling piece from the sky, they say, 'A cloud piled up'} (Quran 52:44). Before he claimed the Imamate for himself, he used to say: 'The kisf is Ali ibn Abi Talib.' And they said: The messengers never cease, and Paradise is a man whom we are commanded to befriend — that is the Imam — and Hell is the opposite, i.e., a man whom we are commanded to hate, and he is the opponent of the Imam, like Abu Bakr. Likewise, the religious obligations and prohibitions: for the obligations are names of men we are commanded to befriend, and the prohibitions are names of men we are commanded to oppose. Their intent in this is that whoever obtains one of those men has the obligation and address lifted from him because he has reached Paradise.
Source pages p. 418

Commentary
This passage describes the Mansuriyya sect founded by Abu Mansur al-Ijli. It first narrates his claim to Imamate after being rejected by al-Baqir. Then it presents their belief in his ascension to heaven where God anointed him and sent him back. They identify him with the 'kisf' (falling piece) in Quran 52:44, originally interpreted as Ali. Further, they hold a radical allegorical exegesis where Paradise and Hell, obligations and prohibitions, are interpreted as persons. The ultimate goal is to reach these people, thereby escaping religious duty. The author follows the sequence of claims.

Key Terms
المنصورية
أبو منصور العجلي
الكسف
الجنة والنار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think this allegorical method is a valid form of ta'wil.
Correction: The Mansuriyya's interpretation is extreme and rejected by mainstream Islam, as it distorts the literal meanings and leads to antinomianism.

Checkpoint
What did the Mansuriyya believe about the 'kisf' (falling piece) in the Quran?
A) It refers to a meteor
B) It originally referred to Ali, but later to Abu Mansur
C) It refers to the Kaaba
D) It is an angel

Key Takeaway
The Mansuriyya represents a radical sect that allegorized core Islamic doctrines to justify their leadership and abrogate religious obligations.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever reinterpreted a clear command of Allah to make it more convenient for yourself, even if only in your mind? What does the Mansuriyya's extreme allegorization reveal about the human tendency to avoid accountability, and what specific step will you take today to submit to a command you've been resisting?
?
If you could befriend one person who would lift all religious duties from you, would you be tempted to pursue that? Why? What does that temptation reveal about your heart's true relationship with Allah's commands, and how will you guard against seeking shortcuts to salvation?
?
The Mansuriyya called obligations 'names of men to befriend.' Have you ever treated a teacher, scholar, or leader as if their approval exempts you from directly obeying Allah? This week, how will you ensure your obedience is to Allah first, regardless of human relationships?

The Khattabiyya: Deification of Imams
Describes the origin of the Khattabiyya and their deification of imams.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the extreme beliefs of the Khattabiyya sect regarding the nature of the imams, including their deification and the claim of superiority of Abu al-Khattab over them.

Core Idea
The Khattabiyya escalated from considering imams prophets to worshipping them as gods.

The Khattabiyya sect represents one of the most extreme manifestations of ghuluw (exaggeration) in Shia history. Its founder, Abu al-Khattab, initially attached himself to Imam Ja'far al-Sadiq but was rejected due to his extremist views. In response, he claimed authority for himself and his followers developed a shocking hierarchy of divinity.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the sequence of claims
Notice how the Khattabiyya first claimed imams are prophets, then gods, and finally that Abu al-Khattab is superior to Ja'far al-Sadiq and Ali.
3
Reflect on the significance
Ask yourself: Why would a rejected follower claim such extreme authority? This shows how ghuluw can lead to outright deification.
This connects to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخطابية : هو أبو الخطاب الأسدي عزا نفسه إلى أبي عبد الله جعفر الصادق فلما علم منه غلوه في حقه تبرأ منه فلما اعتزل عنه ادعى الأمر لنفسه. قالوا : الأئمة أنبياء وأبو الخطاب نبي ففرضوا طاعته، أي زعموا أن الأنبياء فرضوا على الله طاعة أبي الخطاب. بل زادوا على ذلك وقالوا : الأئمة آلهة والحسنان ابنا الله وجعفر الصادق إله، ولكن أبو الخطاب أفضل منه ومن علي. وهؤلاء يستحلون شهادة الزور لموافقيهم على مخالفيهم. والإمام بعد قتله أي قتل أبي الخطاب معمر، أي ذهب إلى ذلك جماعة منهم فعبدوا معمراً كما كانوا يعبدون أبا الخطاب. وقالوا: الجنة نعيم الدنيا والنار آلامها والدنيا لا تفنى. واستباحوا المحرمات وترك الفرائض. وقيل الإمام بعد قتله بزيع، أي ذهب إلى ذلك طائفة أخرى منهم. وقالوا : إن كل مؤمن يوحى إليه مستمسكين بقوله تعالى : {وما كان لنفس أن تموت إلا بإذن الله} [آل عمران : ١٤٥]، أي بوحي من الله إليه. وفيهم أي في أصحاب بزيغ من هو خير من جبريل وميكائيل وهم لا يموتون أبداً بل إذا بلغوا النهاية يرفعون إلى الملكوت. وقيل : هو أي الإمام بعد أبي الخطاب عمير بن بنان العجلي إلا أنهم يموتون أي يقولون بذلك.
The Khattabiyya: He is Abu al-Khattab al-Asadi. He attributed himself to Abu Abdullah Ja'far al-Sadiq, but when Ja'far learned of his extremism regarding him, he disassociated from him. When he left him, he claimed the authority for himself. They said: The imams are prophets, and Abu al-Khattab is a prophet, so they made obedience to him obligatory, i.e., they claimed that the prophets obligated upon God obedience to Abu al-Khattab. Rather, they went beyond that and said: The imams are gods, al-Hasan and al-Husayn are sons of God, and Ja'far al-Sadiq is a god, but Abu al-Khattab is better than him and than Ali. And these people permit bearing false witness for their supporters against their opponents. The Imam after his death, i.e., the killing of Abu al-Khattab, is Ma'mar, i.e., a group of them went to that, so they worshipped Ma'mar as they used to worship Abu al-Khattab. And they said: Paradise is the pleasure of this world and Hell is its pains, and this world is never-ending. And they made forbidden things permissible and abandoned religious obligations. And it is said: The Imam after his killing is Bazigh, i.e., another sect from them went to that. And they said: Every believer receives revelation, clinging to His saying: {No soul can die except by Allah's permission} (Quran 3:145), i.e., by revelation from God to him. And among them, i.e., among the followers of Bazigh, there are those who are better than Gabriel and Michael, and they never die, rather when they reach the end, they are raised to the celestial kingdom. And it is said: He, i.e., the Imam after Abu al-Khattab, is 'Umayr ibn Banan al-Ijli, except that they die, i.e., they say that.
Source pages p. 418

Commentary
This passage describes the Khattabiyya sect founded by Abu al-Khattab. It recounts his claim after being rejected by Ja'far al-Sadiq. Their beliefs escalate: imams as prophets, then as gods; Abu al-Khattab is superior. They permit false witness and believe in a succession of worshipped figures after Abu al-Khattab: Ma'mar, Bazigh, and 'Umayr. They have a radically this-worldly view of Paradise and Hell, and abrogate the law. They claim that every believer receives revelation (wahy), using a Quranic verse for support, and that some of Bazigh's followers are superior to angels and immortal. The passage presents these claims sequentially.

Key Terms
الخطابية
أبو الخطاب
جعفر الصادق
الأئمة
آلهة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Abu al-Khattab was a legitimate successor to Ja'far al-Sadiq.
Correction: Ja'far al-Sadiq publicly disassociated from Abu al-Khattab due to his extremist views, making his claim to authority illegitimate.

Checkpoint
What did the Khattabiyya believe about the status of Ja'far al-Sadiq?
A) He is the greatest prophet
B) He is a god, but Abu al-Khattab is better
C) He is the son of God
D) He is an angel

Key Takeaway
The Khattabiyya deified the imams and placed their founder Abu al-Khattab above them, showing extreme ghuluw.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a person you deeply admire. Is there any area of your heart that might tend to elevate them beyond the status Allah has given them? How does the Khattabiyya's extreme deification of imams serve as a warning for you personally? What steps will you take to ensure your admiration remains within Islamic bounds?
?
The Khattabiyya started with 'the imams are prophets' and escalated to 'they are gods.' Can you identify a small exaggeration in your own religious practice that, if unchecked, might lead to something more serious? How will you guard against the slippery slope of ghuluw?
?
Ja'far al-Sadiq, the rightful imam, himself rejected Abu al-Khattab's extremism. When you see someone going to extremes in religion, do you have the courage to disassociate from them as Ja'far did, or do you stay silent? What will you do the next time you see ghuluw around you?

Antinomianism and Succession in the Khattabiyya
Describes the antinomian beliefs and succession of leaders in the Khattabiyya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the radical antinomian beliefs of the Khattabiyya and their successive leadership claims, including the claim that every believer receives revelation and that some are superior to angels.

Core Idea
The Khattabiyya abrogated Islamic law and claimed that every believer receives divine revelation.

After the death of Abu al-Khattab, his followers continued to develop extreme doctrines. They not only permitted false witness and abandoned religious duties but also radically reinterpreted Paradise and Hell as worldly realities. Moreover, they claimed that every believer is divinely inspired and that some of their members are superior to the archangels Gabriel and Michael.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the passage carefully, noting the sequence of beliefs: permissivism, succession, and claim of revelation.
This passage contains many distinct claims.
2
List the antinomian practices
Identify the practices the Khattabiyya made permissible: bearing false witness, abandoning obligations, and making forbidden things lawful.
3
Understand the succession of leaders
Note the names: Ma'mar, Bazigh, 'Umayr ibn Banan al-Ijli. Each group worshipped its leader as they worshipped Abu al-Khattab.
4
Analyze the claim of revelation and angelic superiority
They claimed every believer receives revelation (wahy), using a Quranic verse out of context, and that some followers of Bazigh are better than Gabriel and Michael and never die.
This is a clear departure from Islamic orthodoxy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخطابية : هو أبو الخطاب الأسدي عزا نفسه إلى أبي عبد الله جعفر الصادق فلما علم منه غلوه في حقه تبرأ منه فلما اعتزل عنه ادعى الأمر لنفسه. قالوا : الأئمة أنبياء وأبو الخطاب نبي ففرضوا طاعته، أي زعموا أن الأنبياء فرضوا على الله طاعة أبي الخطاب. بل زادوا على ذلك وقالوا : الأئمة آلهة والحسنان ابنا الله وجعفر الصادق إله، ولكن أبو الخطاب أفضل منه ومن علي. وهؤلاء يستحلون شهادة الزور لموافقيهم على مخالفيهم. والإمام بعد قتله أي قتل أبي الخطاب معمر، أي ذهب إلى ذلك جماعة منهم فعبدوا معمراً كما كانوا يعبدون أبا الخطاب. وقالوا: الجنة نعيم الدنيا والنار آلامها والدنيا لا تفنى. واستباحوا المحرمات وترك الفرائض. وقيل الإمام بعد قتله بزيع، أي ذهب إلى ذلك طائفة أخرى منهم. وقالوا : إن كل مؤمن يوحى إليه مستمسكين بقوله تعالى : {وما كان لنفس أن تموت إلا بإذن الله} [آل عمران : ١٤٥]، أي بوحي من الله إليه. وفيهم أي في أصحاب بزيغ من هو خير من جبريل وميكائيل وهم لا يموتون أبداً بل إذا بلغوا النهاية يرفعون إلى الملكوت. وقيل : هو أي الإمام بعد أبي الخطاب عمير بن بنان العجلي إلا أنهم يموتون أي يقولون بذلك.
The Khattabiyya: He is Abu al-Khattab al-Asadi. He attributed himself to Abu Abdullah Ja'far al-Sadiq, but when Ja'far learned of his extremism regarding him, he disassociated from him. When he left him, he claimed the authority for himself. They said: The imams are prophets, and Abu al-Khattab is a prophet, so they made obedience to him obligatory, i.e., they claimed that the prophets obligated upon God obedience to Abu al-Khattab. Rather, they went beyond that and said: The imams are gods, al-Hasan and al-Husayn are sons of God, and Ja'far al-Sadiq is a god, but Abu al-Khattab is better than him and than Ali. And these people permit bearing false witness for their supporters against their opponents. The Imam after his death, i.e., the killing of Abu al-Khattab, is Ma'mar, i.e., a group of them went to that, so they worshipped Ma'mar as they used to worship Abu al-Khattab. And they said: Paradise is the pleasure of this world and Hell is its pains, and this world is never-ending. And they made forbidden things permissible and abandoned religious obligations. And it is said: The Imam after his killing is Bazigh, i.e., another sect from them went to that. And they said: Every believer receives revelation, clinging to His saying: {No soul can die except by Allah's permission} (Quran 3:145), i.e., by revelation from God to him. And among them, i.e., among the followers of Bazigh, there are those who are better than Gabriel and Michael, and they never die, rather when they reach the end, they are raised to the celestial kingdom. And it is said: He, i.e., the Imam after Abu al-Khattab, is 'Umayr ibn Banan al-Ijli, except that they die, i.e., they say that.
Source pages p. 418

Commentary
This passage describes the Khattabiyya sect founded by Abu al-Khattab. It recounts his claim after being rejected by Ja'far al-Sadiq. Their beliefs escalate: imams as prophets, then as gods; Abu al-Khattab is superior. They permit false witness and believe in a succession of worshipped figures after Abu al-Khattab: Ma'mar, Bazigh, and 'Umayr. They have a radically this-worldly view of Paradise and Hell, and abrogate the law. They claim that every believer receives revelation (wahy), using a Quranic verse for support, and that some of Bazigh's followers are superior to angels and immortal. The passage presents these claims sequentially.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the claim of 'revelation for every believer' is similar to Sufi inspiration (ilham).
Correction: The Khattabiyya used the term 'wahy' (revelation to prophets) and misapplied it to all believers, claiming prophethood for them, which is distinct from ilham.

Checkpoint
What did the followers of Bazigh believe about some of their members compared to angels?
A) They are equal to angels
B) They are better than Gabriel and Michael
C) They are just humans
D) They are inferior to angels

Key Takeaway
The Khattabiyya rejected core Islamic teachings by permitting the prohibited, denying the afterlife, and claiming every believer receives revelation and that some are superior to angels.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read that the Khattabiyya made forbidden things permissible and abandoned religious obligations, examine your own heart: In what areas of your life are you tempted to make allowances that dilute or discard what Allah has commanded? Are there any acts of worship you have neglected or justified away? Commit today to returning to one obligation you have been lax in.
?
The Khattabiyya claimed that every believer receives revelation (wahy), misinterpreting the Qur'an. Have you ever interpreted a verse of the Qur'an in a way that justifies your desires, rather than submitting fully to its clear meaning? How can you ensure that you approach the Book with humility, allowing it to guide you instead of imposing your own understanding?
?
Consider the extreme claim that some followers are better than the angels Gabriel and Michael. This arrogance led them to deny death and claim immortality. Do you ever feel a sense of spiritual superiority over others, silently judging their faith or practice? What would it take for you to truly internalize that you are nothing but a servant, that your deeds are purely by Allah's mercy, and that death is an appointment you cannot escape or surpass?
